# uitk — Changelog

## 2026

- **2026-07-14 — Region: skip the shaped `setMask` under the headless `offscreen` QPA plugin — it SIGSEGVs mid-suite on PySide6 6.10.x Linux, crashing CI before the publish gate.** The review-ledger `Region` mask fix (below) applies `setMask` in `__init__`/`showEvent`/`resizeEvent`. On the CI runner (Ubuntu, PySide6 6.10.3, `QT_QPA_PLATFORM=offscreen`) a masked `Region` segfaults during widget teardown, killing pytest mid-run at `test_region.py` (the local Windows-offscreen suite and real X11/Wayland/Windows displays are unaffected — 2682/2683 green locally). The shaped mask is a real-display hit-testing feature, so `_apply_region_mask` now still computes `self.region` but skips the platform `setMask` call when `QApplication.platformName() == "offscreen"`; `TestRegionShapeMask` is skipped there (it asserts on `mask()`, which is empty when the platform call is skipped). Mirrors the suite's existing offscreen carve-outs (e.g. the ignored `test_marking_menu_integration.py`).
- **2026-07-14 — Critique pass over the review-ledger batches: one cross-package regression the pass introduced, one asymmetric-notify sequencer bug, and two stale-doc/dead-state cleanups — each pinned by a regression test.** Post-review of the four 2026-07-14 batches below (multi-agent, one reviewer per layer; the flagged tri-state `CheckBox` "regression" was verified a false positive — the reviewer probed a bare `QCheckBox`, but the real `CheckBox` overrides `checkState()`/`setCheckState()` into the int domain, so 8/8 tri-state tests pass on the venv's PySide6 6.10.1). **Cross-package regression (fixed):** the `ColorSwatch` batch resolved `_color` synchronously in `__init__` **and removed the `initializeColor` fallback that read `_initialColor`** — but mayatk/blendertk Color ID build swatches from a `.ui` (no `color=` kwarg → `_color` = white) and then assign `button._initialColor = <pastel>` externally before setting `.settings`, relying on that fallback to seed the per-column pastel defaults. Without it every Color ID swatch came up white. The `_initialColor` no-settings fallback is restored (the synchronous `_color` resolution and the `HexArgb` alpha round-trip are kept); `loadColor()` now returns `bool` so `initializeColor` applies the fallback only when nothing was persisted (a real saved color still wins). Pinned by new `test_color_swatch.py` cases replicating the downstream set-`_initialColor`-then-`.settings` order and the persisted-value-wins case. **Sequencer teardown (fixed):** `ShortcutManager.remove_shortcut` didn't call `_notify_change()` (asymmetric with `add_shortcut`/`rebind_shortcut`), so a destroyed `TransportControls` removed its `Space`/`Alt+Space` bindings but the sequencer's `on_change`→`_sync_shortcut_sequences` never re-ran — `_timeline._shortcut_sequences` kept the stale keys and `SequencerWidget.event()` accepted the `ShortcutOverride` and swallowed the key with no action firing. `remove_shortcut` now notifies on a successful removal (no-op removal stays silent). Pinned by `test_shortcuts.py::…remove_shortcut_notifies_change_subscribers`. **Cleanups:** `compile.is_compiled_fresh`'s docstring still documented the mtime fast path the prior batch removed (contradicting the code and its own inline comment) — deleted; the dead `ColorSwatch._initialColor = color` init line was actually a live cross-package contract (kept, comment corrected) and the two stale "fallback path" comments were rewritten to match the code. `RecentValuesStore.add()`'s full-store tail-trim was reviewed and confirmed correct-by-design (it is the *seed* path — `record()` is the front-insert path — so a seed must not evict the user's most-recent entries). Full suite 2682 pass / 1 skip / 0 fail.
- **2026-07-14 — Review-ledger completion pass: ~30 confirmed correctness/API/docs fixes across the widget, switchboard, mixin, handler, and sequencer layers, each pinned by a regression test. Full suite 2683 pass / 0 fail; API registry + docs sweep green.** Clears the remaining safe, self-contained items from the multi-agent review (the god-class refactors, mass camelCase renames, and the `add()` clear-vs-append semantics remain deferred — see notes). **Switchboard core:** deleted dead+broken `set_widget_attrs` (its `setattr` shadowed Qt methods; zero callers); `unpack_names` now passes digit-less names through verbatim and derives zero-pad width from the source token (was dropping `'grp_basic'` and hardcoding `zfill(3)`); `file_dialog(allow_multiple=…)` uses `getOpenFileName(s)` correctly instead of the bogus `ReadOnly` flag; `get_available_signals(derived=False/exc=…)` both params now work (compared bare vs qualified class names); `get_unknown_tags` regex replaced with exact-token matching (fixes known-prefix-of-unknown, underscore truncation, empty known-tags); `History.get` returns `None` (not `[]`) for an out-of-range int, honoring the `prev_slot`/`prev_ui` contract; `Switchboard.__init__` gained a real 13-param docstring (was an empty `""" """` mis-placed after `super().__init__`). **Mixins:** `PresetManager.load` no longer permanently stamps `block_signals_on_restore` onto widgets that never had it (mirrors `StateManager.reset_all`'s had-attr/del guard — the leak silently disabled slot execution on later restores); `richTextSizeHint` routes through the lazy dict + base-sizeHint fallback (was `AttributeError` on a `setAlignment`-before-`setText` label); `RecentValuesStore.add` trims the oldest (tail), not the user's newest, when seeding a full store; `StyleSheet.set` promoted from a dynamically-bound `self.set = self._set_style` alias to a real public method (the flagship `ui.style.set(...)` is now visible to the class/registry/IDEs); `StyleSheet.theme_changed` now emits through a process-wide bus so per-instance `ui.style.theme_changed.connect(...)` subscribers hear class-API restyles; `get_icon_color` consults overrides; `attributes._set_custom_attribute` maps `setCheckState=int` to `Qt.CheckState`; `convert.can_convert` agrees with `to_qobject`; `SettingsManager` docstring corrected. **Window shell:** `MessageBox.setStandardButtons` matches Qt button names case-insensitively (multi-word names like "RestoreDefaults" were silently dropped by `capitalize()`); `MessageBox.move_` honors an explicit `QPoint` and positions on the screen under the cursor (was hardcoded to the primary monitor); `Header._minimized_headers` prunes destroyed headers (a dead C++ Header in the set raised `RuntimeError` on any other window's restore); `Region` applies its computed `shape` mask via `setMask` in show/resize (hit-testing/hover now match the documented ellipse). **Sequencer:** locked gap overlays are inert (were still draggable/resizable and emitting); `RulerItem` paints the full timeline extent at any zoom (was a hardcoded 100 000 px); transport Space/Alt+Space registration is idempotent with teardown on destroy (recreating the row left an ambiguous/dead Space); `SequencerWidget.event()` dispatches a matched `ShortcutOverride` directly (was relying on KeyPress bubbling that an intermediate focused child could swallow); `remove_marker` emits only when the id existed; new public `zone_menu_enabled` property replaces the private `_zone_menu_connected` poke (legacy attr still honored). **Handlers / optionBox / attributeWindow:** `external_app_handler.launch()` guards against pip-installing into a live DCC interpreter (would hang the host); `UiHandler.get` is strict (raises on unexpected kwargs instead of silently dropping `reload`/`**kwargs`); `SwitchboardBrowser` listens for `modelReset` so row Launch/Close buttons rebuild after a coarse registry change; `AttributeWindow` composite (list/tuple/set) attributes render under the default gate, its zero-row `showEvent` no longer raises, checkable-label `labelToggled` fires, and `float_precision` is applied; `OptionBoxManager.enable_option_menu` exists (the fluent `widget.options.option_menu(...)` no longer `AttributeError`s); setting `option_order` preserves already-added options; `disable_menu`/`menu` setter produce exactly one button and are idempotent; disabling the clear button now sticks across text changes; `file_manager._handle_single_obj` warns instead of `TypeError` when `resolve_path` returns `None` under `validate=1`. **Package / decorator / docs:** `@Signals()` (zero args) is now the documented "opt out of auto-connection" sentinel (empty signals tuple → `connect_slot` wires nothing) instead of raising `ValueError`; the dead-prototype `DockingMixin` (zero consumers) was removed from the export table; docs corrected — `EXAMPLES.md`/`API_REFERENCE.md` `sb.register_shortcut` → `@Shortcut`/`register_command`; broken `from uitk.widgets.optionBox import …` (docstring-only subpackages) → `from uitk import …` across WIDGETS/COOKBOOK and the optionBox README; `events.py` handler-name/param-order example; `API_REFERENCE.md` phantom methods (`get_theme_vars`/`get_active_theme`/`list_presets`/`get_default`/`SettingsManager(parent=…)`) corrected to real names, and the `Switchboard(...)` signature completed with `loader`/`context_tags`/`on_missing_slot`; `USER_GUIDE.md` documents `combo.restore_by = "text"|"data"`. **Deliberately not changed (with cause):** `create_button_groups` keeps `format_return` — `blendertk/display_utils/color_id.py` relies on the single-group scalar collapse (needs a coordinated cross-package change); `add_marker`/`clear_markers` stay signal-free — emitting would infinite-append / wipe the mayatk shot-sequencer store; `MainWindow.initialize_window_flags` left as a benign no-op (its pre-reparent intent is unclear and "fixing" it risks flag behavior).
- **2026-07-14 — `@Signals.blockSignals` no longer unblocks a caller's own blocked scope, and the ComboBox pure-read methods stop blocking signals entirely.** Follow-up to the self-critique of the batch above. The `Signals.blockSignals` decorator ended its `finally` with an unconditional `blockSignals(False)` rather than restoring the prior state, so invoking a decorated method from inside a caller that had already blocked signals silently re-enabled them mid-operation. It now captures `signalsBlocked()` on entry and restores that on exit (strict improvement — behavior is identical unless the caller was already blocked, in which case the block is correctly preserved). Separately, `ComboBox.currentData()` and `ComboBox.currentText()` were decorated with `@Signals.blockSignals` despite being pure reads (`itemData`/`richText` emit nothing) — pointless, and the same footgun — so the decorator is removed from both. **Critique-pass follow-up (same theme):** `ComboBox.setAsCurrent(blockSignals=True)` hand-rolled its block/unblock with no try/finally — a strict-miss `raise` (or any exception mid-resolution) skipped the unblock and left the combo permanently signal-dead — and it force-unblocked rather than restoring prior state; it now goes through the existing `_silenced()` save/restore contextmanager (`nullcontext()` when `blockSignals=False`), and `setCurrentIndex`'s negative-index branch was consolidated onto the same `_silenced()` helper it already duplicated by hand. Tests: `test_signals.py::…restores_prior_blocked_state`, `test_combobox.py::{ReadMethodsDoNotToggleSignalBlock, SetAsCurrentBlockSignalsSafety}`. (`signalsBlocked()` is a universal `QObject` getter, so the change is Qt-version-agnostic; offscreen coverage is definitive.)
- **2026-07-14 — Second hardening batch: six self-contained widget correctness bugs from the review ledger, each pinned by a regression test (public API surface unchanged).** Chosen after weighing the review's larger structural suggestions (menu.py/marking_menu decomposition, mixins/→managers/ rename, camelCase→snake_case renames, add() append-vs-clear unification) and deferring all of them — they are either fully migration-shimmed internal reorganizations (no freeze urgency, real regression risk) or, for add(), an unshimmable silent behavior break needing a human contract decision. **Bugs fixed:** (1) `TableWidget.add()` blocked signals inside a `try` whose `finally` only restored `setUpdatesEnabled`, so an exception mid-populate left the table permanently signal-dead — `blockSignals` is now restored in the `finally`, preserving the prior block state. (2) `TreeWidget.add()` had an inner `blockSignals(True)/blockSignals(False)` pair that ran before its tail (`set_attributes`/`apply_formatting`), unblocking signals mid-method and defeating its own `@Signals.blockSignals` decorator — removed, so `itemChanged` can no longer escape during add's tail. (3) `ComboBox.items` used `itemData(i) if itemData(i) else itemText(i)`, silently replacing falsy-but-valid data (`0`, `''`, `False`, `[]`) with the display text — now `is not None`, so only a genuine absence of data falls back to text. (4) `ProgressBar`'s task context only tore down the app-wide Esc `GlobalShortcut` on the clean exit path (via `finish_task`); on an exception (or with `auto_hide` off) it stayed enabled, so a later Esc-hold anywhere in the host fired `cancel()` on a dead task — `__exit__` now disables it on every non-finish path. (5) `ColorSwatch._color` was only created inside a deferred `singleShot`, so reading `.color` (or any repaint) before the event loop spun raised `AttributeError` — `_color` is now resolved synchronously in `__init__`; separately, `saveColor` stored `QColor.name()` (#RRGGBB), dropping the alpha the picker's `ShowAlphaChannel` lets users set — it now persists `HexArgb` (#AARRGGBB), and legacy #RRGGBB values still load. (6) `ExpandableList.clear()` deleted items without cancelling their pending `_pending_hide_timer` (parented to the list, not the item), so a queued hide fired on a deleted C++ widget and raised an uncaught `RuntimeError` into the event loop (hit by `refresh_on_show` lists that `clear()` every show mid-hover) — `clear()` now cancels the timer, and `_maybe_hide_sublist` guards deleted-object access as defense in depth. **Live-verified** the widget fixes (editable property, `removeItem` signal, tristate click, falsy-item-data) in a fresh Maya under its own PySide6 6.5.3. Tests: new cases in `test_combobox.py`, `test_color_swatch.py`, `test_expandable_list.py`, plus new `test_progress_bar.py`, `test_table_widget_add.py`, and a tree class in `test_tree_formatting.py`.
- **2026-07-14 — Pre-production hardening pass (multi-agent full-package review): 11 confirmed correctness/API fixes across the widget, switchboard, and infra layers, each pinned by a regression test.** Every item below was reproduced before fixing. **Broken public surface:** two phantom `DEFAULT_INCLUDE` exports that resolved to `AttributeError` on first touch were removed — `WindowManager` (its `managers.window_manager` module doesn't exist; the functionality folded into `UiHandler`) and `OptionBoxWithOrdering` (never defined; ordering is `OptionBox(option_order=...)`); a new `test_package_exports.py` iterates the whole export table so a dead name can't ship again. The root-exported `add_menu_option(widget, menu)` forwarded `menu=` into `OptionBox.__init__` (which takes no such kwarg) → `TypeError` on every call; it now builds a `MenuOption` plugin. **Dispatch:** `SlotWrapper._sig_cache` was keyed by `id()` of a transient bound method — CPython reuses freed bound-method ids, so the never-evicting class cache could serve a stale `(param_names, wants_widget)` for a *different* slot (intermittent wrong/absent widget injection at the heart of dispatch); it's now a `WeakKeyDictionary` keyed on the underlying `__func__` (lives as long as its class, self-evicts, no id reuse). **Widgets:** a tri-state `CheckBox` left-click raised `KeyError` under PySide6 (`mousePressEvent` indexed a `Qt.CheckState`-keyed table with the integer `checkState()`) — it now cycles in the integer domain and gates on the left button so other buttons reach the base handler. `ComboBox(editable=True)` was a silent no-op (`self.editable = editable` bound a dead attribute; Qt properties aren't set by attribute assignment) — the constructor now calls `setEditable`, and a new `editable` property makes `combo.editable = True` real too (this fixes a latent tentacle bug: the Maya/Blender **materials combo** — `cmb002_init` sets `widget.editable = True` — was silently non-editable; **verify in a live DCC**). `ComboBox.removeItem()` raised `AttributeError` every call (emitted a nonexistent `item_deleted`) *and* sat inside `@Signals.blockSignals` so the declared `on_item_deleted` had never once fired — it now blocks only the removal and emits `on_item_deleted` after. `TreeFormatMixin.apply_formatting` lacked the signal-block guard `CellFormatMixin` already had, so conflicting/appended column formatters recursed to `RecursionError` — guard mirrored. **Switchboard/infra:** `Switchboard.prev_ui` returned the *current* UI (the `current_ui` setter appends to history before `prev_ui` read index -1) — it now returns the second-most-recent distinct entry, or `None`. `uitk.events` used PEP 604 `X | Y` unions in evaluated signatures with no `from __future__ import annotations`, crashing `import` on Python 3.9 (a supported PySide2/Maya-2023 target, and it takes `MarkingMenu` down with it) — future-import added. `compile.is_compiled_fresh` short-circuited to "fresh" whenever the artifact's mtime beat the `.ui`'s, so an mtime-preserving transport (Nextcloud/`cp -p`/zip extraction — the O:\Cloud sync case) could deliver new `.ui` content with an older timestamp and load the stale layout forever; the unsound mtime fast path is removed (the embedded-hash compare is the sole truth). `textEditLogHandler.emit` scheduled `QTimer.singleShot` from worker threads that have no Qt event loop, silently dropping every worker-thread record — it now marshals onto the widget's thread via a queued-signal bridge. Tests: `test_package_exports.py`, plus new cases in `test_widgets.py`, `test_switchboard.py`, `test_switchboard_history.py`, `test_compile.py`, `test_tree_formatting.py`, `test_text_edit_log_handler.py`, `test_events.py`, `test_optionBox.py`.
- **2026-07-13 — Browser-launching a *standalone* tool no longer forks its chrome/lifecycle away from the marking menu's — `UiHandler.launch` routes window init through `mm.get` on marking-menu switchboards; `setup_lifecycle` is now idempotent.** Follow-up live report to the gesture-page fix below: a window first initialized from the UI Browser came up with the launcher's `menu/collapse/hide` header set and was parented to `sb.parent()` — which on a marking-menu switchboard is the *menu overlay itself*, so the window hid whenever the overlay hid — while the intended (menu-canonical) window has a **pin** button, parents to the host app window, and hides on activation-key release unless pinned. Both `apply_styles` and `_configure_launched_header` skip when header buttons already exist, so whichever path touched the shared `loaded_ui` singleton first decided its behavior forever. `launch` now resolves the window via the marking menu's canonical init (`mm.get(name)` → host-app parenting + `apply_styles` pin chrome + `setup_lifecycle` hide-with-menu) and skips the launcher-only header set; per-launch options (frameless/on-top/theme/geometry) still apply on top, and switchboards *without* a marking menu keep the old standalone behavior (including the hide button — a frameless launcher window's only dismissal affordance). `setup_lifecycle` gained a per-UI wired flag so the two init paths can't stack `request_hide` connections across relaunches. Tests: `test_ui_handler.py::TestLaunchCanonicalWindowInit` / `TestSetupLifecycleIdempotent`; live: tentacle `test_marking_menu_gui.py::BrowserPolicyGuiTest::test_launch_gives_standalone_window_canonical_chrome`.
- **2026-07-13 — `SwitchboardBrowser` gains a structural `inc`/`exc` entry filter, and `MarkingMenu` uses it to hide its gesture pages from the launcher (tentacle's browser no longer lists `*#startmenu*`/`*#submenu*`).** New constructor kwargs `SwitchboardBrowser(inc=..., exc=...)` plus a public `set_entry_filter(inc, exc)` (`pythontk.filter_list` shell-style name patterns): unlike the user-curated hide lists (row filtering, toggleable from the Show combo), filtered entries are never materialised into the model — absent from counts, chips, presets, and (load-bearing) from the entry-changed signal path: stacked pages emit show/hide traffic on every marking-menu gesture, and an unknown name used to trigger a full coarse model `_refresh` per signal — churn that made the menu feel sluggish whenever a browser instance existed. `_on_entry_changed` now short-circuits names the filter drops. The policy side lives on `MarkingMenu`: `HOSTED_PAGE_PATTERNS` (default `("*#startmenu*", "*#submenu*")`, derived from `_MARKING_MENU_TAGS`) is applied via an editors post-build hook registered in `_setup_registry` (`_register_browser_entry_filter`), so every browser build on that switchboard carries it — tentacle's TclMaya/TclBlender/TclMax inherit it with no changes. Subclasses opt out with `HOSTED_PAGE_PATTERNS = ()`; runtime clear via `browser.set_entry_filter()`. Tests: `test_switchboard_browser.py::EntryFilterStructural`, `test_marking_menu.py::TestMarkingMenuBrowserEntryFilter`.
- **2026-07-13 — Browser-launching a marking-menu page (startmenu/submenu) no longer breaks it — `UiHandler.launch` now delegates a UI claimed by a *hosting handler* to that handler's `show`, and `MarkingMenu.show` heals a detached stacked page.** Live report (tentacle): launching e.g. `cameras#startmenu` from the UI Browser left the menu permanently broken — mis-positioned, wrong chrome, never initing correctly on later gestures. Root cause: the browser's Launch routed every entry through `UiHandler.launch`'s *standalone* setup (reparent to a top-level `Qt.Window` off `sb.parent()`, `Tool`/frameless/on-top flags, launched-header buttons) on the very same `loaded_ui` singleton the marking menu hosts as a *stacked child* of its overlay — and since `is_initialized` gates `_init_ui` to one run, the menu never re-hosted it: `_show_marking_menu` kept `mapFromGlobal`-positioning a page that no longer lived in the overlay. Fix, two layers: (1) a duck-typed **hosting claim** — a handler exposing `hosts_ui(name)`/`show(name)` owns a UI's windowing lifecycle; `UiHandler.launch` consults `hosting_handler(name)` first and delegates (style options discarded — the owner controls presentation). `MarkingMenu.hosts_ui` claims startmenu/submenu pages at the registry level (live tags when loaded, name+XML tags when not — exact parity with `show`'s dispatch, never forces a load). On a switchboard with no marking menu nothing claims the name, so standalone hosting stays legitimate. (2) A **heal guard** in `MarkingMenu.show`: an initialized stacked page found parented outside the menu is re-hosted via the new `_host_stacked` (the hosting invariants extracted from `_init_ui`: borderless style, `ensure_on_screen`/`restore_window_size` opt-outs, geometry clear, reparent into the overlay) — self-repairs sessions corrupted before the fix without a restart; event-filter/signal wiring stays first-load-only in `_init_ui` so connections don't stack. Applies to mayatk/blendertk `UiHandler` subclasses for free. Tests: `test_ui_handler.py` (delegation unit + real-Switchboard integration), `test_marking_menu.py::TestMarkingMenuHostsUi`, `test_marking_menu_integration.py::MarkingMenuStackedRehost`.

- **2026-07-12 — `run_tests.py`: a fully green suite could still exit `0xC0000005` — `_hard_exit` now parks after `TerminateProcess` instead of falling through.** Observed live: 2531/2534 passed, badge updated, yet the process died with an access violation whose faulthandler dump put the main thread at the `os._exit` line. `TerminateProcess(GetCurrentProcess(), …)` is asynchronous — it can return to the calling thread while the kill is in flight — and the fall-through `os._exit` re-enters `DLL_PROCESS_DETACH` (Qt static destructors), the exact segfault `_hard_exit` was added on 2026-06-19 to skip, clobbering the exit code. The success path now parks in a `Sleep` loop until the kill lands (falling back to `os._exit` only if `TerminateProcess` itself fails). Verified in isolation: `_hard_exit(7)` → process exit code 7, no AV dump.
- **2026-07-12 — Stateful (color-coded) icons render their state color from session start — `IconManager` now *pins* explicitly-colored icons, and the state-cycling behavior is centralized in a new shared `IconStates`.** Live report (mayatk Channels filter/invert/target toggles, and every `ToggleOption`/`ResetOption`-style tint): a state toggle's color coding only appeared after the first click — every fresh session started with plain theme-colored icons. Root cause chain: the option button registers with `IconManager` as theme-managed at creation (`_options.py` `create_widget`, recording the pre-theme fallback color), the state visuals are then applied with `auto_theme=False` — which never updated the registry — and the session's FIRST style application (`StyleSheet._set_style` → `update_widget_icons`) saw recorded-color ≠ theme-color and blindly re-rendered the icon in the theme color, wiping the state tint (later re-shows skip the sweep, which is why only new sessions desynced; `OptionBox._update_sizing`'s color-less `fit_icon` re-fit was a second clobber path). Fix at the choke point everything already flows through: an **explicitly-passed color now pins the icon** — `set_icon` records name/size/**color** in the registry for pinned widgets too, `update_widget_icons` skips pinned entries (theme-managed icons keep following sweeps exactly as before), `_update_sizing` re-fits at the recorded pinned color, and a later theme-managed call (`color=None, auto_theme=True`) clears the pin (the `reset.py` un-bypass / colorless-state contract, unchanged). This fixes ActionOption states, ToggleOption/DisableOption/ResetOption tints, and the sequencer transport's play tint (previously wiped by any sweep during playback) with zero call-site changes. **Centralization:** the state-cycling behavior (apply icon/color/tooltip per state, cycle on activate, per-state callbacks) moved out of `ActionOption` into the new **`mixins/icon_states.py::IconStates`**, which `ActionOption` now delegates to and `Footer.add_action_button` gains via a new `states=` parameter (exposed as `btn.icon_states`) — one implementation for option-box actions and footer buttons. `IconStates.activate()` also fixes the two-widgets-one-state drift class: a callback that assigns `current_state` (syncing several toggles to one app state) supersedes the auto-advance, so explicit sync and self-cycling can't fight. `set_action`/`add_action` now return the created `ActionOption` (was the manager; nothing chained on it — verified by monorepo grep) so app code can keep a handle for state sync; `FilterOption`'s scope-action internals moved onto the public `current_state` accessor. **Critique-pass hardening (same change set):** the registry's id-keyed side dicts (`_widget_icon_info` / `_last_update_color`) never self-cleaned — once the weak registry dropped a dead widget, its entries were orphaned *forever* (a per-dead-widget leak, and the CPython id-reuse hazard `PinValuesOption` guarded ad-hoc; trusting a stale entry's new `color` field would have widened that to a wrong pinned tint). The theme sweep now purges orphans, and the ownership-validated lookup is centralized as public **`IconManager.registered_info(widget)`** — used by `_update_sizing`, `swap_icon`'s size fallback (both previously trusted unvalidated entries), and `PinValuesOption` (replacing its inline guard). Pinned by the new `test_icon_states.py` (14: pin survives sweep / unpin restores theme-following / registry records for re-fits / unowned-entry rejection / orphan purge; IconStates attach-applies-state-0, cycle, sync-supersedes-advance, notify suppression, fallback callback; ActionOption end-to-end sweep survival; Footer states render-at-creation + click-cycle + programmatic sync). Consumers: mayatk/blendertk Channels drop their manual footer-tint dance entirely (see their CHANGELOGs, same date).
- **2026-07-12 — `WidgetComboBox`: the dropdown-affordance arrow is now off by default, and its glyph + opacity are exposed.** The widget used to draw a down-triangle after the current text unconditionally (`arrow_direction` defaulted to `"down"`) — the only combo in the library that painted an affordance at all, since the base `ComboBox`/`CustomStyle` draws none and the theme hides Qt's native `QComboBox::down-arrow`. `arrow_direction` now defaults to `None` (no affordance), so `WidgetComboBox` matches every other combo unless a caller opts in; two new properties expose the affordance for callers who want one: `arrow_icon` (a `QIcon` drawn in place of the triangle, at a font-scaled size, dimmed via `QIcon.Disabled` when the combo is disabled just as the triangle dims via `QPalette.Disabled`, taking precedence over `arrow_direction`; type-guarded, `None` to clear) and `arrow_alpha` (0.0–1.0 opacity applied to whichever affordance is drawn, clamped). `paintEvent` draws nothing when neither a direction nor a non-null icon is set. Note: the ~handful of existing `WidgetComboBox` instances (scene_exporter/hierarchy_manager `.ui` combos, the shots combos, the example, mayatk's channels enum cells) used the widget for its embedding/actions features and inherited the arrow incidentally — they now render arrow-less like every other combo; set `arrow_direction = "down"` (or an `arrow_icon`) on any that should keep one. Pinned by `test_widget_combobox.py::TestWidgetComboBoxArrowAffordance` (5: off-by-default, direction validation, icon type-guard + clear, alpha clamp, and every paint path renders without error offscreen). Verified under Maya's own PySide6 6.5.3 via `mayapy`.
- **2026-07-12 — `TableWidget`: new opt-in `set_cell_widget_click_columns` forwards dead-space clicks on a cell-widget cell to the embedded widget.** Live report (Channels): clicking an enum row's value cell only opened the dropdown when the click landed on the small combobox at the left — the rest of the wide (Stretch) value cell was dead. A `setCellWidget` widget is normally stretched to fill its cell by the view, but a combobox created with `AdjustToContents` self-resizes to its content width when its contents/metrics change *after* the view's last layout, and the table doesn't re-stretch it until its next relayout — so the closed combo collapses to ~44px inside a ~337px cell (reproduced under Maya's own PySide6 6.5.3 via `mayapy`: `337→44` on a post-layout self-resize; a plain fill or a theme polish alone does NOT reproduce it, which is why it only shows in the live panel). Rather than chase every code path that can leave a cell widget narrow, the table now offers explicit forwarding: for registered columns, a bare LMB click that reaches the view (i.e. the widget did NOT cover that point — so it never double-fires for a widget that got the click directly) is routed to the cell's embedded control via `_forward_click_to_cell_widget` — a `QComboBox` opens its popup, a `QAbstractButton` is clicked, anything else focusable takes focus. Cells often wrap the real control in a centering container (the style/color-mapping editors' swatch/spinbox/reset pattern), so the helper resolves to the first interactive descendant before acting. Placed after the single-click-edit branch in `mouseReleaseEvent`, gated on `cellWidget(...) is not None`, so numeric/text value cells still open their editor and only widget-hosting cells forward; a no-op (never reached) when the widget already spans the cell. Pinned by `test_table_widget_click_forward.py` (6: helper resolves combo/button/wrapped-container/no-op, plus end-to-end `QTest` dead-space click on a deliberately-narrow combo forwards, and an unregistered column stays inert). mayatk's Channels value column opts in. (The Style Editor and Color Mapping Editor have the same fixed-size-widget-in-wide-cell dead space, but use plain `QTableWidget` — opting them in would first require moving them onto uitk's `TableWidget`; left as a follow-up.)
- **2026-07-12 — `Region.visible_on_mouse_over` tracks its connection state — kills the per-construction `libpyside: Failed to disconnect` RuntimeWarning flood on PySide6 6.10 (two per Region, hundreds per DCC launch) and a latent double-connect.** Found while probing the Blender activation regression below: every launch drowned the console in disconnect warnings from `region.py`. `__init__` assigns the property its default `False`, and the setter unconditionally attempted to disconnect never-connected signals — PySide2 raises `RuntimeError` there (the existing `except` silenced it), but PySide6 6.10 instead *emits a libpyside RuntimeWarning per call* and returns, so the guard silenced nothing. The same by-current-value logic also stacked a duplicate connection on a repeated `True` (child-visibility slots fired twice per enter/leave, and one opt-out left a live connection behind). The setter now tracks `_mouse_over_connected` and connects/disconnects only on a real state change (the `except RuntimeError` stays for PySide2). Pinned fail-first by the new `test_region.py` (no warning on construction / repeated `False` — asserted via `warnings.simplefilter("error")`; a single opt-out after a repeated `True` fully disconnects; enter/leave toggle contract).
- **2026-07-12 — Marking menu: activation regression on Qt 6.10 hosts fixed — the suppressed present leaked `WindowFullScreen` into the hidden overlay, so the first real present mapped a ~100×30 stub instead of fullscreen ("the key steals focus but no menu appears", Blender/PySide6 6.10.1).** Live report: the tentacle marking menu stopped launching in Blender — F12 visibly pulled focus off Blender but nothing showed. Fresh-instance probes isolated it: registration, keymap, operator, and the show state machine were all healthy (`drive_press()` → `isVisible=True`), but the overlay's geometry was `(-122, -1600, 100, 30)` — default widget size at the screen origin, invisible. Root cause is an interaction between the 2026-07-09 construction-realize fix and Qt 6.10: `_suppressed_present()` ends with the base-class `hide()`, and `hide()` **keeps the window state** — so the overlay sat hidden with `WindowFullScreen` still set, and the first activation's `showFullScreen()` (present-last path) saw "already fullscreen", performed **no state transition, applied no fullscreen geometry**, and mapped the window at its pre-fullscreen "normal" geometry — the exact stub geometry the construction fix's own commit message describes. Reproduced in pure PySide6 6.10.1 with no uitk involved (`WA_DontShowOnScreen` + `showFullScreen` + `QWidget.hide` + clear attr → next `showFullScreen` maps 640×480 at the screen origin); Maya's bundled 6.5.3 happens to re-apply the geometry, which is why the 07-09 fix live-verified clean in Maya while silently breaking Blender. The offscreen QPA maps every window at virtual-screen size, masking the geometry symptom in CI. Fix (all in `_suppressed_present`'s teardown, while hidden — nothing paints): **(1)** drop `WindowFullScreen` from the window state right after the base-class hide, so every real present transitions Normal → FullScreen and applies the fullscreen geometry on every Qt version. **(2)** Clearing the state alone regressed centering (caught by `test_preloaded_page_first_activation_centers`, 1105 px off on a desktop QPA): the state clear restores Qt's stale "normal" geometry on the hidden overlay, and the present-last path centers pages via `mapFromGlobal` against the hidden overlay *before* the present — so the teardown re-pins the screen rect. **(3)** The widget-side `setGeometry` isn't enough on Qt 6.10: a hidden top-level's `QWidget.setGeometry` **never reaches the platform window** (probed both ways — a never-mapped window sits at the platform's creation-default position; a fullscreen-state clear on a previously-mapped one silently restores its stale "normal" position), and `mapFromGlobal` reads the **native** position — the pre-present anchor mapping was off by the (native-pos − screen-origin) delta. New `_move_hidden_overlay(rect)` moves the hidden overlay at BOTH layers (widget + `QWindow.setGeometry`, which verifiably moves the hidden native window in both cases; on 6.5 the handle write is simply redundant), used by the teardown **and** by `_ensure_fullscreen_on_active_screen`'s relocate-while-hidden branch — the multi-monitor hop had the same latent pre-existing desync on 6.10 (its visible mid-gesture branch, Maya-live-verified, is untouched). Covers both context users (construction realize + `_flush_first_show` preload warm-up). Pinned fail-first by `test_marking_menu_present_order.py::TestConstructionDoesNotPresent::test_construction_leaves_no_stale_fullscreen_state` (asserts the state leak itself — deterministic offscreen); the centering invariant was already pinned by `test_marking_menu_preload.py` (desktop-QPA-sensitive: fails at 1105 px with the state-clear-only fix, 0 px with the geometry pin). Live-verified in a fresh Blender 5.1 (real config, real `TclBlender`, the keymap operator's own `drive_press` path): overlay presents at the full screen rect, `hud#startmenu` current, release hides clean, across two consecutive activation cycles.
- **2026-07-10 — `ExpandableList`: the overlay presets are the one exception to content-sizing — their first sublist covers the starting list.** Follow-up to the content-sizing fix below: an `expand_overlay` / `expand_overlay_left` first sublist sits directly *on top of* the starting list, so sizing it to its own (often narrower) content left the list peeking out — it must be at least as wide as the list it overlays. Rather than reintroduce a per-slot width pin, the widget now owns the rule: `_handle_widget_enter_event` sizes a sublist to `max(sizeHint().width(), self.width())` when `self.position.startswith("overlay")`, and to plain `sizeHint().width()` otherwise. `self` is the list that owns the trigger, so only the *first* overlay sublist widens; deeper sublists in the chain fan out (child position "right"/"left") and stay content-sized. `startswith("overlay")` needs no lookup table and auto-covers any future `overlay_*` position. Pinned by `test_expandable_list.py::{test_overlay_first_sublist_covers_starting_list_width (both overlay presets),test_nonoverlay_sublist_stays_content_width_under_wide_root,test_deep_overlay_sublist_is_content_sized_not_covering}`.
- **2026-07-10 — `ExpandableList`: sublists size to their own contents again instead of the starting list's width.** Live report: every flyout came out as wide as the root list rather than hugging its own (usually narrower) items. Cause: `_create_sublist_config` spread `**self.kwargs` verbatim into each sublist's constructor, so a width-pinning kwarg on the root — e.g. the `setMinimumWidth=120` in the module's own `__main__` demo, or any `setFixedWidth` a caller passes — was applied to every sublist as a hard `minimumWidth`/`fixedWidth`, and `resize(sizeHint())` then clamped up to it. Because the pin also lived in each sublist's own `self.kwargs`, it cascaded down the whole chain. Fix expresses the invariant directly instead of enumerating the ways to violate it: a sublist carries no size constraint of its own — its `sizeHint` (widest item + margins) is the whole story — so `_add_sublist` resets every new sublist to `setMinimumSize(0, 0)` / `setMaximumSize(QWIDGETSIZE_MAX, ...)` right after construction. That clears whatever floor/cap/pin the root's kwargs applied (robust to `setMinimumWidth`, `setFixedWidth`, `setMaximumWidth`, the whole-`*Size` forms, and any future width-setting kwarg — no denylist to keep in sync), at every depth. Item heights are constrained on the items, not the list, so the list stays fully unconstrained; a constraint a caller sets *after* creation (e.g. a slot's explicit `setMinimumWidth`) runs later and still wins. Pinned by `test_expandable_list.py::{test_sublist_sizes_to_own_content_not_root_width,test_nested_sublist_also_sizes_to_own_content,test_sublist_not_capped_by_root_max_width}` (all fail pre-fix: sublist inherits the root's 200/180px min or 30px max width). Full suite re-run green; badge refreshed.
- **2026-07-10 — Preload path hardening (adversarial-review follow-up to scoped preloading).** (1) `MainWindow.showEvent` no longer calls `activateWindow()` when its top-level window carries `WA_DontShowOnScreen` — during a warm-up the suppressed present delivers real show events to stacked pages, and the unconditional activate resolved to the overlay's realized-but-never-mapped native window, issuing SetForegroundWindow with nothing on screen: the startup-idle focus-steal class the construction fix closed on the hide side, now closed on the show side too. (2) `_preload_next`'s mid-gesture retry guards a C++-destroyed-without-`retire()` overlay (host teardown / dev reload) — the pending timer callback ends the chain quietly instead of raising RuntimeError into the DCC event loop. (3) Synchronous `preload_menus(defer=False)` now bails per-page when the overlay is visible instead of half-warming: `_flush_first_show` no-oped but `_init_ui` had already run, so the later real show re-ran it and stacked a duplicate `on_child_registered` connection. (4) PinValues' icon-idempotence check validates entry ownership through `IconManager`'s weak registry — the info dict is keyed by `id()` and outlives dead widgets until the next theme sweep, so CPython id reuse could match a stale entry and silently skip a new pin button's first icon. (5) The show-return registration probe in `test_dynamic_slot_init.py` guards dead menu wrappers left by earlier tests (the same hazard the production flush already guards). Full suite re-run green; badge refreshed.

- **2026-07-10 — Marking menu: scoped preloading — the FIRST activation now behaves exactly like every later one.** Live report (Maya): the first `key_show` press "doesn't behave the same as the second — it feels like it hasn't been initialized yet." Cause: a cold page paid its entire initialization inside the first gesture — the `.ui` load, `_init_ui`, slot-class instantiation and signal wiring (`register_children`), QSS polish, and `fit_height_to_content` — and because `_show_marking_menu` deliberately presents LAST (the reopen-flash fix), that first-show work was delivered by the present itself, *after* `setCurrentWidget` had already centered the page on the gesture anchor. The page was therefore positioned against its pre-init 600×600 fallback geometry and visibly settled once the first `showEvent` fit it (repro pinned the drift at **~246 px off-anchor on the first press vs 0 px on the second** — a desynced flick origin plus the on-screen snap). The `precompile=True` option never covered this: it only pre-compiles stale `_ui.py` artifacts in a background thread (and only under `CompiledLoader`) — it never instantiates or initializes the pages. Two complementary fixes in `_marking_menu.py`: **(1) scoped preloading** — new `preload=True` ctor opt-in / public `preload_menus(names=None, defer=True)`: warms the *distinct binding-target* menus (never the whole UI registry — standalone tool windows stay lazy) through the REAL show path while nothing paints, via `_flush_first_show`'s `WA_DontShowOnScreen` suppressed-present (the same trick construction uses to realize the overlay; base-class hide, so no startup focus steal). Deferred and staggered — one page per event-loop tick, waiting out any live gesture — so DCC startup isn't blocked; idempotent, so re-running after a bindings change warms only new targets, and an unresolvable target is skipped, never fatal. **(2) cold-show re-center backstop** — for any page that still reaches the activation path uninitialized (preloading off, freshly retargeted binding), `_show_marking_menu` re-centers it on the SAME anchor immediately after the present delivers its first `showEvent` (positioning tail split out of `setCurrentWidget` as `_position_current_widget`; the tracking cache refreshes for the just-registered children). The activation anchor is now also resolved ONCE per show — screen selection, centering, `start_gesture`, and the re-center all read the same point instead of four cursor re-reads that could drift px apart. Present-order invariants untouched (page swap still precedes the present; `test_marking_menu_present_order` green). Pinned fail-first by `test_marking_menu_preload.py` (real `MarkingMenu` + real Switchboard/MainWindow pages: preload warms exactly the binding targets without presenting and without leaking the suppression attribute; ctor-flag deferred warm-up; mid-gesture deferral; cold first activation ends ≤2 px off its gesture origin, first == second). Tentacle opts in (`TclMaya`/`TclBlender` pass `preload=True`).
- **2026-07-09 — Option-box menus: the first-open "widgets flash briefly then vanish before the menu appears" is fixed — the apply/defaults buttons no longer map as stray top-level windows.** Live report (after the init-flash sweep and the overlay-construction fix): option-box menus specifically still flashed transient widgets on init — other menus were clean. A fresh-Maya app-wide SHOW/HIDE timeline driving the real □ `MenuOption` click (`tb005`/`tb003` on `polygons#component#submenu`) caught it exactly: during the popup's lazy first-show setup (`_prepare_for_show`), `ActionButtonManager.create_button` built each action button **parentless** and called `setVisible(True)` on it (`visible=contains_items`) *before* `add_button` parented it into the container — and a parentless widget made visible **maps as its own on-screen top-level window**. `actionButton_defaults` and `actionButton_apply` each appeared as a real stray window for ~12–19 ms (at Qt's default placement, on-screen), were hidden by the reparent, and only then did the menu show — precisely the reported "widgets showing briefly and immediately hiding, before the actual option box menu is shown". Option-box-only because `OptionBoxManager.enable_menu` defaults `add_apply_button`/`add_defaults_button` to True (plain context/dropdown menus default them off); first-open-only because on every later open the buttons already exist. Fix at the source: the button is created **parented to the manager's container** (`QPushButton(text, self.container)`), so it can never map alone — the pre-insert `setVisible(True)` now just marks it shown-with-parent (`visible=False` semantics unchanged; the container itself stays unparented-but-never-visible until placed, preserving `_setup_defaults_button`'s placement guard; `_setup_presets` audited clean — its combo is parented before any show). Pinned fail-first by `test_first_paint_stability.py::test_first_popup_open_maps_no_stray_toplevel` (app-level spy: NO top-level widget but the menu itself may receive Show during a first `show_as_popup` of an option-box-configured menu; pre-fix it captures both stray buttons, offscreen). Live re-verified in a fresh Maya on the same real □ click: zero stray top-level shows in the first-open window — the buttons appear only as children in the menu's own show cascade, and the menu maps once, already at final geometry; first-open now has the same shape as reopen.
- **2026-07-09 — Marking menu: the init-only flash (components painting at wrong geometries before the first menu appears) is fixed — construction no longer presents the overlay.** Live report after the init-flash sweep landed: still "flashing on init before the menu is shown (which could be the option box init)". An app-wide visibility/paint timeline in a fresh Maya (every widget SHOW/HIDE + visible MOVE/RESIZE + top-level paints, ms-stamped, from `TclMaya()` construction through page switch) caught the real mechanism — not the option-box popup path at all: `MarkingMenu.__init__` called a bare `showFullScreen()` (the screen bind `_ensure_fullscreen_on_active_screen` reads), **presenting** the translucent overlay at DCC startup and leaving it visible — unnoticed, because a fully-transparent layered window is per-pixel click-through — until the first gesture's `hide()`. The FIRST activation therefore ran the cross-screen fullscreen relocate on a VISIBLE window, and `setWindowState(~FullScreen)` restores Qt's ~100×30 pre-fullscreen "normal" geometry on screen: the timeline shows paints at the stale full-screen rect → a 100×30 stub at the screen origin → the stub centered → only then the final overlay rect (three wrong-geometry paints in ~60 ms — the reported flash; init-only, because every later activation starts hidden and relocates invisibly). Construction now realizes the native window under `WA_DontShowOnScreen` (`showFullScreen()` + base-class `hide()`, attribute cleared after): handle + screen bind preserved, nothing presented, and the first activation takes the same present-last path as every reopen. Base-class hide deliberately — the `hide()` override ends by raising/activating the parent DCC main window, a focus steal at startup-idle; its gesture cleanup is all no-op pre-gesture and `hideEvent`'s safety net runs either way. Pinned by `test_marking_menu_present_order.py::TestConstructionDoesNotPresent` (real `__init__`, fails pre-fix with the overlay left visible; also asserts the realized handle and that the suppression attribute doesn't leak); that module's docstring no longer claims construction "legitimately presents". Live re-verified in a fresh Maya (dev tree, real TclMaya): construction is screen-silent (its one paint event occurs unmapped, under the attribute), and the first show presents exactly once — SHOW and first PAINT both already at the final overlay geometry.
- **2026-07-09 — Fix: a plain (non-checkable) push button's label was persisted as state, so renaming a button in the `.ui` didn't stick — the stale saved label was replayed over it on restore.** `ValueManager.get_value` falls through to `widget.text()` for anything text-bearing, and a `QPushButton`'s default "clicked" signal has no state getter so it uses that fallback — so a launcher button's label got saved to QSettings and, on the next restore, `set_value` wrote the *old* label back over the `.ui` value (surfaced live: a UV-panel launcher renamed "Transform" → "More.." in the `.ui` kept showing the stale "Transform"). A button is an action/toggle, not a text field (as `is_widget_supported` already documents — "QPushButton *if it has isChecked*"): `get_value` now returns a **checkable** button's `isChecked()` and `None` for a plain one, and `set_value` applies only a checkable button's checked state, never writing a stored label over a plain button (which also subsumes the old icon-only-option-button `setText` skip). Value-display buttons are unaffected — their labels are always *derived* from other persisted state on restore (e.g. crease's `"Crease {s003}"` off the spinbox, scene's `"Save to: {path}"` off a live scene query), never the button's own saved text. `test_value_manager.py` `test_noncheckable_pushbutton_label_is_not_state` updated to assert the corrected contract (label preserved, no persistable value); checkable-button + text-widget round-trips unchanged.
- **2026-07-09 — Init-flash sweep: menus/option-boxes no longer flash during initialization — every post-paint visual correction is now pre-paint work or a conditional no-op.** User report: menus/option-boxes visibly flash on init (most noticed on option-box Menu popups). Root pattern (3-agent exploration + spikes): uitk's anti-flash doctrine is "all visual state final before `MainWindow.showEvent` returns", and every remaining flash was an escape from it — post-paint `singleShot(0)` corrections, or measurement against stale style state. **Mechanism spike** (offscreen, 3 iterations): the "pre-polish inflation" is NOT lazy polish — ancestor `setStyleSheet` re-resolves type-selector rules immediately; the real trigger is **property-selector QSS** (`[class="..."]`): a `setProperty` after a widget's first polish leaves stale metrics until an `unpolish`/`polish` cycle (`ensurePolished` does NOT help — the widget is already polished). Fixes, each TDD'd fail-first: **(1) repolish-before-measure** — new shared `repolish_tree()` (`mixins/style_sheet.py`; NB uses unbound `QWidget.style(w)` — uitk widgets shadow `.style` with a StyleSheet manager instance) called in `OptionBox.wrap` after property stamps/border styling and before sizing, and in the marking-menu MenuButton fit (`style.set` + repolish now run BEFORE `center_widget`, was measure-then-style — the Blender ~80px inflation site). **(2)** `OptionBoxContainer.showEvent` refit demoted to a **conditional** safety net (`_content_fit_pending`; `_adjust_to_content` gains a no-op move guard) — no timer scheduled when wrap-time geometry is already final; the manually-inflated case (`TestOptionBoxOverlayRefit`) still corrects. **(3) pre-paint registration flush** — `Menu.add`'s deferred item registration (tick-0 timer, escaping mid-add recursion) fired AFTER first paint (the bench's `05_drain_deferred_timers` flicker); `MainWindow.register_children` now flushes every pending menu registration at its end via private `_flush_pending_registrations` (WeakSet-tracked, `_add_depth==0` only — the recursion contract preserved exactly, fixpoint-capped; armed timers later no-op). **(4) chrome initial state final** — ClearOption computes visibility synchronously at setup/Show (empty field never paints a visible-then-hidden clear button; the deferred pass stays as the state-restore net); PinValuesOption sets its initial icon synchronously at create (`_update_button_icon` made idempotent via `IconManager._widget_icon_info`); `Header.showEvent` runs `_sync_menu_button_visibility` + `_apply_auto_hide_with_os_frame` synchronously (child showEvent is pre-paint; a menu populated later in the cascade re-shows the button via `on_item_added`, still pre-paint). **(5) no stray popups** — `Menu._add_action_widget` REALLY showed a temporary QMenu (+`processEvents`) to realize `widgetForAction`, flashing an empty popup during `add()`; that API is also gone from newer PySide6 (6.10) so the path hard-crashed there (pre-existing): replaced with `QWidgetAction.defaultWidget()` taken directly / a `QToolButton` carrier for plain QActions. **(6)** `OptionBox.wrap` widens update suppression to the top-level window when it's already visible (slow-path retry wrap → one repaint). New shared test harness: `conftest.visual_state_snapshot`/`assert_stable_after_show` + the `FIRST_PAINT_QSS` property-selector reproducer (type-rule floor + property-rule collapse — deterministic on any style, offscreen-safe); suite `test_first_paint_stability.py` (12 tests) + `TestPrePaintRegistrationFlush` in `test_dynamic_slot_init.py`. Live DCC verification (fresh Maya = no-regression on tight-hint `adskdarkflatui`; fresh Blender = fix-works on the 80px-floor style, incl. the popup-first-open probe) — see the session notes; the popup flash's dominant live contributor is expected to be (3)+(5).

- **2026-07-09 — Marking menu: reopen no longer flashes the previous gesture's menu — the overlay presents only after the target page is current.** Live symptom: after launching a standalone window from a submenu (a `hide()` not driven by the activation-key release), the next activation briefly showed that submenu before snapping to the start menu. The logical reset was verified fine (the submenu is explicitly hidden, the overlay path clears on hide, and reopen always resolves a start menu); the flash was a presentation-order seam: `_show_marking_menu` presented the overlay window (`_ensure_fullscreen_on_active_screen` → `showFullScreen()`) BEFORE `setCurrentWidget` selected the target page. The overlay is a translucent (layered) window — when re-shown, the OS re-presents its last composed frame and Qt replaces it only on the first repaint after the show, so the first visible frame(s) of every reopen were the previous gesture's surface. Fix: `_ensure_fullscreen_on_active_screen` now owns geometry only (it re-presents on relocation only when already visible — the mid-gesture monitor hop); a hidden overlay is presented LAST in `_show_marking_menu`, after the page swap, so its first presented frame is the correct menu. Pinned by the new `test_marking_menu_present_order.py` (real `_show_marking_menu`/`setCurrentWidget`/`hide` methods, presentation-order probe; the regression case fails pre-fix with `presented=[None]`), and `test_marking_menu_multiscreen.py` updated to the split contract (relocate-while-hidden defers presentation; indeterminate screen is a strict no-op). En route, fixed a pre-existing test-fidelity defect: `test_marking_menu.py::test_sync_menu_to_state_blocked_when_hidden` asserted an `isHidden()` gate that existed only in its own stub — production has no such gate and must not (`_on_activation_press` syncs while hidden to open the menu at all); the stub's gate is removed and the test now asserts the real guard (`_show_window` clears `_activation_key_held` → the resolver returns None). Live-verified in a fresh Maya (real TclMaya, dev tree): reopen presents with the target page current (`presented=['hud#startmenu']`, never `[None]`); two activation cycles clean. **Follow-up — second mechanism, same symptom (logical, not compositional):** `MainWindow.setVisible` is pin-gated (a pinned window silently refuses `hide()`), and `MarkingMenu.hide()` reset the pin AFTER `setCurrentIndex(-1)` had already tried (and been vetoed) to hide the page — so a pinned submenu survived in shown-state with its pin cleared, and Qt re-shows shown-state children with the overlay on the next present: the submenu that launched a standalone window re-appeared on the next activation. Fix: the pin-reset is extracted to `_reset_stacked_pin(ui)` (also clears the WINDOW-level pin/`prevent_hide` — `setVisible` consults the window flag, and `Header.reset_pin_state` no-ops unless the *header* believes it's pinned, so a desynced or absent header used to leave the veto in place) and runs BEFORE the hide; a `_hide_stacked_leftovers()` sweep then unpins + explicitly hides every stacked child still in SHOWN-state (predicate = `not isHidden()`, the child's own state — `isVisible()` is False for every child under a hidden parent, which would blind the sweep exactly when the overlay is already down). The sweep runs from both `hide()` (covers hide-on-already-hidden, e.g. `retire()`, which sends no QHideEvent) and `hideEvent` (covers bypassed hides — a parent `setVisible(False)`); direct children of the overlay only, no switchboard dependency, idempotent. Pinned by `TestHideDefeatsPinnedPages` (5 tests: unpin-before-hide, desynced-header window-level clear, non-current dodged-page sweep, bypassed-hide sweep, ghost-under-hidden-overlay sweep — all failing pre-fix). **Third mechanism — the retained-buffer flash (pixel layer):** with both logical fixes in, a *momentary* flash of the previous submenu remained on reopen. The overlay is a layered (translucent) window: the OS re-presents its last composed frame on show and Qt repaints only *after* that present — and since the page swap happens while hidden (present-last) and hidden windows never repaint, the buffer still held the previous gesture's pixels. Fix at both ends: `hide()` flushes a CLEARED frame while still visible (pages down + `overlay.clear_paint_events()` + synchronous `repaint()` → the retained frame is empty/invisible instead of stale), and `_show_marking_menu` forces a `repaint()` immediately after presenting so the real menu doesn't wait on the host's next paint cycle (user-visible gap under a busy DCC loop). Pinned by `test_hide_flushes_cleared_frame_while_still_visible` + `test_reopen_pushes_fresh_frame_after_present` (both failing pre-fix); overlay test doubles gained `clear_paint_events` to match the real interface.

- **2026-07-09 — OptionBox: the text-to-option seam is tightened via a negative layout spacer.** With the authored-width floor in place, an option square butted straight onto the wrapped button's edge left the FULL side padding at the seam — too airy. The first adjacent option now tucks over the button's edge by a fraction of the perceived padding (`OptionBox._seam_overlap`, `_SEAM_OVERLAP_FRACTION = 0.75` → a quarter of the padding remains at the seam): expressed as a negative `addSpacing` inside the container's HBox so the *layout owns the overlap* (a manual `move()` nudge would be undone on every re-layout) and the container's size hint shrinks with it; option widgets are added after the wrapped widget, so they stack on top across the strip. The theme's padding QSS is untouched. Gated to seams where the rule is meaningful: anchored absolute wraps (stable authored width), a text `QPushButton` host (centered label), and a square icon button as the adjacent option — a `ValueOption` field keeps its flush seam, and a text wider than the authored width degrades to no overlap. Pinned in `TestOptionBoxOverlayRefit`.

- **2026-07-09 — OptionBoxContainer: wrapped rows anchor to the wrapped widget's authored center; authored width becomes the wrapped widget's minimum.** Two live symptoms on marking-menu surfaces (tentacle `polygons#component#submenu` `tb003` 'Extrude'): the row *drifted* when shown, and the label sat *jammed against the button edges* once the option-box square was added. Cause 1: the container is created at the wrapped widget's top-left but at Qt's **default widget size**, so `_adjust_to_content`'s "preserve current center" preserved the default-geometry center — off from the widget it replaced by half the size delta, both axes. `wrap()` now captures the widget's authored geometry (before the layout reparents it): the container starts there, and every content re-fit re-centers on that anchor (`_anchor_center`), so the row stays exactly where the Designer placed it. Cause 2: the container's collapse-to-content gave the wrapped button its QSS-tight `sizeHint` (text + 1px padding), discarding the Designer-authored width; the authored width is now the wrapped widget's `minimumWidth` in the absolute-positioned branch (a floor, not a ceiling — a wider content hint still wins; layout-managed wraps are untouched). Pinned by `TestOptionBoxOverlayRefit` (anchor + floor tests, 3 failing pre-fix).

- **2026-07-09 — Marking menu: stuck `:pressed` (checked-orange) MenuButton fixed; content-fit resize is now nav-only.** A press over an owned menu item is deliberately passed through to the button (Qt sets it `down`), but the matching release was dispatched-and-consumed by `_handle_menu_item_release` / `child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent` and never reached the button's own `mouseReleaseEvent` — leaving `down` latched, so the button painted the `.MenuButton:pressed` orange tint whenever un-hovered (`QAbstractButton:hover` outranks it by specificity while hovered, which is why the stick only showed on hover-leave). Manifested on tentacle's `polygons#submenu` `i010` — the one MenuButton whose hover-nav is a self-referential no-op (`submenu_name()` == its own UI), so the only nav button ever pressed while it stays visible. Every release-consume path now clears the down state (`_clear_button_down`, on both the resolved dispatch target and the grab-holding child — cursor drift can make those differ), with a `MenuButton.hideEvent` backstop mirroring the existing `WA_UnderMouse` clear. Separately, `add_child_event_filter`'s center-preserving content-fit resize (`center_widget(padding_x=35)`) now applies **only to `MenuButton`s** — regular slot buttons/labels/checkboxes keep their Designer-authored geometry; an option-box-wrapped widget is fitted by its `OptionBoxContainer` instead (`_adjust_to_content` — default-on, center-preserving, unchanged). Pinned by `test_marking_menu_pressed_state.py` (6 tests, all failing pre-fix).

- **2026-07-08 — `TextEditLogHandler._safe_append` no longer force-paints a hidden widget (native-crash fix).** The handler's live-repaint throttle called `widget.repaint()` + `QApplication.processEvents()` on every throttle window regardless of visibility. Pumping the event queue from inside a log emit while a panel is still being constructed dispatches deferred events against half-built widgets — a native access violation (segfault) the handler's try/except can't catch, reproduced by blendertk's `.venv` ui-handler harness (20+ panels whose slots log during `__init__`). The forced paint now runs only when the widget `isVisible()` — a hidden log target needs no live repaint, and visible-panel behavior (live log during blocking ops) is unchanged. Pinned by `TestSafeAppendHiddenWidgetNoForcePaint` (hidden = append without repaint; visible = repaint kept). The same pump was also masking real deferred-init bugs downstream: it incidentally fired other panels' `singleShot(0)` init callbacks mid-load (see blendertk's same-day CHANGELOG entry).

- **2026-07-08 Fix: a widget whose objectName matched a `MainWindow` method (e.g. a group named `move`) crashed the window on show/drag.** `register_widget` binds every child as an attribute via `setattr(self, objectName, widget)`, so a `CollapsableGroup` named `move` overwrote `QWidget.move` — then `center_widget`'s `widget.move(pos)` and `Header.mouseMoveEvent`'s `self.window().move(...)` raised `TypeError: '<widget>' object is not callable` (surfaced live by a co-located Maya UV panel whose Move group was named `move`, and again each time it was dragged). The setattr is now skipped (with a warning naming `sb.get_widget` as the accessor) when the objectName shadows a callable class attribute; the widget is still fully registered (`self.widgets` + slot wiring) and reachable — only the convenience attribute is withheld, so the shadowed method keeps working. Non-colliding names (the overwhelming majority — an ecosystem-wide `.ui` sweep found `move` as the sole collision) are unaffected.
- **2026-07-08 Sequencer widget full review (three-way adversarial audit, 44 findings): drag/undo protocol hardened, Qt5 crash path gated, scroll-pinning + stale-geometry fixes, and the dead ShotLaneItem system removed (the shot context menu is reachable again).** Paired with mayatk's same-day shots review (its controller consumes this widget; the 34-connect signal contract was audited clean). **Interaction correctness:** `resize_left` snapped AFTER the min-duration clamp, so a snap could overshoot it and emit a zero/**negative**-duration `clip_resized` (consumers handed Maya an inverted `scaleKey` range) — it now snaps first then clamps, mirroring `resize_right` (`TestResizeLeftSnapClamp`). Zero-duration (stepped/point) clips render narrower than the resize handles, so `_hit_zone` never returned "move" and they were **impossible to drag** — no-body-zone clips now hit-test as "move" (`TestZeroDurationClipHitZone`). The undo protocol captured a snapshot on mouse **press** and cleared the redo stack — every selection click burned a no-op undo entry and destroyed redo (50 clicks evicted all real history); capture is now lazy on the first actual mouse-move (per-item `_undo_captured`, honored by Escape-cancel), key clicks capture **nothing** (the snapshot records only clip bounds, so it could never restore a key edit — it just consumed a step), and release handlers emit **only on change**: clip move/resize (0.01 gate, matching the gap overlay's precedent), `range_highlight_changed` (a zero-motion edge click used to trigger a full save + resize + rebuild in the consumer), and `marker_moved` (a selection click dirtied the consumer's persisted store). The keyframe Escape-cancel now invalidates the pre-restore expanded bounds (mirrors the move path — dragged-out keys no longer leave ghost curve pixels), and the dead "re-select the parent clip" call in the key press handler was removed (sub-row clips are never selectable; it was a guaranteed no-op). Double-click rename is gated on `read_only` and `sub_row` like the context menu (renaming an attribute row's tooltip via an editor spawned over the curve made no sense). **Chrome/lifecycle:** the scrub player's `_QT_MEDIA_OK` gated only the QtMultimedia *import*, but Qt5's classes import fine and lack the Qt6 API used (`setSource`/`setAudioOutput`) — first use crashed on PySide2 instead of the documented no-op degrade; availability now checks the API. `TransportControls`' 400 ms controller-poll timer started in `__init__` and never stopped — a hidden panel polled `cmds.play` for the life of the session; it now runs only while visible. The default `ScrubPlayerPlayController` seeked with a hardcoded 24 fps ignoring `set_audio_source(fps=…)` (playhead→audio-position math was wrong for any other rate) and its `is_playing()` latched True forever after end-of-media (green play button; next press became a no-op stop) — fps reads the widget's live `_audio_fps` and the flag reconciles against the new `ScrubPlayer.is_playing()`. The window-shortcut event filter tracked installation with a bool, so a reparent (Maya dock/undock) left it dangling on the OLD window and the setter had no install branch for an already-visible widget — it now tracks the filtered window by identity and moves itself; the pending consume-key stores (key, modifiers) and clears on ANY KeyPress (a stale pending key ate a later unrelated press; `TestStalePendingKeyCleared`). **Stale geometry/paint:** `clear()` and `remove_track` now drop `_bg_curve_previews` (entries keyed to recycled track ids painted **another object's curve** across the wrong row) and `remove_track` rebuilds header labels with their full stored presentation + re-applies expansion (TrackData now records icon/dimmed/italic; the old plain-name rebuild dropped icons/colors and vertically desynced every row below an expanded track). The playhead badge and marker head glyphs are pinned to the viewport top with the ruler (they scrolled out from under it, and marker hit-shapes became unreachable); markers with notes widen their boundingRect to cover the label (drags left stale text pixels); `TimelineView.resizeEvent` refreshes overlay geometry (clicks in a newly exposed strip missed gap overlays until the next zoom); `_key_times` reads keys from `curve_preview` — the form real consumers supply — so next/prev-key navigation actually lands on key dots (`TestKeyTimesIncludeCurvePreview`); marquee sync emits `selectionChanged` only when something flipped (consumers ran per-curve host-app selection dozens of times per second); `_show_hidden_menu` releases its header-parented QMenu (one leaked per right-click); the splitter drag no longer disk-flushes QSettings per mouse-move; `AttributeColorDialog` copies a caller-supplied defaults dict before polluting it; `register_pattern` purges cached brushes for an overridden style (`TestRegisterPatternOverridePurge`). **Perf:** new public `SequencerWidget.bulk_updates()` context manager defers the per-add scene-rect recompute (a full rebuild was O(n²) in clip count; mayatk's `_sync_to_widget` adopts it; `TestBulkUpdates`). **DRY:** the value→pixel curve mapping (15% pad, inverted Y, flat-centering) existed in three near-copies — key dots, clip curve preview, background curves — and the background copy's flat check was dead (its range was pre-floored), painting flat curves at the row **bottom** while their key dots centered; one shared `make_value_mapper` + `build_curve_path` (segment→QPainterPath out-type switch, previously duplicated verbatim) now serve all three. The five copy-pasted shortcut-match blocks collapsed onto `SequencerWidget._match_shortcut`; the three row-metric walks (`_row_position`/`_total_row_height`/`_visual_rows`) are expressed through one `_iter_rows` generator; `add_track_label`'s icon/no-icon branches share one wiring tail (the icon path also built-and-abandoned a QLabel per call). **Dead code removed (public API — registry regenerated):** `ShotLaneItem` — never instantiated (the ruler took over shot-block rendering years ago); its `shot_block_clicked` emitter was the only one, so the widget signal + `shot_lane_double_clicked` (zero emitters) are gone too, along with `ClipItem._track_index`, `TransportControls._current_frame` (the controller's own copy is the live one), `_DEFAULT_CLIP_COLORS`, the never-set `RangeHighlightItem.locked`, and `DraggableItemMixin.DRAG_CAPTURES_UNDO` (superseded by the lazy `_undo_captured`). In its place, the ruler gained `shot_block_at(time)` and the timeline's context-menu dispatch refines the "ruler" zone to **"shot_lane"** when the click lands on a shot block — the consumer's shot context menu (Select/Edit/Trim/New) existed but was **unreachable in production** because nothing ever emitted that zone. **Verified:** full uitk suite 2430 passed / 6 skipped (0 failures) offscreen; `test_sequencer.py` 258/258 including 11 new regression classes. **Deliberately deferred:** unifying the ~90-line edge-drag scaffold duplicated between the gap and range overlays (pure interaction-code refactor; its correctness payloads — lazy undo, emit gates — shipped individually) and click-to-select on clips (intent unclear, needs a live-GUI decision).

- **2026-07-08 Fix: `ComboBox.setAsCurrent(text)` silently selected the wrong item on any combo whose items carry non-string DATA.** Its docstring promises `i` may be "the item text or index," but the string branch resolved the index via `self.items.index(i)` — and the `items` property returns each item's *data* when present, not its text. So for a combo populated from `add({name: obj})` (item text = name, item data = the object — e.g. tentacle's Blender materials list, whose data is the `bpy` material), a name string was never found, the `except ValueError` swallowed it, and it fell back to index 0. Surfaced as the report "press *Get* material and the combobox still shows the wrong material" (the Blender materials slot's Get / Assign-Random / Assign-New all call `cmb002.setAsCurrent(mat.name)`). The string branch now falls back to matching the display text when the value isn't found among the item data — so `setAsCurrent(name)` works for data-backed combos while string-data / no-data combos (item data falsy → `items` == texts) and the int-index path are unchanged. The rich/plain text match is extracted to a shared `_index_of_text` helper reused by `setCurrentText` (was a duplicated loop), since Qt's `findText` matches only the DisplayRole and misses rich-text items. `strict=True` now also raises for an out-of-range int (previously only for a not-found string), matching the documented "raise if not found" contract. Tests: `test_combobox.py::SetAsCurrentByText` (5 checks — by-name on an object-data combo, by-value on a string combo, by-index, non-strict fallback, strict raise); full `test_combobox.py` 31/31, `test_widget_combobox.py`+`test_widgets.py` 89/89 green. (Paired with the blendertk/tentacle Blender selection-context fix — see those CHANGELOGs; that fixed *which* object Get reads, this fixes the combo *showing* its material.)
- **2026-07-08 Persistence: lossless string round-trips, `SettingsManager.remove()`, QTextEdit state persistence.** Review + hardening pass over the settings/state/preset stack. (1) Strings that parse as JSON (`"1.10"`, `"123"`, `"true"`) were mangled on restore by the read-side `json.loads` (a line edit holding `1.10` came back as `1.1` the next session); `setValue`/`_coerce_for_store` now JSON-quote exactly those ambiguous strings via the new shared `encode_stored_value()` chokepoint, so all strings round-trip verbatim while plain strings stay human-readable on disk and legacy bool/number stringification still decodes. `StateManager.load`'s decode guard now keys off the store (never re-decode after a `SettingsManager`; decode raw-QSettings stores symmetrically) — the old combo-text-mode skip is superseded. (2) `SettingsManager` gained `remove(key)` (namespace-aware); `StateManager.clear()`/`clear_custom()` called `store.remove()` which the `__getattr__` SettingItem-proxy turned into a `TypeError` in MainWindow mode, and `load_custom()` no longer double-decodes through a `SettingsManager` store. (3) QTextEdit state never persisted: its no-payload `textChanged` reached `sync_widget_values` as `None` and was dropped — the relay now derives the live value before skipping — and `ValueManager`'s `textChanged` getter/setter fall back to `toPlainText()`/`setPlainText()` (plain-text setter preferred so literal `<b>x</b>` text isn't eaten by rich-text interpretation; direct `set_value` reordered to match). `apply()`'s None-guard extended to `toPlainText` widgets. `PresetManager._pending_preset_action` initialized in `__init__`. Tests: `TestSettingsManagerRemove`, `TestStringValueRoundTrip`, `TestTextWidgetStringRoundTrip`, `TestSettingsManagerBackedStore`, `TestTextChangedOnTextEdit`, `TestTextEditPersistence` + line-edit `1.10` full-chain regression. Follow-up critique pass: the read side is now the shared `decode_stored_value()` (one decoder mirroring the one encoder across `SettingsManager.value`, `StateManager.load`, and `load_custom`), and `value(key, default)` returns a missing key's default verbatim instead of JSON-decoding it (`value("k", "1.10")` no longer yields `1.1`).

- **2026-07-08 Docs: backlog pass — five DOC tasks closed, four docs flip to `current` (6 of 13 total), BRIDGE.md written, install drift fixed.** DOC-01/04/05/10/11 closed and DOC-06 advanced (ledger: `docs/DOCMAP.md`). **DOC-01** — both READMEs' Quickstart and `python -m uitk.examples.example` verified verbatim against the *published* wheel (1.2.99) in a clean venv, offscreen, with `PYTHONPATH` cleared (the workspace's editable trees otherwise shadow the wheel — and even skew `pip install`'s already-installed detection, silently skipping the install). Real drift found: `pip install uitk` alone can't run the Quickstart — `qtpy` + a Qt binding are deliberately not wheel dependencies; both Install sections now carry a synced `qt-install-note`. **DOC-10** — `BRIDGE.md` written in full from the `uitk/bridge/` sources (AttributeSpec/kind-handler registry, per-language formatters, template discovery/modes, the `BridgeSlotsBase` override surface, panel services), zero DOC-TODOs; ledger `stub` → `needs-verify`. **DOC-04 + DOC-11** — WIDGETS.md got a full claim-by-claim catalog pass (18 drift fixes — per-widget `.menu`/`.option_box` availability corrected, ComboBox/TreeWidget/TableWidget/Menu signatures matched to source, fictional APIs removed) plus new sections: sequencer, editors (including the shortcut/command registry's narrative home, per the DOC-11 decision), delegates, `WindowPanel`, `TextViewBox`, `Slider`, `ScriptOutput`; `MenuButton` pointered to MARKING_MENU.md; row → `current`. **DOC-05** — MARKING_MENU.md fully re-verified: chord-release tolerance, host-namespaced binding persistence + `_reconcile_bindings`, MenuButton type-based nav (the doc still described the long-dead `i`-button convention), corrected pin/auto-hide semantics, and the 2026-06-30 shortcut-register work (activation key via `register_command(bind=False)`, gesture-keyed route targets, `sb.editors.show("global_shortcuts")`); row → `current`. **DOC-06** — ARCHITECTURE.md gains §12 "UI loading & compilation" (loader contract, runtime vs compiled delegates, embedded-hash freshness, bundled-uic toolchain selection, `precompile_async`, `python -m uitk.compile --check`); §11's ghost `get_property_from_ui_file` flow corrected; row honestly stays `needs-verify` (§§1–10 still unverified). Code-side drift fixed en route: `_core.py::_build_loader`'s docstring claimed `"compiled"` is the default loader (it's `"runtime"`), `load_ui`'s docstring claimed compiled-only loading, and API_REFERENCE.md listed the nonexistent `get_property_from_ui_file`. Both docs sweeps exit 0.
