- **2026-07-06 Fix: `OptionBoxManager`'s wrap-retry loop could fire into an already-deleted widget.** Same bug class as the `Menu` leave-timer fix below, found while chasing its full-suite noise: `_schedule_wrap_if_needed`'s slow path (widget not yet parented) armed `QtCore.QTimer.singleShot(0 | 15, self._attempt_wrap_when_ready)` — an unowned free-function timer — to retry until a parent shows up (up to 50×). If the widget was destroyed first (e.g. constructed, then torn down before ever being placed in a layout), the retry kept firing and `widget.parent()` raised `RuntimeError: Internal C++ object (PySide6.QtWidgets.QLineEdit) already deleted`, observed live repeating across many tests during a full-suite run. `OptionBoxManager` itself isn't a `QObject` (it's a plain `ptk.LoggingMixin` helper) so it can't own the timer directly; fixed by parenting the retry timer to the wrapped **widget** instead (`_wrap_retry_timer = QtCore.QTimer(widget)`, single-shot, reused by both the 0ms and 15ms call sites via a new shared `_schedule_wrap_retry` helper) — destroyed along with the widget, so it simply stops instead of firing into deleted state. TDD-verified: new `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionBoxManagerWrapRetryTeardown::test_retry_timer_survives_widget_destruction` reproduces the exact `RuntimeError` against the pre-fix code and passes against the fix; full `test_optionBox.py` 146/146 green.
- **2026-07-06 Fix: `Menu`'s deferred leave-timer arm could fire into an already-deleted `QTimer`.** `showEvent` delayed arming the `hide_on_leave` poll timer by 200ms via a bare `QtCore.QTimer.singleShot(200, lambda: self._leave_timer.start() if self._leave_timer else None)`. That free-function form isn't owned by any `QObject`, so if the menu (and its child `_leave_timer`) was destroyed before the 200ms elapsed — e.g. a test's `tearDown` calling `deleteLater()` right after `show()` — the callback still fired later, and the `if self._leave_timer else None` guard didn't help: the Python attribute was still a non-`None` reference to a QTimer whose C++ side was already gone, so `.start()` raised `RuntimeError: Internal C++ object (PySide6.QtCore.QTimer) already deleted.` PySide's slot-exception handling routes this to `sys.excepthook` rather than failing the currently-running test, so it surfaced as console noise attributed to whatever unrelated test happened to be mid-`processEvents()` when the stale callback fired — first noticed as a spurious traceback during `test_header.py`'s `TestHeaderWindowActions` under `python -m unittest` (alphabetical method order), while chasing a one-off full-suite-only failure of `test_minimize_toggle_restores` (not reproduced again in two subsequent full runs — that one remains an unconfirmed offscreen-QPA-under-load flake, not fixed by this change; see `reference_uitk_offscreen_qpa_test_flakes` memory for the established pattern). Fix: replaced the bare `singleShot` with a real `QTimer(self)` (`_leave_start_timer`, single-shot, `timeout` connected to a new `_arm_leave_timer` guard method) — parented to the menu like `_leave_timer` already is, so it is destroyed along with it and simply never fires instead of firing into deleted state. No 3-arg `singleShot(interval, receiver, callable)` overload used (venv-only in PySide6 6.10+, absent from Maya 2025's bundled 6.5.3 — see `reference_venv_pyside6_newer_than_maya` memory). TDD-verified: new `test_menu.py::TestMenuHideOnLeave::test_deferred_leave_timer_arm_survives_menu_destruction` reproduces the exact `RuntimeError` against the pre-fix code (confirmed by temporarily reverting the fix) and passes against the fix; full `test_menu.py` 168/168 green.
- **2026-07-06 Fix: a re-instantiated MarkingMenu no longer leaves the previous instance fighting it — chord releases over MenuButtons dispatch again after a dev reload.** Live symptom (tentacle-in-Maya): after re-instantiating `TclMaya` in a long-lived session (the dev-reload workflow), holding L+R opened the chord menu but releasing over a `MenuButton` launched nothing. Root causes, confirmed by driving the real stack in fresh Maya instances (single-instance runs pass; two-instance runs reproduce): **(1)** `MarkingMenu._submenu_cache` was a class-level dict silently shared by every instance, so a new instance resolved nav targets to the OLD instance's wrappers — whose native-menu content the new instance's builds had re-wrapped (Maya's native menus are process singletons; a second wrap hollows the first) — and `show()` on a hollowed wrapper displays nothing while the release is consumed and the dispatch latch set; **(2)** the old instance's activation `GlobalShortcut` (and grabs) stayed live, so whichever instance won the event race serviced the gesture with dead caches. The offscreen suite never caught it because every test fixture bypasses `__init__` and assigns its own cache. Fix: `_submenu_cache` is rebound per instance in `__init__` (the class default remains only as a bypass-fixture fallback, documented as such); new `MarkingMenu.retire()` + a `_live_instances` WeakSet — constructing a new instance retires all previous ones (activation shortcut disposed, timers cancelled, gesture ended via `hide()`, activation callbacks inert via a `_retired` guard); the dead class-level `_instances` dict was removed. Regression tests: `test_marking_menu_instance_retirement.py` (4: per-instance cache, retire-on-construction, retired-ignores-activation, retired-cannot-rearm-activation; all fail pre-fix). Verified: full marking-menu offscreen group 135 green; live-Maya two-`TclMaya` probe — old instance retired + inert, new instance's chord release launches its target. Investigation also ruled out this cycle's WIP as the cause: the `center_widget` max-width change produces no sibling overlaps on the real chord menus, and the single-instance pipeline passes end-to-end on the current tree. Critique pass caught two follow-ons: `_install_activation_shortcut` had no `_retired` guard, so a stale `ShortcutEditor` callback (e.g. `set_activation_key`) on an already-retired instance could re-arm its `GlobalShortcut` — defeating retirement; guarded. The shortcut-dispose block was duplicated between `_install_activation_shortcut` and `retire()`; extracted to a shared `_dispose_activation_shortcut()`.
- **2026-07-06 Fix: `center_widget`'s padded resize could be truncated by a stale `maximumWidth`/`maximumHeight`.** `padding_x`/`padding_y` request a content-fit resize (`widget.minimumSizeHint()` + padding), but `QWidget.resize()` silently clamps to whatever `maximumWidth`/`maximumHeight` is already set — a Designer-authored ceiling sized for shorter text than the widget's *current* label then cut the resize back down, below the widget's own `minimumSizeHint`. Live symptom: marking-menu submenu buttons (auto-sized via `add_child_event_filter` → `center_widget(w, padding_x=...)`) carrying a stale `.ui` `maximumSize` had their label text crammed flush against the button edges instead of padded. Fixed in `switchboard/utils.py::center_widget`: when the requested size exceeds the current maximum *and* that maximum is acting as a loose ceiling (`minimumWidth < maximumWidth`), the ceiling is raised to fit before `resize()` runs; a `minimumWidth == maximumWidth` fixed-size lock (e.g. a square icon tile) is a deliberate constraint, not a stale leftover, and is left untouched even when the text would want more room. Same handling on the vertical axis. Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestSwitchboardCenterWidget` — 3 new cases (`test_padding_x_raises_stale_maximum_width`, `test_padding_x_leaves_generous_maximum_width_untouched`, `test_padding_x_does_not_widen_a_fixed_size_lock`).
- **2026-07-06 Fix: a loaded UI's widget-state settings branch is now host-namespaced, matching the existing shortcut/marking-menu scheme.** `Switchboard.add_ui` resolved a UI's `ui.settings`/`ui.state` branch as `self.settings.branch(name)` — un-namespaced by host — so a same-named panel shared by co-located mayatk and blendertk sessions (e.g. `"mirror"`) read and wrote the identical QSettings keys: one host could silently inherit the other's saved widget state (checkbox/combo/etc. values) on next load. `MainWindow._relative_state` (the not-loaded sibling fallback used to mirror a value into a sibling surface) had the same gap, and would have resolved to a different key than a loaded sibling's real branch. Fixed via a new `SwitchboardShortcutMixin._host_namespaced_branch(name)` helper (`switchboard/shortcuts.py`) — the widget-state analog of the existing `_shortcut_ns()` — consumed by both `Switchboard.add_ui` (`switchboard/_core.py`) and `MainWindow._relative_state` (`widgets/mainWindow.py`), so a loaded UI and its not-yet-loaded sibling always agree on the same branch; `_migrate_shortcuts_to_host_namespace` now also writes its legacy-key twin under the per-panel-branch head (in addition to the existing global-bucket head) so window/widget-scope overrides survive the move. `mainWindow.py` also drops a dead `from uitk import __package__` import (silently rebinding the module's own `__package__`) and two no-placeholder f-strings, found while touching the same method. Tests: `test_persistence_full_chain.py::TestHostNamespacedWidgetState` (3: separate branch per host, widget state isolated across hosts, `_relative_state` matches a loaded sibling's branch).
- **2026-07-05 Dead-code sweep — library source now pyflakes-clean (probes/re-exports noqa-marked).** Removed unused imports and dead locals across ~30 modules (widgets, mixins, switchboard, handlers, loaders, sequencer). Notable non-mechanical items: `Header.show_menu` carried a dead 10-line grid-introspection loop (computed positions/text and discarded them — leftover debug) now reduced to the single `show_as_popup` call; `mainWindow.py` imported `__package__` from `uitk`, silently rebinding the module's own `__package__` attribute (harmless today only because the module uses no relative imports); two annotation-only forward refs that pyflakes flagged as undefined names (`menu.py`'s `Optional["CollapsableGroup"]`, `preset_manager.py`'s `Optional["StateManager"]`) got proper `TYPE_CHECKING` imports; dead `row`/`index` locals in `widgetComboBox` add/insert paths and a dead `w` in `Header`'s collapse sizing were dropped (all adjacent side-effectful calls kept). Re-export surfaces (`bridge/__init__`, `recent_values`' store names) and the `external_app_handler` qtpy availability probe are now explicitly `# noqa: F401`-marked per the `_factory.py` convention instead of looking accidental; `sequencer/__init__` already followed it. Deliberately untouched: `examples/example_ui.py` (Designer-generated) and `examples/example.py`'s `QSignalBlocker` RAII local (now `noqa: F841`-marked). Verified: full-suite baseline green (2399/2402), 1054 targeted tests over every touched module pass, and the post-sweep full suite green (see the README Tests badge for the count).
- **2026-07-04 Feat: shared `ScriptOutput` console widget (`widgets/scriptOutput.py`).** Extracted from mayatk's `ScriptConsole` so every DCC shares one read-only, syntax-highlighted output view: regex `ScriptHighlighter` (comment/warning/error/result/info — now case-insensitive so it colors Maya's `Error` and Blender's `ERROR` alike), robust Ctrl+C over host shortcut interception, and an `append_text` stream API. Host-specific concerns are **injected** (`clear_callback`, `context_menu_hook`) so the widget carries no `maya.cmds`/`bpy` dependency. Registered in `DEFAULT_INCLUDE`; consumed by mayatk (workspaceControl host) and blendertk (area-shadow host). Offscreen-verified (10/10: highlighting, injected clear, menu hook, no-clear-on-hide, newline-joined copy).
- **2026-07-04 Fix: test-runner badge writer no longer re-breaks the PyPI landing's Tests link.** `test/run_tests.py::_update_readme_badge` hardcoded the badge link target as `](test/)` while writing into `docs/README.md`, so every badge refresh would have regenerated the broken link the docs sweep just fixed (`../test/` is correct from `docs/`). The target is now computed with `os.path.relpath` from the README's own location to the test dir. Same fix applied to the pythontk/mayatk/tentacle runners (each carries its own copy of this helper — a known cross-repo duplication; consolidating the runners is a separate refactor).
- **2026-07-04 Docs: intent narrative + a ledgered, machine-swept documentation framework.** Two changes to how uitk documents itself. **(1) Intent:** both front doors now say *why* the package exists, not just how it wires — a "Why uitk exists" section in `README.md` (the Qt-tax problem in DCC tool fleets, the convention-as-wiring bet, well-behaved-by-default, when it fits / when it doesn't, plus a subsystem→intent table covering Switchboard / MainWindow / widget enhancements / marking menu / handlers / bridge) and a condensed "Why" on the PyPI landing (`docs/README.md`). **(2) Framework:** the nine hand-written docs are now a *ledgered set* governed by `docs/DOCMAP.md` — one row per doc (role, status `current`/`needs-verify`/`stub`, Verified date, sources-of-truth modules), a module→doc **coverage map** over `API_INDEX.md` (longest-prefix rules; every public module must map to a doc home or be opted out with a reason), and an 11-task backlog (DOC-01…DOC-11) sized for incremental completion — each task names its target, its sources, and its done-condition, so finishing the docs is delegable low-context work. The workflow contract lives in `docs/MAINTAINING.md` (verification is claim-by-claim against the cited sources; ledger updates ship in the same edit; `DOC-TODO(task)` markers for honest gaps; `sync:` blocks for sanctioned duplication like the Quickstart shared by both READMEs). Enforced by the new generic `m3trik/scripts/check_docs.py` (stdlib-only, CI-friendly, exit 0 = clean): ledger↔disk sync, relative-link + `#anchor` integrity under GitHub slug rules, Nav-line presence, DOC-TODO census vs. status (a `current` doc may contain none; fenced examples don't count), cross-file sync-block identity, and coverage triage (an UNTRIAGED module fails the sweep — the parity-map fix-or-ledger pattern applied to docs). First sweep immediately caught real drift: a dead `COOKBOOK.md#presets` anchor in the User Guide (fixed) — and surfaced the one uncovered subsystem, `uitk/bridge/`, which got a grounded stub (`docs/BRIDGE.md`: why-it-exists + anatomy written from source; five DOC-TODOs cite the exact modules holding each answer). All 13 ledgered docs sweep clean (`check_docs.py` + `check_doc_line_refs.py` both exit 0); existing docs seeded honestly as `needs-verify` (content complete, not yet traced claim-by-claim) rather than over-attested as current.
- **2026-07-01 Feat: `AffixOption` — a first-class option-box plugin for affix mode (Auto / Suffix / Prefix picker).** Promoted the affix-mode picker — previously duplicated byte-for-byte across `mayatk` and `blendertk` `mat_utils` (plus a third divergent hand-rolled copy in blendertk's lightmap_baker) — into a first-class, DCC-agnostic uitk plugin at `widgets/optionBox/options/affix.py`. It's an inline, non-square option modeled on `ValueOption`: a compact themed `ComboBox` sitting flush beside a text field, gated by `is_compatible` to text-bearing hosts (skipped + warned otherwise). The parsing itself stays in `pythontk.StrUtils.split_affix` (the SSoT); the option only wires the picker and exposes the selection via `AffixOption.mode` / `.resolve()`. Surface: `OptionBoxManager.set_affix(...)` (the universal form — `.option_box` is autopatched onto plain `QLineEdit`), `widget.options.affix(...)` (fluent sugar, `OptionBoxMixin` widgets only), and read-back `widget.option_box.affix_mode` / `.resolve_affix(default=…)` (both fall back to `"auto"` when no picker was added, so callers need no imports). Registered in `DEFAULT_INCLUDE` (`uitk.AffixOption`), `_TYPE_TO_KEY`, and the option order (right after `value`, ahead of the icon buttons); also added the long-missing `value`/`affix` keys to the `option_order` setter's `valid_options`. This replaces the old approach of stuffing a raw `QComboBox` into `option_box.menu` under a hard-coded objectName (`cmb_affix_mode`) — read-back is now via `find_option(AffixOption)`, removing the magic-string dependency the objectName-uniqueness rule exists to prevent. New test `test/test_affix_option.py` (19 cases, all green); option-box regression suites unaffected (145 + 7 + 29 green).
- **2026-07-01 Test-suite cleanup: session-safety bug fix + scratch sweep.** `test/interactive_tests/run_interactive.py` called `MayaConnection.connect(..., force_new_instance=False)` — a direct violation of the hard "never attach to a live DCC session" rule (mayatk `CLAUDE.md`'s AI-agent hard block on this exact flag), meaning a run of this manual script could silently execute code inside — and clobber — whatever real Maya session happened to already be open. Fixed to `force_new_instance=True`, restoring `connect()`'s own safe default; grepped the whole `test/` tree and confirmed it was the only such usage. Swept `test/temp_tests/` (40 stale diag/repro/profile/bench-json scratch files) and `test/logs/` (11 stale debug logs) — both gitignored, so purely disk hygiene, no git history affected. Verified the three `test/bench/*.py` benchmark harnesses and the `test_marking_menu*`/`test_switchboard*` file splits are legitimate (each targets a distinct concern; not accidental duplication). Full suite re-verified green: **2359 passed, 3 skipped, 0 failed/errors** (up from a stale 1817-passed badge). Left two pre-existing Qt `DeprecationWarning` categories untouched and out of scope: (1) 34 call sites across `test_sequencer.py`/`test_tree_selection.py` use a deprecated 5-arg `QMouseEvent` constructor overload — the fix requires a per-call-site `globalPos` computed from the right widget, not a mechanical batch edit, and risks destabilizing carefully-tuned marquee/tree-selection coordinate assertions; (2) `test_shortcut_commands.py`'s two `QApplication.setActiveWindow(...)` calls (including forcing a `None` active window) have no drop-in replacement that preserves synchronous, deterministic control over `activeWindow()` — the non-deprecated `widget.activateWindow()` is async and can't express "no active window" at all. `test_optionBox.py`'s camelCase filename was also left as-is: it mirrors the production package's own camelCase directory (`uitk/widgets/optionBox/`), a repo-wide naming inconsistency spanning dozens of files — out of scope for a test-suite pass.

- **2026-07-01 Fix: uitk CI no longer depends on an unpublished downstream (mayatk) symbol.** `test/test_color_swatch.py` reached *down* into `mayatk.display_utils.color_id` (`ColorId.DEFAULT_SWATCH_COLORS`, `ColorUtils.get_color_difference`) — mayatk symbols, tested from uitk. That inverts the dependency chain: uitk publishes **before** mayatk, and CI installs the last *published* mayatk, so when this cycle's mayatk refactor **renamed** `color_manager` → `color_id` the uitk suite broke (`ModuleNotFoundError: mayatk.display_utils.color_id`) and blocked the whole release cascade — a hazard that recurs whenever uitk tests a mayatk symbol added/renamed in the same cascade. `TestGetColorDifference` was a pure duplicate of mayatk's existing `test_display_extras.py::TestColorUtilsStaticHelpers`; `TestDefaultSwatchColors` (the palette assertions) was unique and moved to mayatk (where `color_id` lives). `test_color_swatch.py` now tests only the palette-agnostic `ColorSwatch` widget — **16 passed** offscreen. The widget itself never imported mayatk (callers pass colors in); other uitk tests that import *stable* mayatk symbols are unaffected. CI comment updated to state the rule: a uitk test must not import a mayatk symbol renamed/added in the current cascade.
- **2026-06-30 Fix: the Shortcut Editor (and any `WindowPanel`) now remembers a user-adjusted window size across sessions.** The editor windows extend `WindowPanel` — a plain `QWidget`, not `MainWindow` — so they never had `MainWindow`'s geometry persistence: a hand-resized editor reopened at the constructor default (`600×600` for the shortcut editor) every session, and its first-show `_fit_to_content` re-fitted it regardless. `WindowPanel` gains **opt-in geometry persistence** mirroring `MainWindow`'s proven contract — `persist_geometry(settings, key)` wires an injected `SettingsManager`, the size/position are debounced-saved on resize/move and saved on hide/close, restored on first show, and a *restored* size is authoritative so `_fit_to_content` is skipped (re-fitting a hand-resized window is exactly what discarded the size). The base stays DCC-agnostic: with no settings injected (the default) persistence is off and the window fits to content as before. `ShortcutEditor` opts in via its own `sb.settings.branch("shortcut_editor")`, keyed **per launch variant** (`window_geometry.main` vs `window_geometry.commands`) so the full editor and the focused ⌘ Commands panel — which share that branch — don't clobber each other's size. New public methods on `WindowPanel`: `persist_geometry`, `save_window_geometry`, `restore_window_geometry`, `clear_saved_geometry` (+ `resizeEvent`/`moveEvent`/`hideEvent`/`closeEvent` overrides). Tests: `test_shortcut_editor.py::TestShortcutEditorGeometryPersistence` (opt-in wiring + focus-keyed key; size persists across sessions; restored size is authoritative over fit; focus variants keep separate sizes; first show with nothing saved still fits) — shortcut-editor **51**, the WindowPanel-consuming editor suites + shortcut-commands **257**, mainwindow **94** + resize **19**, all passed offscreen. API registry regenerated. Deliberately **not** unified with `MainWindow`'s parallel geometry persistence: that lives on a stable, heavily-tested DCC-tool-window path and its restore has idiosyncratic `adjustSize`/logging fallbacks, so a byte-preserving mixin would need several override hooks — a separate refactor warranting its own live-DCC pass. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the real size-grip drag persisting (offscreen QPA can't drag a physical grip, though the save/restore path is deterministic and unit-covered).
- **2026-06-30 Feat: marking-menu bindings surface in the unified Shortcut Editor (external-binding register).** `Switchboard.register_command` gained `bind=` / `on_rebind=` / `value_getter=`: a command can now be listed + edited in the shortcut editor while its real key is owned **externally** — no register-created `QShortcut` (so no duplicate/ambiguous binding), the live value read via `value_getter`, edits (and resets) routed to `on_rebind` instead of command settings. `MarkingMenu` uses it to register its **activation key** (`marking_menu_show` — visible/editable; edits route through the new `MarkingMenu.set_activation_key`, which rewrites every chord's `Key_*` prefix **and** re-installs the activation `GlobalShortcut`) and its four chord→menu **routes** (hidden, read-only — edited via the host's Menu Bindings combos). New gesture-keyed `MarkingMenu.get_route_target` / `set_route_target` (activation-key-agnostic) + `start_menu_names`. New focused launch `sb.editors.show("global_shortcuts")` — the `ShortcutEditor` pinned to the ⌘ Commands view with its UI combo **stripped to the single locked Commands entry** (kept visible, not hidden, so its show-all option-box overlay isn't orphaned) and its **Scope / Description / UI columns dropped** (just Action + Shortcut + Reset); marking-menu route rows name the **target menu** they open (e.g. "Marking Menu: Cameras") in the Action column rather than the mouse button. Also: a command's Scope cell now renders the consistent, non-interactive **application-scoped badge in every state** (bound or unbound, editable or not — `is_command` wins in `_set_scope_cell`) instead of a grey "assign first" icon when unbound. Verified under Maya's bundled PySide6 6.5.3 (mayapy): the register extension, the focused editor (show + strip), and `set_activation_key`'s GlobalShortcut re-install (a stale `key_show` had left the shortcut on the old key — fixed + regression-tested). Tests: `TestExternalBinding`, `test_marking_menu_shortcuts.py` (incl. `TestActivationShortcut`), focused-editor build/strip; offscreen suite green.
- **2026-06-30 Fix: option-box-wrapped fields no longer sit short of their layout cell.** Two issues left some wrapped LineEdits not reaching the cell edge. (1) `OptionBoxContainer` replaced the wrapped widget in its parent layout but kept the default **Preferred** horizontal size policy — so an **Expanding** field (like a `QLineEdit`) became a container that parks at content width instead of stretching (and an Expanding `QTextEdit` stopped filling vertically). `wrap()` now mirrors the wrapped widget's size policy onto the container in **both** axes. (2) `_update_sizing` (which the wrapped-widget `Resize` eventFilter now calls on every height change) ended by `adjustSize()`-ing the container — fine for an absolute overlay, but for a **layout-managed** container it fights the parent layout and snaps it back to content width. `_adjust_to_content` is now a no-op for layout-managed containers (the parent owns geometry); only the self-positioned marking-menu overlay is refit + re-centered. Tests: new `TestOptionBoxLayoutSeating` (container inherits Expanding policy; `_update_sizing` leaves a managed container's width alone); overlay-refit + 500+ option-box/editor/sequencer tests green offscreen.

- **2026-06-30 `ColorSwatch` gains an opt-in `keep_square` aspect lock.** A new `keep_square` property (default `False`, so existing `setFixedSize` callers — style_editor, color_mapping_editor — are untouched) pins the swatch's height to its current width on every `resizeEvent`, so a swatch in a stretch-to-fill grid stays square as its column grows (Qt's `QGridLayout` ignores `heightForWidth`, so this tracks the width directly instead). Settable via kwargs through `set_attributes` (`ColorSwatch(keep_square=True)`). Consumed by mayatk/blendertk's Color ID palette. Tests: `test_color_swatch.py` `TestColorSwatchKeepSquare` (off-by-default, square-in-grid at 200/300px, kwargs path) — **52 passed** offscreen (with style_editor).
- **2026-06-30 Filter matching is now strict — bare terms match exactly; wildcards must be explicit.** `FilterOption.to_patterns` no longer silently wraps a bare `term` into `*term*`. That auto-wrapping made a plain term *broader* than an explicit wildcard pattern — so `!exclude` dropped everything *containing* "exclude" while an explicit `!*endswith` only matched a suffix, an inversion that defeats the point of wildcards. Now every term goes to `fnmatch` verbatim: `char` matches exactly, `*char*` is a substring, `char*` starts-with, `*char` ends-with, and `!*temp*` excludes anything containing "temp". The `!` marker is still stripped and the remainder kept verbatim (a bare `!` is dropped). Consumer tooltips/placeholders updated to teach "exact unless you add wildcards." Tests: `test_filter_option.py` to_patterns/patterns cases rewritten for verbatim output; `test_switchboard_browser.py` / `test_shortcut_editor.py` haystack searches updated to explicit `*…*` (new `test_search_bare_term_is_exact` pins it). Suites **356 passed** offscreen. By design, searching a concatenated name+tags haystack now needs `*term*` for a partial match — honest, predictable wildcards.
- **2026-06-30 Switchboard browser: the separate Exclude row is removed — one search field now covers include + exclude via inline `!`.** Now that filter fields support `!term` inline exclusion (see the prior entry), the browser's second filter LineEdit (`_exclude` / `le_exclude`) and all its logic are gone: the `_exclude`/`_exclude_filter` widgets, `set_exclude_scope`, the dedicated exclude branch in `_row_passes_filter`, and the `exclude.*` settings/preset keys. The single search field (`anim, !test`) keeps anim rows while dropping any matching test, with the same scope cycle applied to both. Preset I/O drops the `exclude` section; a legacy preset that still carries one is tolerated and ignored on import (no migration — the old exclude filter is simply not reapplied). Search placeholder/tooltip updated to advertise `!`. Tests: the old `ExcludeFilter` class is rewritten as `InlineExclude` (substring/glob/combined exclusion via `!`), the filter-toggle and preset-round-trip tests dropped their exclude halves, and a new `test_import_preset_data_tolerates_legacy_exclude_section` covers back-compat — `test_switchboard_browser.py` **83 passed** offscreen. The shortcut editor (the other `set_filter` consumer) already exposes `!` from the prior change; a sweep found no other UI filter fields on the FilterOption API. Note: the DCC reference-manager / macro-manager / channels / workspace-map filters have their own bespoke controller-side matching (not the `filter_list`/`FilterOption` path) and would each need a predicate rework + Maya/Blender verification to gain `!`, so they're intentionally left for a separate DCC-tested pass.

- **2026-06-30 Shortcut-editor Scope/Reset cells became centered, colour-coded *icons* (delegate-painted) instead of cell-widget buttons — fixing the "icon columns are wider than the buttons" misalignment at the source — plus eye-catching assign/conflict feedback and an option-box height-tracking fix.** The Scope toggle and Reset button were `QPushButton`s placed via `setCellWidget`; the themed `QTableWidget::item { padding: 2px 5px }` offsets *any* cell widget (the button landed at +5px and clipped), so the square cells read wider than their content. Rather than zero the table's item padding (which strips the text columns' breathing room) or merge the columns, both cells now render as **centered item icons** drawn by a new reusable delegate, `uitk.widgets.delegates.centered_icon.CenteredIconActionDelegate` — the icon is painted at the cell centre, so cell padding can't offset it, and the cell background stays transparent (matches the table) with a per-state colour/tint. The centering primitive `paint_centered_icon` (and the tint helper `fill_cell_background`) are shared with `table_actions._CenteredIconDelegate` (DRY); the delegate subclasses `RowSelectionBorderDelegate` so the row-selection outline stays continuous across the action cells. The delegate paints the item's `BackgroundRole` tint with an explicit `fillRect` via `fill_cell_background` (the stylesheet style's `CE_ItemViewItem` otherwise drops the item brush for the QSS `::item` rules — the green "modified" / blue command-badge tints would silently vanish); a monorepo sweep then applied the same helper to `table_actions._CenteredIconDelegate`, **fixing the same latent tint-drop in the `TableWidget.actions` `background` state** — a documented feature that never rendered under the QSS style. No current consumer sets a `background` state (the mayatk/blendertk reference managers + channels use `color`/`icon` only, verified by grep), so there's no visible change to existing DCC tables; the fix makes the documented feature correct for future use and keeps the two delegates on one shared implementation. The delegate also dims a disabled cell's icon via an optional `ICON_OPACITY_ROLE` (`paint_centered_icon(opacity=…)`), the delegate-painted equivalent of Qt greying a disabled button's icon — together restoring the colour-coding + disabled states the buttons had (a first pass lost them: the tint brush was style-dropped and the muted-grey disabled icon read identical to the themed-grey enabled one). State lives on the item (`_SCOPE_ROLE` = current scope, `_ACTION_ROLE` = click descriptor / `None` for an inert badge); clicks dispatch through the table's `cellClicked` → `_on_action_cell_clicked` (Scope flips Window/Application, Reset restores the default), and new accessors `ShortcutEditor.scope_at(row)` / `scope_interactive(row)` read the cell back. The muted/disabled, owner-fixed, decorator-only, and command-"App badge" states all carry over (a command's badge is now a tinted item background + coloured icon). **Two more editor fixes:** (a) a refused or duplicate assignment is no longer silent — declining the conflict dialog now footers an amber `'<seq>' is already assigned to … — left unchanged` (+ console `logger.warning`), re-pressing a row's own key footers an info note, and a successful assign footers a green confirmation **after** the repopulate (it was previously set *before* `populate()` overwrote it, so it never painted; also fixed a latent dangling-item read by capturing the label first). (b) Option-box buttons now track a wrapped widget's height: `OptionBoxContainer` re-squares its option buttons on a height-changing `Resize` of the wrapped widget (via a back-ref to its `OptionBox`), so a later `setFixedHeight` on a wrapped combo (e.g. the preset row) resizes its icon buttons too. Tests: migrated the scope/reset cell-widget assertions to the new accessors across `test_shortcut_editor.py` / `test_shortcut_commands.py` / `test_shortcuts.py`, added `test_action_cell_click_dispatch`; shortcut + table + optionBox suites **176 + 22 + 169 passed** offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the real-pointer click/hover on the icon cells (offscreen QPA can't move a physical pointer).
- **2026-06-30 Shortcut-editor column presentation tidied: blank headers on the icon-only columns, and the focused (manager) view hides the now-redundant Scope column.** The Scope and Reset columns are a square toggle / undo button — their text titles ("Scope" / "Reset") only crowded the narrow fixed columns, so `_COLUMN_LABELS` blanks them (icons + per-control tooltips carry the meaning). And when `ShortcutManager.show_editor()` renders a standalone manager through the unified `ShortcutEditor`, every binding's scope is owner-fixed (`scope_editable=False`), so the Scope column's toggles would all be inert — `show_editor` now hides COL_SCOPE alongside the already-hidden Description column (via the existing `set_columns_hidden` API; the real-Switchboard editor still shows Scope). The two icon-only columns are also now sized to a single `ROW_HEIGHT` constant (row height == column width == the square icon button, built at that same size) so each cell is a perfect square with the button filling it edge-to-edge — no more 24 px columns around a 22 px row. Tests: `test_shortcuts.py` gains `test_manager_view_hides_scope_column`, the header-order test updated for the blank titles, and the columns round-trip test retargeted to a default-visible column — shortcut suites **52 + 118 passed** offscreen. No API change.
- **2026-06-30 The editor preset row's "Preset:" label folded into the combo itself as a display-only prefix.** The shared `EditorPanel.init_preset_row` template paired the preset `ComboBox` with a separate `QLabel("Preset:")`; it now sets the combo's existing `current_text_prefix = "Preset:  "` instead (the feature already shipped — it's what the shortcut editor's "Target UI:" combo uses). The prefix paints only on the collapsed current selection, never on the dropdown items or `itemText` (so load/rename/delete still see the raw name), and composes with the existing `current_text_suffix` dirty marker → a modified preset reads `Preset:  name *`; an empty selection shows the placeholder unprefixed. One fewer widget per row, and every editor (shortcut, style, color-mapping, switchboard browser) gets the label consistently. No API change. Editor + combobox suites **92 passed** offscreen.
- **2026-06-30 The two confusingly-named shortcut-editor modules became a `uitk.widgets.editors.shortcut_editor` subpackage, and the bespoke `ShortcutManager` dialog was retired onto the unified editor.** They were near-siblings editing *different* backends: the Switchboard global shortcut **registry** (preset-aware, collision-checking) vs. a `ShortcutManager`'s plain `shortcuts` dict (used live by the Maya shot sequencer). Now `widgets/editors/shortcut_editor.py` → `widgets/editors/shortcut_editor/registry_editor.py` (`ShortcutEditor`, `CollisionConflict`), and the old `shortcut_manager_editor.py` `ShortcutEditorDialog`/`KeyCaptureDialog` are **removed** — replaced by `widgets/editors/shortcut_editor/manager_facade.py` (`ManagerSwitchboardFacade`), a thin adapter that lets a standalone `ShortcutManager` render through the *same* `ShortcutEditor` (so it gets filtering, hidden/editable handling, and collision checks instead of a parallel dialog). The subpackage `__init__` re-exports the public surface and documents the split. In-repo references (editors registry, `ShortcutManager.show_editor`, `row_selection` docstring, mayatk's `hotkey_collisions` `CollisionConflict` import, tests) point at the new paths; the editor-registry name `editors.show("shortcut")` is unchanged. No back-compat shims left behind. Persisted settings branches (`shortcut_editor`, `shortcut_manager_editor`) and class names are unchanged. uitk shortcut suites **162 passed** offscreen; API registry regenerated.
- **2026-06-30 A persisted command shortcut (e.g. "Repeat Last Command") now self-heals when its host namespace settles — fixes "the repeat-last hotkey works once, then is dead next session."** Proven from a field registry dump: the user's assigned key lived correctly under the host-namespaced `shortcuts_maya.Commands.repeat_last_command = M`, yet the live session had **zero** `M` `QShortcut`s — a stale legacy `shortcuts.Commands.repeat_last_command = Ctrl+Shift+R` (un-suffixed, from a pre-namespacing default) was bound instead. **Root cause:** `register_command` eagerly binds during `Switchboard.__init__`; if `context_tags` is still empty at that instant *and* a host window is already visible, the eager bind resolves the **un-suffixed** key (`_shortcut_ns()` → `shortcuts.`) and latches the stale `Ctrl+Shift+R`. `_bind_pending_commands` (wired to `on_ui_loaded` and the `current_ui` setter) only ever bound *missing* commands, so once `context_tags` later settled to the host namespace the stale binding was **never reconciled** and the user's real key never bound. **Fix:** `_bind_pending_commands` now also rebinds a command whose **live binding (key *or* scope) no longer matches what the settings currently resolve to** — the binding self-corrects on the first UI load (or current-UI change) regardless of how the drift arose (late `context_tags`, an external settings edit, an in-process module reload). Scope is compared alongside the key because a binding can drift in scope alone (legacy namespace window-scoped, host namespace application-scoped), and a stale `WindowShortcut` owned by an always-visible host is inert exactly when the app-scoped binding should fire. Still a cheap no-op once the live binding matches, so the per-`on_ui_loaded` cost is unchanged. Tests: `test_shortcut_commands.py::TestCommandNamespaceSelfHeal` — `test_stale_binding_rebinds_when_namespace_settles` (seed the exact field split → eager-bind under empty tags latches `Ctrl+Shift+R` → flip tags to `maya` → the bind pass must rebind to `M`; fail-before/pass-after) and `test_unchanged_binding_is_not_rebound` (a correct binding keeps the *same* `QShortcut` across passes — no churn). uitk shortcut suites **132 passed** offscreen. No public API change (private binder reconcile only). **Live Maya confirmation:** the fix only runs once the corrected module is loaded — a running session must be restarted (or uitk reimported) to pick it up.
- **2026-06-30 `repeat_last_command` ships UNBOUND again, + the Shortcut Editor gains an "Assigned" view.** Two Shortcut-Editor changes — the first **supersedes the two "ships bound to `Ctrl+Shift+R`" entries below** (that default never released): **(1)** the built-in `repeat_last_command` no longer ships with a default key. Like `reopen_last_ui` it ships **unbound**; the user assigns a key in the editor — no surprise default binding. The Maya repeat-last fix is unaffected — it was the *consolidation* onto the single command binding path that killed the ambiguous per-slot `QShortcut` stack, not the default key. tentacle's one-shot legacy migration adapts automatically: a user carrying the old `Ctrl+Shift+R` (or any custom key) keeps it as an explicit override (no working shortcut is yanked), while a never-customized user starts unbound. **(2)** A new **"★ Assigned"** combobox view lists only actions that currently have a shortcut, across every UI + command — the quick "what have I bound?" filter, a sibling of the "⌘ Commands" pseudo-UI. Both special views now sort to the **top** of the combobox and are **accent-coloured** (not just icon-prefixed) to set them apart from the UI names; the editor still *opens* on a concrete UI, not a filtered view. - **2026-06-30 The stateless HTML pipeline moved out of the `widgets/` root into a `RichTextFormatter` class, and the rich-text mixins were DRY'd up.** `widgets/_html_style.py` (a flat module of six functions + three module-level dicts, out of place in the widgets root) is **removed**; its logic is now the `RichTextFormatter` class in `widgets/mixins/text.py` — the rich-text *domain* module that already hosts the `RichText`/`TextOverlay` mixins. The six functions become class methods (`format` ← `format_rich_text`, `resolve_background`, `apply_inline_styles`, `apply_prefix_styles`, `wrap_font_color`, `wrap_font_size`) and the palette/vocabulary become **overridable class attributes** (`LOG_COLORS`, `PREFIX_SEVERITY`, `INLINE_STYLES`, `DEFAULT_BACKGROUND_RGB`) resolved at call time, so a subclass can retheme without touching the transforms — it's now the single overridable SSoT for uitk's styled-tag vocabulary across MessageBox / TextViewBox / Footer / console logs. **Not folded into the `RichText` mixin** deliberately: the consumers don't inherit it and a stateless formatter ≠ a stateful widget mixin. Behaviour is byte-for-byte identical — verified by an old-vs-new parity battery over the full input matrix (constants, every transform, `resolve_background` domain, and the `align`×`font_color`×`font_size` `format` product) **before** the old module was deleted. **DRY cleanup in the same module:** (1) the `RichText` mixin's docstring duplicated the formatter's HTML examples — trimmed to a pointer at the `RichTextFormatter` SSoT; (2) `RichText._createRichTextLabel` and `TextOverlay.textOverlayLabel` hand-rolled the *same* translucent, click-through rich-text-QLabel-in-a-zero-margin-QHBoxLayout scaffold — extracted to one module-level `_make_translucent_label(parent)` helper. Consumers updated in lockstep: `messageBox`/`textViewBox` (`format_rich_text`→`RichTextFormatter.format`, `resolve_background`→`RichTextFormatter.resolve_background`) and `footer` (folded into its existing `mixins.text` import; `LOG_COLORS`→`RichTextFormatter.LOG_COLORS`). No downstream importers existed (mayatk only referenced the old module in comments). Tests: new `test_rich_text_formatter.py` (resolve-background domain + clamping, inline/prefix token substitution, the full `format` pipeline, and a subclass-palette-override case) — formatter + widgets + footer suites **134 passed** offscreen; public surface resolves `from uitk import RichTextFormatter`. API registry regenerated — Removed module `widgets/_html_style` (`format_rich_text`, `resolve_background`, `apply_inline_styles`, `apply_prefix_styles`, `wrap_font_color`, `wrap_font_size`); Added `RichTextFormatter`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the rich-text overlay scaffold extraction (offscreen QPA can't verify the composite render of `RichText`/`TextOverlay` widgets, though the construction logic is deterministic and unit-covered).
- **2026-06-30 "Hotkey"→"shortcut" unified as the package-wide term for uitk's *own* key-bindings; "hotkey" is reserved for DCC-native bindings.** The global key-binding editor is renamed **`HotkeyEditor`→`ShortcutEditor`** (module `widgets/editors/hotkey_editor.py`→`shortcut_editor.py`, history-preserving `git mv`); the Switchboard editor-registry key + accessor `editors.hotkey`→`editors.shortcut` (`sb.editors.show("shortcut")`); the in-cell capture helper `install_hotkey_capture`→`install_shortcut_capture` (+ `HotkeyCaptureEdit`/`HotkeyCaptureDelegate`/`BorderedHotkeyCaptureDelegate`→`Shortcut…`); the sequencer's `ShortcutManager` editor moved to `editors/shortcut_manager_editor.py` to free the `shortcut_editor` name. Window title "Hotkey Editor"→"Shortcut Editor" — which also disambiguates it from Maya's *own* native Hotkey Editor. **Dead code removed:** the unused `ShortcutMixin` + `apply_standard_shortcuts`/`create_standard_shortcuts_config` (zero consumers monorepo-wide). **Saved data migrated:** the preset domain `hotkey_presets`→`shortcut_presets` (new intra-root `_maybe_migrate_renamed_domain`, reusing `_merge_move` — never clobbers a post-rename edit) and the editor's `hotkey_editor` settings branch→`shortcut_editor` (one-shot copy on first construct). "hotkey" is deliberately KEPT where it denotes a DCC's *native* bindings (mayatk's `cmds.hotkey`/hotkey-set collision checker + Macro Manager Maya hotkeys; Blender keymap macros) — conflating those with uitk shortcuts would mislead. The two `shortcuts.py` modules stay (widget-layer primitives vs. Switchboard glue — a deliberate layer split, not duplication; merging would invert the dependency). Cascaded downstream: mayatk (collision-checker + macro-manager imports) and tentacle (settings `b021` "Shortcut Editor", `add_post_build_hook("shortcut")`, `.ui`+`_ui.py`). Tests: preset-migration (+2 new), editor-registry, capture, editor, and command suites green; a pre-existing order-masked command-store leak in `test_shortcut_commands.py` fixed (hermetic `_command_settings().clear()` in the fixture). API registry regenerated — Removed: `HotkeyEditor`, `ShortcutMixin`, `apply_standard_shortcuts`, `create_standard_shortcuts_config`; Added: `ShortcutEditor`.
- **2026-06-30 The three item-view delegates grouped into a `widgets/delegates/` subpackage (de-suffixed), matching the `mixins/`/`editors/` category-subpackage convention.** `RowSelectionBorderDelegate` (the row-spanning selection-border base) and the two in-cell capture delegates that build on it — `ShortcutCaptureDelegate` / `install_shortcut_capture` (key-chord capture) and `ChoiceCaptureDelegate` / `install_choice_capture` (dropdown capture) — were three flat sibling modules in `widgets/`; they are now one cohesive package. The `RowSelectionBorderDelegate` symbol name is unchanged, so facade consumers are unaffected. Pure reorganization — no behaviour change. Tests: delegate + switchboard-browser suites **100 passed** offscreen; facade resolves all seven symbols through the new paths; API registry regenerated.
- **2026-06-30 Hotkey manager consolidated onto one binding path — repeat-last now fires in Maya, and slot/command hotkeys persist per host.** Two fixes to the global-hotkey system, both proven in a fresh GUI Maya (`MayaConnection`, `force_new_instance=True`). **(1) repeat-last fired nothing:** the built-in `repeat_last_command` shipped *unbound*, so out of the box repeat-last relied on tentacle's legacy per-slot QShortcut (see tentacle CHANGELOG) which stacked one app-scoped `Ctrl+Shift+R` shortcut **per loaded UI** → Qt declared an ambiguous overload and fired none (live: 5 UIs → 5 identical shortcuts). It now ships bound to `Ctrl+Shift+R`, binding **once** to an always-visible host (live: 5→1, App-scoped on `MayaWindow`, and it fires); `reopen_last_ui` stays unbound. **(2) host-namespaced persistence:** slot + command overrides were keyed `shortcuts.*` under a shared QSettings `(org, app)`, so Maya and Blender silently shared/collided on one set. The prefix is now host-namespaced via `context_tags` (`shortcuts_maya.` / `shortcuts_blender.` / plain `shortcuts.` standalone) — one helper `_shortcut_ns()` feeds the write path, the registry/read path, and the deferred-bind scan; a one-shot per-host migration copies legacy un-suffixed overrides into the host namespace so customizations survive. The host suffix itself is the new shared `host_namespace_suffix()` (`uitk.widgets.mixins.shortcuts`), used by BOTH `_shortcut_ns()` and `MarkingMenu._binding_store_key` so the two binding systems can't drift on a host's identity (drift is the documented Maya/Blender desync cause). New diagnostic `find_duplicate_application_shortcuts()` (same module) flags the ambiguous-overload state — the guard against recurrence. Tests: `test_hotkey_commands.py` (+10: registry default, single-binding, host-namespacing isolation/migration, duplicate-guard) — uitk hotkey **125** + settings/switchboard/marking sweeps **217** passed offscreen; live Maya re-probe shows `_shortcut_ns()=shortcuts_maya.`, repeat-last fires, zero duplicate app shortcuts. Public API: added `find_duplicate_application_shortcuts` + `host_namespace_suffix`; `repeat_last_command` default changed (no signature change).
- **2026-06-30 Filter line-edit reborn as a first-class `FilterOption` option-box plugin + a widget-compatibility gate.** The standalone `widgets/editors/_filter_lineedit.py` factory (`make_filter_lineedit` / `to_patterns`) is **removed**; the "filter field" pattern is now an all-in-one plugin, `optionBox/options/filter.FilterOption`, added fluently via `widget.option_box.set_filter(...)` (or `widget.options.filter(...)`). One option owns the filter on/off toggle (it *is* a `BinaryToggleOption` leaf sibling of `ToggleOption`/`DisableOption`), the field's text persistence, a `patterns()` accessor (`None` when off/empty), and an optional N-state scope cycle — replacing the loose `_filter_toggle` / `_scope_action` / `_text_settings_key` attrs that used to be stashed on the widget. `to_patterns` moves to the same module (single source of the comma/glob query convention). Persistence is routed through the caller's `settings` object so text, on/off, and scope share **one** store (presets see a single namespace). New general hook `BaseOption.is_compatible(widget)` (default `True`; `FilterOption` requires text `text`/`setText`/`textChanged`): `OptionBoxManager.add_option` now **skips incompatible pairings with a warning** — "plugins only seen by compatible widgets". Consumers migrated: `switchboard_browser` (search + exclude rows, scope, preset I/O) and `hotkey_editor` (action filter) now build a plain `LineEdit` and call `set_filter`, reading state via `find_option(FilterOption)`. Tests: new `test_filter_option.py` (patterns/gating/scope/persistence + the compatibility skip); `test_switchboard_browser.py` / shortcut-editor filter cases migrated to the new accessors; optionBox + editor suites green offscreen.
- **2026-06-30 Filter fields gain inline `!term` exclusion.** Building on pythontk's new `filter_list(negate_prefix=…)` (see pythontk CHANGELOG 2026-06-30), a single filter field can now carve out exclusions inline: type `anim, !test` to keep `anim` rows while dropping any matching `test`. `FilterOption.to_patterns` preserves a leading `!` and wraps only the remainder (`!drop` → `!*drop*`, not `*!drop*`; a bare `!` is dropped), exported as `NEGATE_PREFIX`; the switchboard browser's search field and the shortcut editor's action filter pass `negate_prefix=NEGATE_PREFIX` to `filter_list` and advertise the syntax in their tooltips. Especially useful for single-field filters with no separate exclude row. Tests: `test_filter_option.py` (+5 to_patterns negation + an end-to-end patterns→filter_list case).
- **2026-06-30 Fix: option-box overlay drifted off-center when re-squared on a post-wrap height change.** The container's `_update_sizing` ended with a plain `container.adjustSize()`, which keeps the top-left and shifts the center as the box narrows. Now that a wrapped widget's `Resize` re-squares the option buttons through that path, an absolute-positioned (marking-menu) overlay drifted left. Centralized the center-preserving adjust into `OptionBoxContainer._adjust_to_content` (layout-managed → plain adjust; self-positioned → restore center) and routed both the show-time refit and `_update_sizing` through it. Regression caught by `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionBoxOverlayRefit` (143 optionBox tests green).

- **2026-06-30 `repeat_last_command` ships bound to `Ctrl+Shift+R` by default — the consolidation that fixes "repeat-last does nothing in Maya".** The built-in nav command shipped *unbound*, so out of the box repeat-last relied entirely on tentacle's legacy per-slot `QShortcut` path (see tentacle CHANGELOG) — which created one application-scoped `Ctrl+Shift+R` shortcut **per slot instance**, so with several UIs loaded Qt saw a stack of identical enabled app shortcuts, declared the activation ambiguous, and fired none. Giving the command a sensible default binds it **once** to an always-visible host (the existing command path, already proven reliable), so the action works with no user setup. Proven live in a fresh Maya 2025 (`MayaConnection`, `force_new_instance=True`): with 5 UIs loaded the live `Ctrl+Shift+R` count drops **5→1** (App-scoped, owned by `MayaWindow`, enabled) and the command **fires** on activation. `reopen_last_ui` stays unbound (no conventional default key). Tests: `test_hotkey_commands.py::TestCommandRegistry::test_builtin_nav_commands_registered` + `::TestCommandBinding::test_repeat_last_ships_bound_single_shortcut` (fail-before/pass-after); uitk hotkey suites **107 passed** offscreen. No public API signature change — a default-value change on a built-in command.

- **2026-06-29 The global commands (Reopen Last UI / Repeat Last Command) now actually *fire* across sessions — the real cause was a `GlobalShortcut` press-latch, not persistence or binding.** Prior rounds chased persistence (the override value) and startup *binding* timing; both were already correct. Proven live in a fresh Maya 2025 (`MayaConnection`, `force_new_instance=True`): the value persists to the registry and a fresh-session Switchboard **does** bind the command at `__init__` against the always-visible `MayaWindow` — yet the command still went dead. Root cause: commands (and the cold-start slot standins) were bound through `_make_host_shortcut`, which always created a **`GlobalShortcut`**. `GlobalShortcut.pressed` only re-emits after its application-level event filter sees a matching `KeyRelease` reset an internal `_is_down` latch — but in a DCC host that release is **routinely missed** (the native viewport has focus, or focus shifts while the action runs), so the latch sticks `True` and *every press after the first is silently swallowed*: the command fires once, then is dead for the session. Regular slot hotkeys were unaffected because `register_slots_shortcuts` binds a **plain `QShortcut`** (`robust=False`) that fires on every press with no latch. **Fix:** `_make_host_shortcut` now creates a plain `QShortcut` (`activated`, `setAutoRepeat(False)` to keep the prior one-fire-per-press feel) instead of a `GlobalShortcut`. Commands and slot standins are fire-on-press and never used `released`, so the entire release-detection machinery was pure liability for them — and they now behave identically to the slot hotkeys that already work reliably (the standins already only wired `pressed`, so this is behaviour-equivalent for them, minus the latch). The vestigial `"robust": True` on the command carrier's `_shortcut_meta` (never read by the binder) was removed. `GlobalShortcut` itself is unchanged — the marking menu still uses it for genuine hold-and-release. **Verified live in Maya against the exact failure mode:** the bound command is a plain `QShortcut` owned by `MayaWindow` at App scope, fires on 3/3 clean key clicks, and — the regression proof — still fires after a *missed* `KeyRelease` (a lone `KeyPress` then more clicks: the old `GlobalShortcut` swallowed them, the `QShortcut` does not). Test: `test_hotkey_commands.py::TestCommandBinding::test_command_uses_plain_qshortcut_not_latching_global_shortcut` (the bound command is a plain `QShortcut`, not a `GlobalShortcut`, App-scoped, and activates — fail-before/pass-after); the two existing command tests that reached into `GlobalShortcut._shortcut` were updated to the `QShortcut` directly. hotkey-commands / hotkeys / switchboard-history / marking-menu suites **106 passed** offscreen. No public API changed (private binder internals only).
- **2026-06-29 Editor option widgets no longer wedge a `hide_on_leave` menu open — the real cause of "Merge's option menu never hides, Separate's always does".** Field report: in the Maya tentacle *Polygons* module the *Merge* option menu never hid on mouse-leave while *Separate* always did, despite identical construction. Root cause, isolated by diffing the two (`slots/maya/polygons.py`): *Merge* adds a `QDoubleSpinBox` option; *Separate* adds only checkboxes. A spin box / line edit defaults to a focus policy with Tab/activation focus, so it **auto-grabs keyboard focus the instant the menu shows and activates** — even though the user never touched it. `Menu._text_edit_in_progress` (the guard that suppresses `hide_on_leave` during an in-progress edit, added for the preset inline-rename overwrite bug) then read True forever, so the menu never hid. Confirmed headlessly: a menu with a `QDoubleSpinBox` reports `focus=QDoubleSpinBox, text_edit_in_progress=True` and stays visible after the pointer leaves; a checkbox-only menu hides. This is the per-menu, init-determined cause behind every "some option menus won't hide" report (any menu containing a spin/text widget). Fix: `Menu._demote_editor_autofocus` (run in `showEvent`, before the window activates) demotes editor *items* (`get_items()` of `_EDIT_FOCUS_TYPES`) in a `hide_on_leave` menu from Tab/activation focus to `ClickFocus`. That drops only the *passive* auto-focus — click-to-edit and explicit `setFocus` still work, so deliberate editing (and the preset rename, whose inline editor isn't a menu item and is explicitly focused) stays protected. Verified: Merge-shaped menu now hides; clicking *into* the spin box still suppresses hide while editing. Tests: `test_menu.py::TestMenuHideOnLeave::test_editor_item_demoted_so_menu_hides_on_leave` and `test_actively_focused_editor_still_blocks_hide_on_leave`. menu/optionBox **310** + marking/mainwindow/combobox/events/widgets **323** passed offscreen.
- **2026-06-29 `hide_on_leave` menus opened-but-never-entered no longer linger forever (complementary robustness).** Found while chasing the editor-focus cause above, but a distinct issue: an option menu opens anchored to the button the user clicked, so the cursor sits on the *button*, not the menu *body*. `Menu.showEvent` sets `_mouse_has_entered=False` when the menu doesn't open under the cursor, and `_check_cursor_position` *hard-gated* hiding on `if self._mouse_has_entered:` — so a menu the cursor never crossed never armed and **stayed open forever even with the pointer far outside** (repro: never-entered menu, cursor far the whole time, still visible after 600ms). Fix: replace the hard guard with a **dual-threshold grace** in `_check_cursor_position` — consecutive out-of-family samples now always accumulate, and the menu hides once they exceed `leave_grace_samples` (entered: a deliberate leave, default 1 ≈ immediate) or the longer `unentered_grace_samples` (never entered: default 15 ≈ 1.5s — time to reach a menu that popped up away from the cursor, after which an ignored menu auto-dismisses instead of lingering). Preserves "don't yank a menu before the user can reach it" while guaranteeing `hide_on_leave` always eventually fires when unpinned. Pinned / actively-edited / child-popup-open menus are unaffected (they short-circuit before the grace). New public tunable `Menu.unentered_grace_samples`. Test: `test_menu.py::TestMenuHideOnLeave::test_unentered_menu_auto_dismisses_after_grace` (stays up before the grace, dismisses after — fail-before/pass-after). menu/optionBox/marking-menu/mainwindow/combobox suites **631 passed** offscreen. **Live confirmation still warranted** for the exact dwell time feeling right in a real DCC session (offscreen can't move a physical pointer).
- **2026-06-29 Menu hover robustness — `hide_on_leave` menus now stay open while you use their child popups, and close them together.** Unpinned option-box menus dismissed the moment the cursor moved onto a popup opened from within them (an option-menu dropdown, a pinned-value context menu), and could leave that popup orphaned when they did close. Root cause: `_check_cursor_position` decided "is the pointer still in my work area?" from this window's rect plus a QObject-subtree walk (`_widget_in_subtree`) — but every option-box child popup is parented to the *wrapped widget*, a **sibling** of the menu, so it falls outside that subtree. Headless repro confirmed the gap: a ComboBox dropdown (lives inside the menu) reads as in-family, but an option-menu dropdown / value popup (parented to the wrapped widget) reads as outside, so the leave-poll hid the menu. Three uncoordinated dismissal mechanisms had grown around this (the menu's `_DismissOnAncestorMove`, each popup's own `_install_visibility_filters`, and a `pin_values` band-aid that toggled `hide_on_leave` off/on around its context menu). New **transient popup family** primitive on `Menu`, ownership-based rather than parenting-based: `adopt_transient(child)` registers a child popup (held weakly, pruned lazily — a child that dies can't wedge the menu open), `_pointer_in_family()` generalizes the rect+subtree test to "over this menu **or any adopted child** (window geometry or subtree, recursively, cycle-guarded)", a `leave_grace_samples` debounce (default 1 = legacy immediate hide; auto-raised to 3 on first adoption) bridges the gap the cursor crosses between menu and child, and `hideEvent` now **cascades** the hide to adopted children so closing the menu can't orphan a popup. `nearest_enclosing(widget)` lets a spawn site adopt into the right host. Wired at the spawn sites: `OptionMenuOption._show_menu` adopts its dropdown into the enclosing menu (no-op when the button sits in a bare container, so a standalone dropdown still self-manages); `PinValuesOption._show_context_menu` adopts its context menu (the band-aid is gone). Public API: `Menu.adopt_transient`, `Menu.nearest_enclosing`, `Menu.leave_grace_samples`. Tests: `test_menu.py::TestMenuTransientFamily` (sibling popup is outside the family until adopted; adoption keeps the menu open on leave-to-child; adoption raises the grace; grace requires sustained leave; hide cascades to children; a destroyed child is pruned without crashing; idempotent/bad-input; `nearest_enclosing`), `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionMenuAdoptedByHost` (dropdown adopted by its host menu; standalone dropdown has no host) — all fail-before/pass-after. menu / optionBox / dismiss-on-move / events suites **383 passed** offscreen. The common path is unchanged: with no adopted child a menu's `_pointer_in_family` reduces to the prior rect-or-subtree test and (grace 1) hides on the first outside sample. New opt-in live diagnostic `UITK_MENU_LEAVE_DEBUG=1` (set via `Maya.env`, read once at import) logs every leave-poll tick's gate (`hol`/`pinned`/`entered`/`timer`/`self_rect`/`in_family`/`widgetAt`) to pin down a real-platform "won't hide" symptom that doesn't reproduce offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted**: real cursor traversal from an option-box menu onto its dropdown/context-menu and back (offscreen QPA can't move a physical pointer, so the gap-crossing grace and family hit are exercised only via mocked `widgetAt`/`QCursor.pos`).
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey system follow-up — the global commands (Reopen Last UI / Repeat Last Command) now persist across sessions.** The override *value* always persisted and re-read fine; the bug was **startup binding timing**. A command is bound on `on_ui_loaded`, which fires while the just-loaded UI is still *hidden* (the caller shows it afterward), and at next-session startup nothing is the active window — so `_command_host()` (which fell back to `app.activeWindow()`) returned `None`, `_bind_command` bailed, and the persisted command silently never bound. When a tool was later shown no fresh `on_ui_loaded` fired, so it stayed dead (regular slot hotkeys were unaffected — they bind when their tool is actually *opened* and thus visible). Two fixes: **(1)** `_command_host()` now falls back to an always-visible *application* host via `resolve_application_host(None)` — the DCC main window (`MayaWindow`/`3dsMaxWindow`), else any visible non-transient top-level — instead of `activeWindow()`, so in a DCC the command binds at the first `on_ui_loaded` even before any uitk tool is opened (the fallback is guarded so it never owns a command by a transient `startmenu`/`submenu` surface). **(2)** the `current_ui` setter now retries the deferred binds (`_bind_pending_commands` + `_bind_deferred_slot_shortcuts`) — a window becoming current means it's on screen, a reliable second bind chance for a standalone host that shows its main window only *after* the `on_ui_loaded` that would otherwise be the command's one shot; both calls are cheap no-ops once everything is bound. This also makes the cold-start slot standins (next entry) bind on the same broadened trigger. Tests: `test_hotkey_commands.py::TestCommandBinding` — `test_command_host_falls_back_to_visible_dcc_window`, `test_persisted_command_binds_at_startup_via_dcc_host` (binds with only a DCC host up and `activeWindow()` nulled — fail-before/pass-after), `test_deferred_command_binds_when_a_ui_becomes_current` (fail-before/pass-after). commands / hotkeys / history / switchboard / marking-menu / ui-handler suites **265 passed** offscreen (the `current_ui` retry runs in every navigation path with no regression). **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted**: assign a hotkey to a global command, restart, confirm it fires without opening any tool first.
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey system follow-up — app-scoped slot hotkeys now fire from a *cold* session, and "Reopen Last UI" reopens a closed window.** Two field bugs remaining after the earlier round. **(1) An app-scoped slot hotkey was dead next session until the tool was opened.** The earlier fix made `register_slots_shortcuts` re-create the binding *when the UI builds* — but tool UIs are lazy, so on a fresh session (tool never opened) the shortcut was never created though the editor still listed it as assigned. New cold-start **standins**: at the first `on_ui_loaded` with a visible host, the switchboard scans persisted *application*-scoped slot overrides straight from settings (`_ui_names_with_shortcut_overrides` — one settings scan, so the per-UI `get_static_shortcut_registry` XML read is only paid for UIs the user actually customised; no UI is built) and owns a host-window `GlobalShortcut` per binding (`_deferred_slot_shortcuts[(ui_name, method)]`) that **builds-then-invokes** the slot on press — firing the action without popping the tool open. The standin is disposed the instant its real UI builds (`register_slots_shortcuts` → `_dispose_deferred_slot_shortcuts(ui)`), handing the key to the real UI-context shortcut so the two never collide (a duplicate app-scoped `QShortcut` on one key makes Qt's activation ambiguous → neither fires). Window-scoped overrides get no standin — they only fire while their window is focused, which already requires it open. The host-owned `GlobalShortcut` creation shared by the command binder and this path is unified into `_make_host_shortcut`. **(2) "Reopen Last UI" worked once, then did nothing after the window was closed.** `show_prev_ui` skipped `_current_ui`; but showing a window gives it focus, so the reopened window *becomes* `_current_ui`, and once the user closed it the "skip current" rule made it unreopenable. The gate is now **visibility, not currency**: it shows the most-recent non-transient UI that isn't already on screen — so a just-closed (hidden) window is the reopen target, and repeated presses step back through hidden windows instead of re-showing the one in view. **Pre-existing limitation noted, not changed:** a slot whose signature requires a *signal-payload* positional (a list slot's `item`, a combo's `index`) still can't be driven by a bare hotkey trigger — `_adapt_shortcut_callback` only injects `widget` — so both the normal and deferred paths raise `TypeError` on such a slot; binding hotkeys to action slots (`(self)` / `(self, widget)`) is the supported shape. Tests: `test_hotkeys.py::TestDeferredAppScopedSlotShortcuts` (settings-key parsing; standin created only for app-scoped + bound + unbuilt; built-UI skipped; `register_slots_shortcuts` disposes standins for the built UI; the build-then-invoke callback injects `widget=None`), `test_switchboard_history.py::TestSwitchboardNavigation` (`show_prev_ui` skips visible + transient, reopens a closed current window, None when the only UI is already visible — fail-before/pass-after). switchboard / marking-menu / hotkey / mainwindow suites **379 passed** offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted**: a cold-session app-scoped slot hotkey firing its action without the tool open, and the reopen-after-close cycle (offscreen QPA can't exercise real key activation).
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey system — three field bugs in the newly-added editor/command/repeat flow.** All three surfaced from live use of the recent navigation-command + hotkey-editor work. **(1) `repeat_last` dropped the slot's signal payload.** `repeat_last()` re-invoked the captured `SlotWrapper` *bare* (`wrapper()`), so any slot taking a required positional from its signal — a list slot's clicked `item`, a combo's index — raised `TypeError: …list000() missing 1 required positional argument: 'item'`. The wrapper now snapshots the exact args/kwargs it last ran with (in `SlotWrapper._invoke`, guarded by `_suppress_slot_capture` so a replay can't re-capture) and `repeat_last` replays them through `_invoke` (wait-cursor + timeout still apply; debounce bypassed so a repeat fires immediately). **(2) An editor-assigned hotkey on an *undecorated* slot was dead next session until reassigned.** `register_slots_shortcuts` (which re-creates a UI's shortcuts every build) bailed at `if not default_sequence: continue` for any slot lacking a `@Shortcut` default — *before* reading the persisted user override — so a hotkey bound via the editor to a plain widget slot (the common case) was silently dropped on the next session's rebuild. The override (sequence + scope) is now read first; only a slot with neither a default nor an override is skipped. **(3) The global commands ("Repeat Last Command" / "Reopen Last UI") never fired.** A command is (re)bound the moment the user assigns a key in the hotkey editor, at which point `app.activeWindow()` *is* that editor — an ephemeral tool window. `_command_host()` returned it, so the application-scoped `GlobalShortcut` was owned by the editor and went inert the instant it closed (Qt disables an application shortcut whose owner window is hidden — the same gate `resolve_application_host` documents). `_command_host()` now prefers a persistent, visible `loaded_ui` window — skipping the editor (not a registered Switchboard UI) and the marking menu's transient `startmenu`/`submenu` surfaces (visible only mid-gesture, so they'd make the command inert again on release, the same skip `show_prev_ui` applies) — and only falls back to `activeWindow()` when no eligible UI is shown; `resolve_application_host` still upgrades to a DCC host window when present. Tests: `test_switchboard_history.py::TestSwitchboardNavigation` (repeat replays a required positional; dead-widget replay fails soft), `test_hotkeys.py::TestUndecoratedSlotHotkeyPersistence` (persisted override re-created on rebuild; unbound slot still skipped — both fail-before/pass-after), `test_hotkey_commands.py::TestCommandBinding` (`test_command_owner_is_persistent_ui_not_active_window` — owner is not the transient editor, survives its close, and the binding still fires; `test_command_host_skips_transient_marking_menu_surface` — a visible startmenu/submenu surface is never chosen — both fail-before/pass-after). hotkeys / hotkey-commands / hotkey-editor / switchboard-history suites **117 passed** offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for actual key firing of a bound command and the next-session re-bind of an app-scoped slot hotkey (offscreen QPA can't exercise activation).
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey Editor: command scope cell now reads as an active "App" badge, not a dead toggle.** A command (the `⌘ Commands` rows) has no window of its own, so its scope is fixed at Application — the scope toggle was `setEnabled(False)`, which looked broken once a key was assigned (greyed-off control next to a live shortcut). It's now rendered by `HotkeyEditor._make_fixed_scope_badge`: still disabled (truly non-interactive — the scope can't change) but painted in its *on* state — a coloured pill with a crisp icon (the normal pixmap is reused for the disabled icon mode so Qt doesn't dim it). Per the rule "disabled is confusing unless it's disabled in the on state." Unbound rows keep the greyed "assign a shortcut first" state. Test: `test_command_scope_shows_active_badge_after_assign`.
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey Editor: cap the Shortcut column and add per-row tooltips.** The Shortcut column was `Stretch`, so on a wide window it ballooned to absorb the slack while showing a short centered sequence — wasteful. It's now `Fixed`, sized via font metrics to the longest realistically-bound chord (`Ctrl+Shift+Alt+Backspace` + padding) by `HotkeyEditor._size_shortcut_column`, re-measured on `showEvent` so the *themed* font (applied via QSS after `__init__`) is measured, not the default app font (the repo's "measure before polish" gotcha); the Description column (still `Stretch`) absorbs the freed space, keeping Reset pinned to the right edge. To keep the full context reachable now that both the Shortcut and Description cells can elide, each row's Shortcut and Description cells carry a composed rich-text hover card built by `HotkeyEditor._binding_tooltip` — bold action name, muted description, then the bound key set off on its own line, colour-coded + monospaced (or an italic "Unassigned"), inputs HTML-escaped. The Action cell keeps its `"Method: …"` tooltip (handlers and a test parse it). Also added `test_scope_toggle_enabled_after_interactive_assign` pinning that an in-cell key assignment re-enables that row's scope toggle (the delegate→`_apply_shortcut`→`populate` rebuild). Tests: `test_hotkey_editor.py` green (43 passed).

- **2026-06-28 Filter/enable toggles now actually disable their field, and the red icon tracks the disabled state (follow-up to the `DisableOption`/`GatingMixin` entry below).** The first pass added the *primitive* but left the in-the-wild toggles unchanged, so the behaviour still looked wrong: a filter toggle turned "off" greyed its **icon** red while leaving the **field** fully enabled (red-while-usable — backwards), and the Hotkey Editor's "show all" asterisk went red while the combo was *enabled*. **Fixes:** (1) `set_toggle` / `ToggleOption` now forward `gate_wrapped` + `keep_enabled_when_wrapped_disabled` (previously only the option class took `gate_wrapped`; the fluent manager helper silently dropped it), so a filter toggle can grey out its own field. (2) The shared filter field (`_filter_lineedit.make_filter_lineedit`, used by the Hotkey Editor and Switchboard browser) and both reference managers (mayatk + blendertk `txt001`) pass `gate_wrapped=True` — toggling the filter off now disables the field (query preserved, not cleared) while the toggle button stays clickable to re-enable, so red == disabled field everywhere. (3) The Hotkey Editor "show all" asterisk's `is_on` was inverted to mean *"filtering by the selected UI"* (combo enabled), so its red/off state now coincides with the disabled combo (show-all) instead of the usable one. (4) `GatingMixin` gained an `active_color` override (threaded through `BinaryToggleOption`/`ToggleOption`/`DisableOption` + `set_toggle`/`set_disable`) so **both** state colours are centralized-yet-overridable (the disabled tint already was; the icon already was). Channels' filter uses a *menu*-based enable/disable (not an option-box toggle button), so it's untouched. Tests: `test_optionBox.py::TestToggleOption::test_active_color_override_used_when_on`; `test_hotkey_editor.py::test_filter_toggle_off_disables_field_but_keeps_button_live`; existing show-all/filter suites still green (optionBox+hotkey-editor+switchboard-browser **264 passed**). uitk API registry refreshed (`set_toggle`/`set_disable` signatures). **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the reference-manager filter field greying + the red-icon contrast on the disabled field.
- **2026-06-28 Universal option-box *disable* button (`DisableOption` / `widget.options.disable()`) + a shared `GatingMixin`; fixes a toggle that disabled its own combo trapping itself.** Field symptom (Hotkey Editor): the Target-UI combobox's "show all UIs" toggle disabled `cmb_ui` (`setEnabled(False)`), but the option-box container's `_sync_option_buttons_enabled` **cascade-disables every option button** whose widget lacks the `keepEnabledWhenWrappedDisabled` property — and `ToggleOption` never set it, so the toggle disabled *itself* and couldn't be clicked to re-enable (the in-code comment claiming the sibling toggle "stays usable" was wrong). The "disable a widget but keep my button live" behaviour already existed **once, ad-hoc**, inside `ResetOption`'s bypass (keep-live property + gate the wrapped widget + swap icon to the error tint + emit `toggled`); `ToggleOption` re-implemented the icon swap and signal but lacked the keep-live flag and any way to gate its own wrapped widget. **Centralised into `GatingMixin`** (`optionBox/options/_options.py`): `_install_keep_enabled()` (sets the keep-live property — the one line that fixes the trap), `_apply_gating(active)` over an `_effective_gated()` set (explicit `gated_widgets` plus the wrapped widget when `gate_wrapped=True`), and `_apply_icon_state(...)` (the theme-vs-`disabled_color` `IconManager.swap_icon` dance). **`ToggleOption` consumes the mixin** and gains `gate_wrapped=False` + `keep_enabled_when_wrapped_disabled=True` (default True — strictly a fix; the only in-the-wild `ToggleOption` was the trapped asterisk). **New `DisableOption`** (`optionBox/options/disable.py`) — the universal "disable this widget" primitive: "on" = enabled, clicking disables the wrapped widget (default `gate_wrapped=True`) while the `ban`-glyph button stays live to re-enable; tints to the project error colour when off; emits `toggled(bool)`. Reuses the existing `icons/ban.svg` (circle+slash) — no new asset. Fluent `widget.options.disable()` / `option_box.set_disable()` / `add_disable()`; the Hotkey Editor's asterisk toggle now passes `keep_enabled_when_wrapped_disabled=True` explicitly (comment corrected). **Design note — siblings, not subclass:** `ToggleOption` and `DisableOption` are *siblings* under a shared `BinaryToggleOption` base, deliberately **not** one subclassing the other. Making `DisableOption` a subclass of the `_TYPE_TO_KEY`-keyed `ToggleOption` tripped a CPython `ABCMeta` cache pathology: `isinstance()` against a class that *has subclasses* runs the C-level `__subclasses__()` recursion, which cross-contaminated the abc caches of these `QObject`/`ABCMeta` options and made `issubclass(DisableOption, ToggleOption)` intermittently return **False** for a true subclass (reproduced: `BinaryToggleOption in mro` True yet `issubclass` False, DisableOption wrongly in the negative cache). Keying `_TYPE_TO_KEY` off the two **leaf** classes (neither has subclasses) sidesteps it entirely.
