Tests: `test_optionBox.py` — fail-before/pass-after regression that a `ToggleOption` whose wrapped widget is disabled keeps its button enabled; `gate_wrapped` disables the wrapped widget while the button stays live; a `TestDisableOption` suite (ban icon, gate + keep-live, initial-off starts disabled, `toggled` emits, tooltip/icon-state swap, extra gated widgets, sibling-not-subclass via MRO, `set_toggle(replace=True)` leaves a `DisableOption` intact). optionBox/hotkey-editor/menu/hotkeys/mainwindow-menus suites **380 passed** offscreen. New public symbols (`DisableOption`, `OptionBoxManager.set_disable`/`add_disable`) registered in `API_INDEX.md`/`API_CHANGES.md`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the disabled-tint icon contrast and the keep-live button rendering on a disabled host (offscreen QPA can't verify the visual).
- **2026-06-28 UI-less, hotkey-bindable *commands* — register an action in code (e.g. the Switchboard's own `show_prev_ui`/`repeat_last`) and it appears in the Hotkey Editor with a colour-coded "no UI" tag, bindable like any slot shortcut.** Closes the gap that the hotkey editor was strictly UI-driven: its bindable list came only from registered `.ui` files (a method shows up if its name matches a widget *or* it carries `@Shortcut("…")`), so a Switchboard verb with no owning UI/widget/slots-class had nowhere to live, and the `@Shortcut` path couldn't even list an *unbound* action (it required a non-empty default sequence). **New Switchboard command registry** (`SwitchboardShortcutMixin`): `register_command(name, callback, *, label, sequence="", scope="application", doc)` / `unregister_command` / `get_command_registry()` / `set_command_shortcut(name, seq, scope)` — the UI-less twins of the per-UI shortcut machinery. Overrides persist under the Switchboard's own settings (`shortcuts.Commands.*`, the same key shape a UI uses, rooted at `self.settings` instead of a per-UI branch); a command ships **unbound** by default yet still lists (the registry path, not the decorator path). `get_command_registry` reuses `_build_shortcut_entries` verbatim (each command wraps as a carrier exposing synthetic `_shortcut_meta`), so default/override/scope/doc resolution is identical to slots. **Live binding** owns a `GlobalShortcut` by the always-visible application host (`resolve_application_host`, the same hidden-owner fix slots use) and is deferred to the first `on_ui_loaded` when no window exists yet, so registration order is free; `set_command_shortcut` recreates the shortcut on rebind and an empty sequence disposes it (stays listed, just unbound). The Switchboard auto-registers two built-ins — **Reopen Last UI** (`show_prev_ui`) and **Repeat Last Command** (`repeat_last`) — for every host; host packages add their own. **Hotkey Editor** surfaces them via an appended **"⌘ Commands"** pseudo-UI in the Target-UI combo (appended, not prepended, so a real UI stays the default view) and in the 'show all' view; command rows store a `_COMMAND_UI` sentinel on the Action item (in place of a UI name) so the in-cell capture, reset, and collision paths route through `set_command_shortcut` instead of `get_ui`/`set_user_shortcut`, and the UI column renders a colour-coded `⌘ global` tag. The scope toggle is **disabled** on command rows — a UI-less command has no window of its own, so window scope would bind it to an arbitrary host window (and die if that window closes); commands are always application-scoped. Commands join the internal collision scan (an app-scoped command collides with everything on its key, offered the same Clear-&-assign path) and preset export/import (captured under the sentinel key, always — no build needed — so the dirty marker and snapshots cover command bindings too). Tests: `test_hotkey_commands.py` (registry list/label/persist/clear/unregister; live bind when a host exists, dispose on clear, deferred bind on `on_ui_loaded`; editor pseudo-UI appended, sentinel+tag rows, edit/reset routing, show-all inclusion, export/import round-trip, command-vs-command collision) + the command scope toggle stays disabled even when bound; an updated `test_hotkey_editor.py::test_combobox_lists_all_registered_uis` (expects the appended Commands entry). Full uitk suite **2182 passed, 4 skipped** offscreen. New public symbols (`Switchboard.register_command`/`unregister_command`/`get_command_registry`/`set_command_shortcut`) registered in `API_INDEX.md`/`API_CHANGES.md`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for actual key firing of a bound command (a `GlobalShortcut` owned by the host window — the offscreen QPA can't exercise the activation) and the colour tag's contrast under a real DCC stylesheet.
- **2026-06-28 Marking-menu fade now also reaches option-box menus hosted on a startmenu/submenu surface.** Follow-up to the orphaned-menu fade fix below. Field symptom: an option-box ⋯-menu launched from a *standalone* window fades on `key_show`, but the same menu launched from a marking-menu **submenu** stays opaque. Root cause: an option-box `Menu` registers (via `owner_window()`) to the MainWindow that hosts its button — a submenu surface, tagged `submenu` — and `_dim_targets` skipped *the whole window* (`win is self or win.has_tags(_MARKING_MENU_TAGS): continue`), so the surface's child menus were skipped along with the surface itself. That skip is only meant to keep the radial **surface window** bright (it's the active gesture surface); a popup hosted on it is never part of the gesture. Fix: the surface-tag check now gates only the window's *own* dim, and a window's open menus are yielded regardless of its tags — so a surface-hosted option menu backgrounds exactly like a standalone-hosted one. (`self` is still skipped whole, and a menu opened *during* the hold still stays bright via the once-per-hold snapshot.) Test: `test_mainwindow_menus.py::TestMarkingMenuDim::test_dims_option_menu_hosted_on_a_surface_window` (fail-before/pass-after — an option menu on a `submenu`-tagged window fades to 0.15 while the surface window stays at 1.0); `test_skips_transient_windows` was narrowed to `test_transient_surface_window_itself_is_not_dimmed` (asserts just the window-skip). Marking-menu + menu-tracking suites **133 passed** offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** (offscreen can't verify the composite): an option-box menu opened from a submenu dims on `key_show` like one opened from a standalone panel.
- **2026-06-28 Marking-menu fade now reaches the *orphaned* menus of hidden parent windows.** Follow-up to the fade pass added below (same day, point (4) of the entry that follows). Field symptom: the dim-on-`key_show` correctly fades a window and its open child menus, but if the parent `MainWindow` is **hidden** while one of its menus stays open, that menu stays fully opaque during the hold. Orphaned menus are intentional — you can dismiss a full panel and keep a small floating tool menu — so the menu legitimately outlives its parent's visibility (a `Menu` is a separate top-level `Qt.Tool` window and doesn't inherit the window's composited opacity). **Root cause:** `dim_other_windows` discovered menus *transitively through* `sb.visible_windows`, so the moment a parent hid it dropped out of the iteration and its still-open menu was never reached. Nothing was wrong with the tracking — the discovery *scope* was. **Fix:** discovery now spans `sb.loaded_ui` (every loaded window, visible or not) via a new `_dim_targets` generator that yields a window only when it `isVisible()` (a hidden window needs no dim) but yields its open menus regardless — reaching the orphaned menus while never wasting a fade on a hidden window. Menus are pulled by the registration-time association (`win.menus(visible=True)` — the `WeakSet` the menu joined on show), **not** by re-resolving a reparented menu's owner (a shown menu has usually reparented to a Tool window, severing the live parent chain, so `owner_window()` at dim time is the fragile path). The `["startmenu","submenu"]` skip literal — previously repeated at ~17 sites across the file — is hoisted to a single **module-level** `_MARKING_MENU_TAGS` constant (module-scoped, not a class attr, so the methods that read it stay callable when borrowed onto the lightweight test doubles, and because the tag convention is shared with the switchboard core — `_core`/`ui_handler` — rather than being MarkingMenu-specific), and the now-unneeded `hasattr(win, "menus")` guard is dropped (`loaded_ui` only ever holds `MainWindow`s, which always expose `menus()`). A switchboard-level menu *registry* was deliberately **not** added: it would duplicate `MainWindow._menus` (two sources of truth) only to reach menus the design intentionally leaves untracked (`run_modal` on a bare widget, no MainWindow owner); a derived `sb.visible_menus` is the right shape if a future consumer (a dashboard, a "close all menus" action) needs the global handle. Test: `test_mainwindow_menus.py::TestMarkingMenuDim::test_dims_orphaned_menu_of_hidden_parent` (fail-before/pass-after — a hidden parent's visible menu fades to 0.15 while the hidden window itself is left at 1.0 and out of the restore set); the fake `Switchboard` now mirrors both `loaded_ui` and the derived `visible_windows`. Marking-menu + menu-tracking suites **132 passed** offscreen. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted**: offscreen QPA can't verify the composite — warrants a live check that a tool menu left open over a hidden panel dims in lockstep on `key_show` and restores on release.
- **2026-06-28 Switchboard navigation API (`show_prev_ui`/`repeat_last` + a shared `History` primitive) and `MainWindow` child-menu tracking that lets the marking menu fade open menus with their windows.** Two related additions. **(1) `switchboard/history.py::History`** — one ordered/capped/de-duplicating/filtering primitive now backs both `Switchboard.ui_history` and `slot_history`, which were previously two hand-rolled lists with *divergent* capping (UI capped at the write site with a hard-coded 200; slots capped at the read site via `length`) and a latent leak: the UI list held **strong** refs in the `current_ui` setter, pinning up to 200 closed windows alive and defeating the weakref design of `loaded_ui`. `History(weak=True)` holds the UI history weakly (dead UIs pruned lazily on read); de-dup is by item identity (most-recent-wins, order preserved) and the `key` mapper drives only `inc`/`exc` filtering — both `ui_history()`/`slot_history()` public signatures and read contracts (incl. the `int→[]` out-of-range quirk and `slot_history`'s `add`/`remove`/`length`) are byte-for-byte preserved (the `length` setter trims immediately, as before). **(2) Navigation verbs** — `Switchboard.show_prev_ui()` re-shows the most-recent UI that is neither the current one nor a transient `startmenu`/`submenu` overlay; `repeat_last()` re-invokes the last slot **with its widget context** (the bare `prev_slot` method loses the widget most slots read), captured as the live `SlotWrapper` in `_invoke` (separate from `slot_history`, which keeps bare methods so `prev_slot` consumers like the HUD's `.__doc__` label are unchanged) and guarded by `_suppress_slot_capture` so a repeat bound as a slot can't capture itself. **(3) `MainWindow.register_menu()`/`menus(visible=/pinned=/persistent=)`** — a `WeakSet` of child `Menu`s that have shown themselves (registered from `Menu.showEvent` via the reparent-robust `owner_window()`), with a tri-state status filter; never triggers lazy menu creation (only already-shown menus are tracked), so reading them can't re-introduce the deferred-popup flash. **(4) Marking-menu fade** — `dim_other_windows` now fades each backgrounded window **and its open menus** (`win.menus(visible=True)`); menus are separate top-level Tool windows, so they don't inherit the window's composited opacity and were staying bright. The dim is a **once-per-hold snapshot** (new `_dim_snapshot_taken` guard — a QShortcut auto-repeats, and a re-run would re-snapshot and dim windows/menus opened *during* the hold, which are the current operation and must stay bright), the per-target fade is unified into `_set_dimmed` (guarded against a member destroyed mid-hold — the prior `restore_other_windows` had no such guard, latent until short-lived menus joined the set), and restore clears the flag so the next hold can snapshot again. Pin status is deliberately **not** a fade criterion. Tests: `test_switchboard_history.py` (History cap/immediate-trim/dedup/filter/oob/weak-prune/remove; ui_history weak store; `show_prev_ui` skips current+transient; `repeat_last` re-invokes with widget + capture stays stable + no-op; `prev_slot` still bare method; slot_history dedup/length/filter regression), `test_mainwindow_menus.py` (register/idempotent/visible+pinned+persistent filters/WeakSet-prune/lazy-creation-invariant; a real `Menu` self-registers on show; dim fades window+visible-menus, skips transient windows, once-per-hold snapshot exempts mid-hold menus, restore resets + survives a deleted member). Both new verbs fail soft (return `None`) when their target's C++ object was torn down since capture (DCC teardown / module reload) rather than crash a hotkey/command handler. Full uitk suite **2163 passed, 4 skipped** offscreen. New public symbols (`History`, `show_prev_ui`, `repeat_last`, `MainWindow.register_menu`/`menus`) registered in `API_INDEX.md`/`API_CHANGES.md`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the visual fade (offscreen QPA can't verify the composite) and that an option-box menu open over a backgrounded panel dims in lockstep on `key_show`.
- **2026-06-28 Hotkey editor — display-only "Target UI:" combo prefix, a disable-able filter field, and a "show all UIs" view that lists every UI's slots without building them.** Four related additions. **(1) `ComboBox.current_text_prefix`** — the left-side twin of the existing `current_text_suffix`: a prefix painted only on the *collapsed* current selection (via the style's `drawControl`), never on the dropdown items or `itemText`/data. The composition is now unified into one testable `AlignedComboBox.format_current_display_text`. The hotkey editor's Target-UI combobox carries `"Target UI:  "` as this prefix, replacing the separate `QLabel` + `fontMetrics` width math (the combo is now the uitk `ComboBox`, not a bare `QComboBox`). **(2) Shared filter LineEdit** — extracted `make_filter_lineedit` + `to_patterns` into `widgets/editors/_filter_lineedit.py` (DRY: the Switchboard browser's `_build_filter_lineedit` now delegates to it, its private `_to_patterns` removed), and the editor gains a filter field whose option-box carries a filter on/off toggle (silence the query without clearing it). Matches hide table rows in place (no rebuild) and the footer shows `showing X of N`. Bug fixed along the way: the editor's empty/load-failure `populate` branches now reset the footer via a new `_set_status`, so a stale filter count can't linger after switching to a UI with no shortcuts. **(3) Static (no-build) shortcut registry** — `SwitchboardShortcutMixin.get_static_shortcut_registry(ui_name)` resolves the slots class + widget objectNames from the registry and the `.ui` XML on disk (never a live tree) and reads overrides from the same `self.settings.branch(name)` a loaded UI uses, so a UI's slots can be listed without instantiating it. `get_shortcut_registry` was refactored to share its entry-builder (`_build_shortcut_entries`) with this path (single source of truth for entry shape + default/override resolution; live output byte-for-byte unchanged). Fidelity note: slots bound to widgets created in code (not in the `.ui`) appear only once that UI is loaded. **(4) "Show all UIs" toggle** — an option-box toggle on the Target-UI combo lists every registered UI's slots at once (loaded UIs live, unloaded UIs static — never force-building the whole set, the host-shutdown crash), reveals a 6th "UI" column, and disables the combobox (its toggle stays usable — sibling, not child). Rows now carry their UI on the Action item, so the in-cell edit / scope toggle / reset / collision check all key on the row's UI and lazily instantiate it via `get_ui` only when that row is edited — fixing a latent bug where `_apply_shortcut`/`_collect_conflicts` read the combobox instead of the row. Tests: `test_combobox.py` (`current_text_prefix` display-only + base-class fallback), `test_hotkeys.py::TestStaticShortcutRegistry` (static matches live methods/defaults, reads persisted overrides via the right branch, never instantiates), `test_hotkey_editor.py` (filter hide/toggle/footer/stale-count, all-view column/combo/lazy-instantiate, per-row-UI regression). combobox / switchboard-browser / hotkeys / hotkey-editor / state-manager suites **188 passed, 2 skipped** offscreen. New public symbols registered in `API_INDEX.md`/`API_CHANGES.md`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation warranted** for the option-box toggle rendering on a disabled combo and the filter LineEdit's option-box button layout (the offscreen QPA can't verify the visual).
- **2026-06-27 `Menu` chrome (Header + Footer) is now built lazily on first show — the OptionBox-init-perf "Phase 2" deferred from the 2026-06-21 Phase-1 entry below.** Field symptom: a dense tentacle panel (the `animation` panel is the worst case — ~21 option-box buttons) is noticeably slower to open than most. Root cause: every `tbXXX` option box constructs a `Menu` during `register_children`, and `Menu.__init__` called `init_layout()` eagerly, which built a `Header(config_buttons=["pin"])` **and** a `Footer(add_size_grip=True)` — the heaviest part of a Menu — even though *most* of those menus are never opened. Removing the eager call alone was insufficient: `Menu.add()` and `setTitle()` both route through `_ensure_layout_created()` → `init_layout()`, and every `tbXXX_init` calls `.menu.setTitle(...)` then `.menu.add(...)`, so the chrome rebuilt at register time regardless. **Fix — split scaffold from chrome.** `init_layout()` now builds only the scaffold (`_layout`/`_frame`/`_frame_layout`/central widget/`gridLayout`/stretch); a new idempotent `_ensure_chrome()` builds the Header (frame layout index 0) + Footer (last), and is called first inside `_prepare_for_show()` (the existing first-show hook that already defers the apply/defaults/presets buttons, so chrome is in place before `_resize_height_to_content()` and the popup `adjustSize()` measure — no refit regression) with a `showEvent` safety net. **`setTitle` no longer force-builds** — it stashes `_pending_title` (applied when the header builds) so the ~79 slot call sites (21 in `animation.py` alone) don't each materialize chrome at init; `title()` returns the pending value until then. **Public escape hatch `Menu.ensure_chrome()`** force-builds the chrome now, for the three callers that read `.header` *before* show: `run_modal` (modal dialogs configure the header up front) and mayatk/blendertk `channels_slots.py` "Create Attribute" (the pin→hide button swap). **Persistent mode fix:** with the header deferred, `enable_persistent_mode` on an `add_header=True` menu opened before any normal show would snapshot `had_header=False` and then `disable_persistent_mode` would delete the *permanent* header — so the snapshot is now `self.add_header or bool(self.header)` and the layout-ensure routes through `_ensure_chrome()` (header lands in the frame layout, consistent with eager builds); the `add_header=False` hide-button injection into `centralWidgetLayout` is unchanged. `.footer` has zero external readers anywhere (uitk/mayatk/tentacle/blendertk), so the footer half is pure-win. **Measured (headless micro-bench, PySide6 6.10.1 offscreen, 50 menus):** per-menu construct+setTitle+add dropped **0.59 → 0.23 ms (~2.6×)** with chrome 0/50 built at construct and 50/50 after show; the deferred chrome is ~0.77 ms/menu (~16 ms for a 21-menu panel) now paid only for menus actually opened. That isolated figure is a lower bound — the real cold-panel saving also avoids QSS-polish/layout work and cold icon loads on the un-built chrome, which only the live-Maya panel bench (`tentacle/test/bench/run_in_maya.py`) captures. Regression: `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionBoxInitPerfRegressions` — `test_footer_deferred_until_show`, `test_header_deferred_and_title_survives` (stashed title survives to the built header), `test_ensure_chrome_builds_immediately` (the channels_slots pin→hide swap path), `test_headerless_menu_stays_chromeless` (no chrome recursion via `Header.menu`'s headerless sub-menus); plus `test_menu.py::TestMenuPersistentMode::test_persistent_mode_on_deferred_header_menu_keeps_header` (fail-before/pass-after — a deferred `add_header=True` menu that enters persistent mode keeps its frame-layout header across disable, instead of the snapshot deleting it). Full uitk suite **2109 passed, 4 skipped** offscreen (incl. overlay-refit, recent-values-sizing, adjustsize, run_modal). New public method registered in `API_INDEX.md`/`API_CHANGES.md`. **Live Maya + Blender confirmation still warranted** (per the phased plan): option-box titles render + pin button present, footer size-grip/height correct, tb016/tb019 progress bar (the UI MainWindow footer, not the menu footer — unaffected), the "Create Attribute" modal shows title + hidden pin, persistent-mode hide button, and especially the Blender first-open refit *width* (the historical width-before-QSS-polish gotcha).
- **2026-06-27 MainWindow — a restored window geometry is authoritative; on-show fit-to-content no longer discards a user's saved size.** Field symptom: panels (Shot Manifest, and any resizable window) didn't keep their user-adjusted size across sessions — each session's first show restored the saved geometry and then `fit_height_to_content` immediately snapped the height back to the content minimum, so a deliberately-expanded window "resized itself" every launch. Root cause: `showEvent` ran `fit_to_content_on_show` *unconditionally*, even right after `restore_window_geometry` applied a saved size, so the fit always won. Fix: `restore_window_geometry` now returns whether it applied a valid saved geometry, and `showEvent` skips the on-show fit when it did — a restored size is the user's own and is authoritative. The fit still runs when there's nothing to restore (first-ever show, or a `restore_window_size=False` window), so trailing dead space is still trimmed on first launch. This is the DRY replacement for per-window `fit_to_content_on_show=False` opt-outs (the Macro Manager's was removed — see mayatk CHANGELOG 2026-06-27). Tests: `test_mainwindow.py::test_restored_geometry_is_authoritative_over_fit` (a saved 500×600 survives the on-show fit on both axes) + `::test_first_show_without_saved_geometry_fits_to_content` (a first-ever show still trims to content); full mainwindow + resize suites 113 green.
- **2026-06-27 Hotkey editor — re-binding a taken key works, internal uitk collisions are overwritable, scope gates collisions/buttons, and presets moved to the header menu.** Four field refinements to the Hotkey Editor assign flow. **(1) Re-assigning an already-taken key was impossible.** Once a key was bound at *Application* scope, double-clicking another row and pressing that same chord just *fired the existing slot* instead of capturing — the app-scoped `QShortcut` (owned by the always-visible host window, so it fires regardless of focus) won the key before the capture editor saw it. Fix at the capture-widget layer: `HotkeyCaptureEdit.event()` now accepts `QEvent.ShortcutOverride`, which Qt sends to the focus widget *before* shortcut processing — accepting it cancels the shortcut and delivers the chord as a normal key press to `keyPressEvent`, so every key (including one already assigned app-wide) is captured, never fired. Esc/Return still close the editor via the delegate's own filter. **(2) Internal uitk collisions now offer overwrite, like Maya's do.** `_builtin_internal_collision_checker` reported an app-vs-window same-key clash as a *soft* "may fire alongside" note with no clear action, so the user couldn't resolve it. Every collision that survives the scope-overlap rules is genuinely ambiguous (Qt can't disambiguate), so all are now `breaks_binding=True` with a `clear_action` — the conflict dialog's **Clear conflicting && assign** path frees the other uitk binding, mirroring the existing Maya clear option. **(3) Scope drives collisions, and scope buttons gate on a binding.** The "safe unless application wide" rule is the overlap logic itself: window-scoped dupes across *different* UIs don't collide (independent focus targets) and aren't reported; once either side is app-scoped the key collides with everything. The per-row scope toggle is now disabled (with a "Assign a shortcut before choosing its scope" tooltip) on rows that have no key bound — scope is meaningless without a sequence to fire. **(4) Presets moved to the header ⋯-menu.** `EditorPanel.init_preset_row(..., in_header_menu=True)` (new, reusable by any editor) tucks the preset selector into the `Header`'s menu popup instead of a body row, adding the header `menu` button automatically; the Hotkey Editor opts in so the body stays focused on the shortcut table. Tests: `test_hotkey_capture_delegate.py::test_accepts_shortcut_override`; `test_hotkey_editor.py` (app-vs-window overwrite offered, window dupes across UIs allowed, scope button disabled without a key, preset row lives in the header menu). hotkey_capture / hotkey_editor / hotkeys / preset_manager / switchboard-editors suites green offscreen (154).
- **2026-06-27 `Menu` hide-on-leave no longer dismisses the popup mid-edit — fixes accidental preset-template overwrites.** Field symptom (preset template manager): clicking **Save** put the preset combo into inline-edit mode (line edit focused, pre-filled with the *active* preset's own name, `selectAll`), but reaching for the keyboard moved the cursor off the unpinned popup; the 100 ms `hide_on_leave` poll (`_check_cursor_position`) saw the cursor outside and called `hide()` mid-edit — ending the edit before the user could retype the name and re-saving over the active template. **Root cause:** the leave check only knew cursor geometry; it had no notion of "a widget is being edited," so an in-progress text entry was indistinguishable from an idle popup. **Fix (general, at the `Menu` layer):** `_check_cursor_position` now suppresses the hide while a *text-entry* widget inside the menu's subtree has keyboard focus — `_text_edit_in_progress()` checks `QApplication.focusWidget()` is a `QLineEdit`/`QTextEdit`/`QPlainTextEdit`/`QAbstractSpinBox` (the editable combo focuses its internal `QLineEdit`) *and* walks back to the menu via the shared `_widget_in_subtree` helper (extracted from the existing cursor-over-descendant parent-chain walk — DRY, crosses window boundaries like the cursor check). Scoped deliberately to text entry: a click that merely parks focus on a button or plain combo still lets the fast hide-on-leave fire, preserving the snappy popup UX the design relies on; the menu hides normally the moment the edit ends. The existing `ComboBox.focusOutEvent` cancel (`emit_signal=False`) remains the backstop, so a legitimate hide during an edit cancels rather than commits. Tests: `test_menu.py::TestMenuHideOnLeave` (focused child text widget keeps the popup open mid-edit; focus outside the subtree still hides; a focused *non-text* child still hides — locks the narrowed scope) and `test_preset_manager.py::TestBuiltinTier::test_inline_save_cancelled_by_focus_out_does_not_overwrite` (the backstop: an inline Save ended by focus-out leaves the active preset's file untouched). menu / preset_manager / dismiss-on-move / comboBox / switchboard-browser suites green offscreen.
- **2026-06-25 `PresetManager.wire_combo` — the Refresh button now re-scans the preset directory, not just the active preset's values.** Field gap: presets a user added to or deleted from the preset dir *by hand* (dropping in / removing `*.json` files) didn't appear in the combo until the next `wire_combo` — `on_refresh` only re-applied `active_preset`'s stored values to the widgets. It now calls the existing `refresh()` closure first (repopulating the combo from disk via `mgr.list()`), then re-applies the active preset's values (discard edits), guarded by `mgr.exists(active)` so a manually-deleted *active* preset is skipped without the misleading "Preset not found" warning — matching `PresetStore.active`'s documented contract (a stale pointer is returned deliberately; the GUI falls back to no-selection). Bonus: Refresh at combo index -1 (post session-restore) now also restores the visible selection, not just the values. Tests: `test_preset_manager.py::TestBuiltinTier` (`test_refresh_picks_up_preset_added_to_dir_by_hand`, `test_refresh_drops_preset_removed_from_dir_by_hand` — both fail-before/pass-after); existing refresh/toolbar-tooltip tests updated. preset_manager suite green (73).
- **2026-06-25 Hotkey editor conflict UX — scope toggle no longer pops a modal, and the conflict dialog can free a clashing Maya binding.** Two refinements to the assign/conflict flow. **(1) Scope toggle is modeless.** Flipping a binding's Window↔Application scope ran the full collision check and could pop the conflict modal — heavy for a one-click, reversible mode flip. It now applies immediately and surfaces any conflict the new scope introduces inline in the footer (`_on_scope_toggle` uses the new non-prompting `_collect_conflicts`, extracted from `_resolve_collisions`); the modal is reserved for the deliberate act of binding a key. **(2) The conflict dialog can clear a Maya binding.** Previously a Maya hotkey clash was informational only. The dialog now offers **Assign & free Maya binding** when Maya's active hotkey set is editable — it unbinds Maya's hotkey (plus any uitk duplicates) and assigns; on the locked factory set the option is shown **disabled** with a "switch to a custom Maya set" tooltip rather than silently absent. `CollisionConflict` already carried `source`/`clear_action`, so no schema change — the dialog keys off `source=="maya"` + whether a clear-action is present. Tests: `test_hotkey_editor.py` (scope toggle never calls the prompt yet still applies; the dialog offers + runs the Maya clear when editable; shows it disabled when locked). hotkeys / hotkey_editor suites green offscreen (48).
- **2026-06-25 Hotkey editor — assigning a shortcut is fast again, and overwriting/clearing a binding now actually clears it.** Two field bugs from live tentacle/Maya use. **(1) Assign built every UI (slow, crash-prone, slot/menu spam).** `_builtin_internal_collision_checker` looped every *registered* UI and called `sb.get_ui(name)` on each — so each assign synchronously built all ~143 UIs (instantiating their slot classes and re-running Maya's native-menu build procs, hence the `NucleusCacheMenu`/`buildHelpMenu`/`buildToonMenu` MEL errors and "extra slots initialized" log), which was slow and could crash Maya. Its own docstring said "across all **loaded** UIs", so the `get_ui` was a bug: it now uses `loaded_ui.peek` (already-built UIs only). An unbuilt UI has registered no `QShortcut`, so its bindings are inert and can't collide at runtime; the edited UI (and any navigated to) is loaded, so live conflicts are still caught. Verified in a fresh Maya: the checker builds **0** UIs and runs in **2 ms** (was building 143). **(2) Overwriting/clearing didn't clear the old binding.** `set_user_shortcut(ui, m, "")` correctly stored an empty override and tore down the live `QShortcut`, but both read paths (`get_shortcut_registry` and the build-time `register_slots_shortcuts`) tested the override with `if override:` — an empty string is falsy, so a cleared binding *fell through to its decorator default*. A binding with a non-empty `@Shortcut("…")` default therefore reverted to that default on clear (and was re-registered live), so the overwritten/conflicting shortcut looked uncleared and kept firing. Fix: distinguish *present-but-empty* (`""` → explicit "no shortcut") from *missing* (`None` → use default) via `if override is not None:`. Confirmed in a fresh Maya that `ui.settings` round-trips a stored empty string as `""` (not `None`), so the distinction is reliable. Tests: `test_hotkeys.py::TestClearedShortcutBinding` (default present without override; overwrite-then-clear yields empty not the default; cleared binding registers no live `QShortcut`), `test_hotkey_editor.py::test_collision_checker_peeks_not_builds` (the internal checker never calls `get_ui`). hotkeys / hotkey_editor / preset_manager suites green offscreen (116).
- **2026-06-25 Hotkey editor opens ~100× faster — the preset "modified?" check no longer builds every registered UI.** Field symptom (tentacle in Maya): the Hotkey Editor "took forever to launch." **Root cause:** opening the editor runs the preset dirty-marker check (`init_preset_row` → `wire_combo` → `_resync_active` → `is_modified` → `_capture_values` → the editor's `value_provider` = `export_shortcuts`), and `export_shortcuts` called `sb.get_ui(name)` for **every** registered UI to read its shortcut state — building all ~143 UIs (and instantiating their slot classes) just to compare against the active preset. Proven in a fresh Maya 2025 (force_new_instance): with the active preset `test_hotkeys` present, the full export builds **143 UIs in 9.8 s** — that ran on every open. **Why the obvious fixes are wrong:** `get_shortcut_registry` genuinely needs a *built* UI (it walks `findChildren()` for widget→method matches and introspects the slots instance for `@shortcut` methods and their defaults — QSettings holds only *overrides*), so "read from QSettings instead" can't reproduce the export; and a "clean-since-sync then compare" flag only *defers* the 143-build to the user's first edit. **Fix (extends the existing strategy-callable seam, no new mode):** `PresetManager` gains an optional `modified_value_provider` — a *cheaper* capture used only by `is_modified()`, falling back to `value_provider` when unset (so save still uses the full capture). `_capture_values(..., for_modified=True)` selects it. The Hotkey Editor supplies `export_shortcuts(loaded_only=True)`, which **peeks** already-loaded UIs (`loaded_ui.peek`, never `get_ui`) — an unbuilt UI has no live edit to differ from the preset, so it's correctly skipped. The dirty marker stays a *real* value comparison (not a dirty-since-load approximation), just over the loaded subset; the three edit handlers (`_apply_shortcut`, `_on_scope_toggle`, `reset_shortcut`) now call the (now-cheap) `refresh_modified_state()` so the marker is live. **Save is untouched** — `export_shortcuts(loaded_only=False)` still captures a complete snapshot of every UI. Verified in a fresh Maya: editor open builds **1 UI in 0.09 s** (was 143 / 9.8 s; ~100×), the dirty-check builds **0** new UIs (0.001 s), and the full save export still builds all 143. Trade-off: the marker reflects loaded UIs, so a UI customized last session but never opened this session won't flip the marker until opened — negligible and self-correcting. Tests: `test_preset_manager.py::TestSemanticPresetMode` (`is_modified` uses the cheap provider and never the full one; save uses the full provider; falls back to `value_provider` when no cheap one is set), `test_hotkey_editor.py` (`loaded_only` export never calls `get_ui`; the editor wires `modified_value_provider` to the cheap export). preset_manager / hotkey_editor / hotkeys / style_editor / optionBox / state_manager suites green offscreen (277).
- **2026-06-25 Hotkey editor "Application" scope now actually fires app-wide — an application-scoped shortcut is owned by the host's always-visible main window, not the (usually hidden) slot UI.** Field symptom (tentacle in Maya): set a shortcut to **App** scope in the Hotkey Editor and it does nothing — the key never triggers the action. Root cause is a Qt visibility gate: `QShortcutMap::correctContextWidget` rejects a `QShortcut` whose **owner widget is hidden** *before* it ever checks the context, so even `Qt.ApplicationShortcut` is inert when its owner is hidden. `SwitchboardShortcutMixin` parented every shortcut to its slot UI (`_create_switchboard_shortcut`'s `parent = ui`), and tentacle's tool UIs are hidden whenever the tool isn't open — exactly when "fires anywhere in the host app" is supposed to work. (The marking menu's own F12 never hit this because its `GlobalShortcut` is owned by the always-visible `MayaWindow`.) Proven both ways: a hidden-owner `ApplicationShortcut` fired 0×, a visible-owner one fired, and showing the owner made the hidden one start firing. **Fix:** new `resolve_application_host(widget)` (in `widgets/mixins/shortcuts.py`) returns an always-visible top-level (known DCC host `MayaWindow`/`3dsMaxWindow` → nearest visible top-level ancestor → any visible top-level → the widget itself); `_create_switchboard_shortcut` owns application-scoped shortcuts by that host instead of the slot UI. `set_user_shortcut` now **recreates** the shortcut on rebind (rather than `setContext` in place) so flipping Window↔Application re-owns it to the correct window — `setContext` alone can't reparent. Verified end-to-end in a fresh Maya 2025: `resolve_application_host(hidden_widget)` → `MayaWindow`; a MayaWindow-owned app shortcut fires on a key sent to the main window while the slot UI is hidden, the hidden-owned one stays inert. Window/widget scopes are unchanged (still owned by the UI). Regression: `test_hotkeys.py::TestResolveApplicationHost` (3) + `TestApplicationScopeOwner` (3 — app-scope owner is visible & not the hidden UI; window-scope owner is the UI; Window→App re-owns to the host); existing `TestShortcutScope` (context persistence) stays green via the recreate path.
- **2026-06-25 `PresetManager.load` — a loaded preset/template now persists to session state, so the active preset's *values* survive to the next session (not just its name).** Field symptom (mayatk Scene Exporter): end a session with the 'unity_basic' template active and all widgets showing its settings → next session the template *name* is restored in the combo but the widget *values* are the stale pre-template ones. **Root cause:** `load`'s MainWindow path applied the preset values inside `with self.state.suppress_save():` and the docstring framed that as intentional ("loading a preset does not overwrite the user's QSettings session state"). But `wire_combo` restores only the active *name* across sessions by design ("widgets restore themselves from session state") — which only works if the preset's values ARE the session state. Suppressing the save left them out of QSettings, so the name (persisted in the `.active` sidecar) and the values (per-widget QSettings) desynced: the combo showed 'unity_basic' while the widgets reverted to their pre-load values. Confirmed headlessly with a real `StateManager` (manual state {chk:False,spn:0} → load template {True,5} → QSettings still {False,0} → next-session restore = stale). **Fix:** keep `suppress_save` *during* the bulk apply (so a mid-apply slot cascade can't persist a half-applied state) but persist the final values once *after* it (`state.save(widget)` per applied widget, outside the suppression). The preset now becomes session state: next session restores the template's values, and a manual edit after loading both persists and marks the combo modified (`'unity_basic *'`). Standalone (`from_widgets`, no `state`) and semantic (`value_applier`, e.g. the DCC bridges) paths are unchanged — the fix is in the `state` branch only. Tests: `test_preset_manager.py::TestLoadPersistsSessionState` (3 — load writes the applied value to QSettings, the active template's values restore next session, a manual edit coexists with the template); previously this state path was only exercised by a live-Maya probe. persistence/bridge/state-manager suites green offscreen.
- **2026-06-25 `StateManager` — combos can persist by item *text*/*data*, not just index (`widget.restore_by`); fixes a dynamically-populated combo "resetting to None" across sessions.** Field symptom (mayatk Scene Exporter): the FBX-preset combo (`cmb000`) reset to "None" every session and the user's selection never stuck, while static combos in the same panel (`check_framerate`, `set_linear_unit`) restored fine. **Root cause — index-based persistence of a *dynamic* list.** Every uitk combo persists via `currentIndexChanged` → `StateManager` stores the integer **index**; `apply` restores it (skipping out-of-range). That's correct only when the item list is identical across sessions. `cmb000` is rebuilt from a `*.fbxexportpreset` directory scan on every show (`refresh_on_show=True`), and `pythontk.get_dir_contents` uses unsorted `os.scandir`, so the index of a given preset can shift between sessions — and when the list is now shorter, the saved index falls out of range, `apply` skips it, and the combo drops to item 0 ("None"). The live registry corroborated it: `…\scene_exporter\cmb000\currentIndexChanged = 0` while the static combos held their non-default indices. The save side was never broken; index identity was. **Fix (opt-in, general):** a new `widget.restore_by` attribute — `"index"` (default, unchanged for every existing widget) / `"text"` / `"data"`. In text/data mode `_get_current_value` captures `currentText()`/`currentData()`, `save` re-derives that identity even though the change signal still delivers an index, `apply` selects via `findText`/`findData` (a value no longer present is a no-op — keeps the current selection rather than forcing item 0), and `load` skips JSON-decoding so a preset literally named `"123"`/`"true"` stays a string. Default-mode behavior is byte-for-byte identical (the index out-of-range guard, `-1` no-selection transient, etc. all unchanged). mayatk's `cmb000_init` opts in with `restore_by="text"` (preset name = stable identity, survives the dir moving). Proven headlessly: reorder/shrink the item list and index mode picks the wrong preset / resets to "None", text mode survives both. Tests: `test_state_manager.py` (9 — index default incl. the documented shrink-resets-to-0 bug, text mode round-trip through reorder/shrink, save ignores the index the change-signal passes, missing-value keeps selection, numeric-looking name stays a string, data mode); persistence/combobox/mainwindow/optionBox/switchboard suites green offscreen (446).
- **2026-06-25 Option-box menu + preset init perf — the dropdown `Menu` is now built lazily, and `PresetManager` stops re-hitting the filesystem on every `preset_dir` read.** Follow-up to the preset-template redesign: live testing reported a noticeable init slowdown. Profiling `wire_combo` (offscreen, the QPA stylesheet is trivial — the gap is *wider* under a real DCC stylesheet where QSS application dominates) traced the added cost to the new per-combo `option_box` toolbar. Two fixes, both general (not preset-specific): **(1) `OptionMenuOption`/`ContextMenuOption` build their `Menu` lazily.** The constructor used to eagerly `Menu.create_dropdown_menu(...)` — applying the menu's QSS and building its chrome at *wrap* time, a cost paid by every option-box menu even if the user never opens it. Construction now just stores the config; a new `_ensure_menu()` (and the `menu` property / `_show_menu`) creates it on first access/show. `set_wrapped_widget` only reparents an already-built menu (never forces creation). Nothing the option-box framework does at wrap touches `option.menu`, so the menu now materialises only on the first ⋯-click. **(2) `PresetManager.preset_dir` ensures the directory once, not on every read.** The getter ran `_maybe_migrate_legacy` + `mkdir` on *every* access, and the `_store` property (rebuilt per access) plus `source()` (called per preset name while italicising built-ins) hammered it — N presets ⇒ N migrate+mkdir syscalls per refresh. It now memoises the ensured path (`_ensured_dir`); a reassigned dir re-ensures, and writes self-heal the dir at the `PresetStore` layer (its `save`/active-write both `mkdir`), so reads never need to. **(2b)** Relatedly, the combo's built-in italicising (`mark_builtins`) probed `source(nm)` *per preset name* — each rebuilding the store + stat-ing both tiers (O(N) on every refresh) — now replaced by two `list(tier=…)` globs and set membership (shadow-aware: a name is read-only built-in iff it ships built-in AND isn't shadowed by a user preset), O(1) per name (~1.6× on a 26-preset panel, scaling with preset count). Measured: `ComboBox()+wire_combo()` **8.4 ms → 5.7 ms (~32%)** offscreen (the eager `Menu` and the FS churn both gone); the remaining cost is the inherent option-box container wrap (border-trim `setStyleSheet` per widget + sizing) — deferring *that* to the container's first `showEvent` is the larger remaining lever but is the [`OptionBox init perf`] Phase-2 refactor that needs live Maya+Blender verification, so it's left for that effort rather than rushed here. Today's `_add_menu_item` / `Menu._check_cursor_position` changes are **not** on the init path (they run on menu-open and hover-polling). Regression tests: `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionMenuClickableRows::test_menu_is_built_lazily` (construction leaves `_menu` None for both option classes; first access materialises + populates), `test_preset_manager.py::test_wire_combo_does_not_build_menu_eagerly`.
- **2026-06-25 In-cell choice (dropdown) capture (`widgets/choice_capture_delegate.py`) — the dropdown sibling of `hotkey_capture_delegate`.** Field symptom (mayatk Macro Manager): the Category column embedded a *persistent* editable `QComboBox` cell widget in every row, which painted over the cell, grabbed hover/select, and read as a permanently-armed control — inconsistent with the Hotkey column's double-click-to-edit feel. New reusable primitive mirroring the hotkey delegate exactly: `ChoiceCaptureDelegate` (emits `captured(row, col, value)`, deferred one tick so a slot may rebuild the view; `createEditor` returns a `QComboBox` seeded with a fixed choice list, a dropdown pick commits + closes immediately, a stored value outside the choices is preserved via `setEditorData`), `BorderedChoiceCaptureDelegate` (composes `RowSelectionBorderDelegate`), and the turnkey `install_choice_capture(table, column, choices, on_capture, *, editable=True, bordered=False)` helper that wires the delegate + opens it on double-click even under `NoEditTriggers`. The cell stays a plain item — no persistent widget, no select-on-hover. **Deliberately no auto-`showPopup`:** opening the list on the same double-click that creates the editor lets the click's trailing mouse-release land in the freshly-opened popup — on a cell whose value is already a list item that release re-selects the current row and commits a no-op (the cell reads as "not editable"), while an empty cell has nothing highlighted under the cursor and opens fine (the "only empty category cells are editable" field symptom). The user opens the dropdown with a deliberate click instead. Tests: `test_choice_capture_delegate.py` (pick emits row/col/value + sets the cell, editable typed value, non-editable combo, custom-value preservation, bordered variant, `NoEditTriggers` open-via-editItem, `set_choices`, and an integration case against the real uitk `TableWidget` proving the column is a plain item with no cell widget) — 8 green offscreen on PySide6 6.10.1.
- **2026-06-25 Preset template redesigned.** `PresetManager.wire_combo` now builds a uitk `ComboBox` with an `option_box` toolbar (Refresh / Save / ⋯-menu: Rename / Open folder / Delete) and inline Save/Rename (no pop-up dialogs) instead of a `WidgetComboBox` with an in-dropdown action row. `wire_combo` now returns the option-box container; added `make_preset_combo` (one-call build, used by `EditorPanel`). `EditorPanel` now delegates preset save/load to `PresetManager` (removed its duplicated JSON plumbing). The ⋯ menu is a cursor-centred plain action list (no header / footer / apply chrome). Three follow-up fixes from live testing: **(1)** `wire_combo` clamps an *unbounded* combo to its natural row height — the option-box icon buttons are sized to the combo's height, so a combo dropped into a stretchy container (a menu's `add_presets` "Menu Actions" group) otherwise ballooned the buttons to ~480 px squares and squeezed the dropdown to nothing; in-panel callers that set an explicit height are untouched. **(2)** `Menu._check_cursor_position` (hide-on-leave) now walks `widget_at`'s QObject parent chain back to the menu instead of `QWidget.isAncestorOf` (which is *same-window only*) — so a child popup that is a separate top-level window (a `ComboBox` dropdown, or an option-box ⋯ menu opened from a widget inside the menu) no longer closes the host menu the moment the cursor moves onto it. **(3)** The ⋯-menu rows (Rename / Open folder / Delete) were inert — no hover feedback, clicks did nothing. `OptionMenuOption`/`ContextMenuOption` added items via `menu.add(label, callback)`, but `Menu.add(text)` maps a non-widget string to a **QLabel** (no hover, no `clicked` signal) and stores the second arg as inert item-DATA that is never invoked — so every `(label, callback)` entry rendered a dead row (the documented `option.menu.add("X", cb)` examples never actually fired). Fixed at the option layer via a shared `OptionMenuOption._add_menu_item` that builds a real `QPushButton` and wires `clicked` → callback (hiding the menu first so the pop-up releases focus/grab before the action runs, e.g. inline rename focusing the combo); fixes both the static-`menu_items` and the dynamic-`menu_provider` paths for every option-box context menu, not just presets. Regression tests: `test_preset_manager.py` (height clamp + explicit-height preserved + cursor-centred chrome-less menu + **real-dispatch clickable rows that fire `Delete`** — not the provider-closure proxy), `test_menu.py::TestMenuHideOnLeave` (nested-popup keeps open / truly-outside hides), `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionMenuClickableRows` (static + dynamic items render as clickable buttons that fire, and clicking dismisses the menu).
- **2026-06-25 In-cell hotkey capture (`widgets/hotkey_capture_delegate.py`) + PySide6 chord-capture crash fix.** Field symptom: assigning a shortcut in the Hotkey Editor (and the mayatk Macro Manager, which shared the dialog) crashed under PySide6 with `TypeError: QKeyCombination.__init__ called with wrong argument types`. **Root cause:** `QKeySequence(key | modifiers)` where `key` is a plain int (`event.key()`) and `modifiers` is a `Qt.KeyboardModifier` enum — in PySide6 `int | KeyboardModifier` routes through a deprecated `__ror__` that builds a `QKeyCombination(modifier, int)` with swapped types and raises. **Fix + DRY refactor:** the modal "double-click → dialog → type chord → OK" flow is replaced by an in-cell capture editor extracted into a reusable primitive. `HotkeyCaptureEdit` (read-only `QLineEdit` that interprets the next key chord as a shortcut; Backspace clears, Esc cancels), `HotkeyCaptureDelegate` (emits `captured(row, col, sequence)`, deferred one tick so a slot may rebuild the view), `BorderedHotkeyCaptureDelegate` (composes `RowSelectionBorderDelegate` for tables that paint the row-spanning selection outline), and the turnkey `install_hotkey_capture(table, column, on_capture, *, bordered=False)` helper that wires the delegate + opens it on double-click even under `NoEditTriggers`. Sequence building coerces both operands to plain ints via the canonical `ConvertMixin.to_int` (handles Qt enum/flag — `Qt.KeyboardModifier` rejects `int()` but exposes `.value` on PySide6 — and plain ints on PySide2) before the OR. `HotkeyEditor` now uses `install_hotkey_capture(..., bordered=True)` and its dead `KeyCaptureDialog` (plus now-unused `StyleSheet`/`IconManager` imports) was removed; the Macro Manager's double-click and context-menu "Assign" both route through the shared delegate. Tests: `test_hotkey_capture_delegate.py` (chord captures without crashing, bare-key/lone-modifier/Backspace handling, full `install_hotkey_capture` flow incl. `NoEditTriggers`) — 6 green offscreen on PySide6 6.10.1; existing `test_hotkey_editor.py` 17 green.
- **2026-06-25 `PresetManager` — per-instance capture `scope` + `include`/`exclude` allowlist.** Templates/presets could only ever capture one implicit widget set, chosen by the manager's *parent* type: a header-menu preset (`menu.add_presets = True`) saw **only the menu's own items**, never the host window's panel widgets. New `PresetManager.scope` (`"auto"` default — unchanged legacy resolution; `"menu"`; `"window"`; `"explicit"`) makes the choice explicit per instance, and `include(*names_or_widgets)` / `exclude(*names_or_widgets)` refine it by `objectName` (names resolve at save/load time, so widgets that don't exist at config time still match). `"window"` scope resolves the owning `MainWindow` even from a menu parent — via the new `Menu.owner_window()` (a public alias for the reparent-race-robust `_resolve_registration_window`) — adopts its `StateManager` for value get/set, and captures only **value-bearing** widgets (`_get_widget_value` predicate), so action buttons, group boxes, header chrome, and option-box plumbing are never swept into a preset. Default (`"auto"`) is byte-for-byte the prior behavior, so existing `add_presets` callers (reference_manager, color_manager) are unchanged. Tests: `test_preset_manager.py::TestCaptureScope` (scope selection, exclude/include filtering, auto-stays-menu regression guard, window-scope round-trip).
- **2026-06-25 `RecentValuesOption` — the popup no longer shows the widget's *current* value.** It previously pinned the current value as a styled row at the top of the dropdown (followed by a separator), which is redundant noise: the popup exists to restore a *previously used* value, and re-selecting the value you already have is a no-op. `_populate_popup` now lists only the history with the current value excluded (deduped by restore-data, as before), and falls back to the "No recent values" message when nothing else remains. Removed the now-dead `is_current` plumbing and `add_separator`/`recentValueRow_current` from `RecentValuesPopup`. Test: `test_optionBox.py::TestRecentValuesExcludesCurrent` (current value absent from the row list, no current-row/separator, empty message when history holds only the current value).
- **2026-06-24 Test suite no longer wipes the developer's *live* settings (the "persistent settings revert to defaults after a while" report).** Field symptom: marking-menu bindings, widget state, and theme restore fine across back-to-back DCC sessions, then "after a while" silently reset to defaults. **Root cause — the test suite, not the runtime.** `SettingsManager` persists to the real per-user store (`HKCU\Software\uitk\shared` on Windows), and `test_settings_manager.py::TestSettingsManagerDefaults` called `QSettings("uitk","shared").clear()` in **both** `setUp` and `tearDown` — so every `pytest` run emptied the production store on its way out (the file's docstring *claimed* it only touched `test_uitk_*` orgs; that held for `TestRegistryMigration` but not this class). "After a while" = "after a test run"; back-to-back DCC sessions worked only because no test ran between them. The live registry corroborated it: dozens of fixture roots (`ClearOnInitTest`, `TestGeomClear`, `StandaloneKeepsPersistTest`, …) written straight into the real hive. **Two-layer fix.** (1) Targeted: `TestSettingsManagerDefaults` no longer clears `(uitk, shared)` (its assertions only inspect `organizationName()`/`applicationName()`/`namespace` — they never needed a clean store) and pins `_legacy_qsettings_pairs_for → []` so construction can't drain real legacy data. (2) Suite-wide guard in `conftest.py` (`_sandbox_qsettings`, activated at import so it covers `unittest`/`mayapy` too): swaps `QtCore.QSettings` for a thin subclass that rewrites the two registry-bound overloads — `QSettings(org, app[, parent])` and `QSettings(scope, org, app[, parent])` — to the explicit `IniFormat` constructor under a throwaway temp dir, so **no** test can read, write, or clear the real store, and the fixture-root pollution stops. Other overloads (explicit-format, `QSettings(path, IniFormat)`, no-arg) pass through. A dedicated meta-test (`test_conftest_qsettings_sandbox.py`) pins this down — it would have caught the inert first attempt below. **Qt gotcha that made the obvious approach fail:** `setDefaultFormat`/`setPath` do *not* redirect `QSettings(org, app)` on Windows — that overload always uses `NativeFormat` (registry) and `setPath` is a no-op for it; only the explicit `QSettings(Format, Scope, org, app)` constructor honors `IniFormat`. Verified: every QSettings-using suite green under the sandbox (settings/persistence/recent-values/color-swatch/tree/resolver + mainwindow/optionBox/switchboard/preset/marking-menu) with the real `HKCU\Software\uitk\shared` provably untouched (binding blob byte-length and top-level key count unchanged; zero new fixture roots).
- **2026-06-25 `LineEdit` gains a display/data split, and recent-values become data-aware.** `LineEdit.set_value(value, display=None)` shows a friendly *display* string while `value()`/`data()` carry the real payload (Qt item-data style, single payload); `data()` returns `None` when the text *is* the value, and a manual edit (`textEdited`) clears the payload so typed text becomes the value again. The validator mixin now validates against a `_validation_value()` hook (defaults to `text()`, `LineEdit` overrides to `value()`) so validation/`valid_tooltip` see the real data, not the display. `RecentValuesStore` learns `RecentValueEntry(data, display)` (mirrors `PinnedValueEntry`): dedup/normalize key off `data`, persistence serializes entries to a tagged dict, and `display_map` prefers an entry's explicit display. `RecentValuesOption.record()`/restore read the widget's `data()` and use `set_value` on restore, so an entry shows its label and still resolves to the real value. Backward compatible — plain string history and non-data-aware widgets are unchanged. Tests: `test_line_edit_validator.py` (value/data split, payload invalidation, validator-against-payload, data-aware record/restore), `test_recent_values_store.py::TestRecentValueEntry` (dedup/persist/display).
- **2026-06-24 `ComboBox` — an option-box combobox no longer drops a *fast* item click (THE real combobox fix; supersedes the combobox half of the entry below, which wrongly blamed `MouseTracking`).** Field symptom: open an option-box combobox from a marking-menu submenu, the dropdown opens but clicking a row often doesn't change the value ("took many tries"); intermittent. **Root cause — Qt's own `QComboBoxPrivateContainer.blockMouseReleaseTimer`** (not uitk): it swallows the *selecting* mouse-release for `QApplication.doubleClickInterval()` (~400 ms) after the popup opens, so the click that OPENS the popup can't instantly pick the row under the cursor. In a fast marking-menu workflow the user clicks a row *within* that window, so the first item click is silently dropped — the live `UITK_INPUT_LOG` probe caught it exactly: `view pressed row=N` with the release landing on the right row and a valid current index, but **no** following `activated`; a second, later click on the same row commits (the textbook timer signature). Reproduced in isolation (no marking menu): open a combo via a real click, click a row immediately → `currentIndex` unchanged; click after the interval → commits. This is why hiding the marking menu ("recovery") seemed to fix it — it only slowed the user past the window — and why `MouseTracking` was a red herring (it is **dormant** during the clicks; zero grab records). **Fix: `_PopupItemClickCommitter`**, an event filter installed on the popup view's viewport (so it runs *before* the container's own filter): a press **and** release that both land on the same valid/enabled/selectable list row is an unambiguous selection (unlike the opening click, whose press is on the combo, not the list) — it commits (`setCurrentIndex` + best-effort `activated`) and consumes the release, bypassing the timer; the opening click and drag-to-select still fall through to Qt unchanged. Tests (**the actual symptom**, end-to-end via `QTest`, not a proxy): `test_combobox.py::ItemClickCommitsWithinBlockWindow` — a fast item click commits (fail-before `0 != 2` / pass-after) and the opening click does not auto-select (popup stays open); skip-guarded if the offscreen QPA won't display the popup. combobox / events / optionBox suites green offscreen (202). The same-window `MouseTracking` filter and `_is_popup_menu_child` gate from the entry below are real and kept (they stop the tracker/gesture handlers from claiming foreign-window option-box controls — the *checkbox* synthetic-release path), but they do **not** fix combobox selection.
- **2026-06-24 `MarkingMenu` — an option-box menu launched from a submenu menu button is no longer input-dead (checkbox wouldn't toggle; combobox opened but wouldn't select).** Field symptom: marking menu → submenu → release over a menu button to launch its option-box `Menu`, and inside it the checkbox won't toggle and the combobox dropdown opens but no row can be picked; recovered only by re-showing the marking menu and hiding it. **Unified root cause:** the option-box `Menu`'s controls live in a *separate popup window* but stay QObject-**children** of the marking-menu page (the `Menu` is Qt-parented to the page's wrapped button), and `findChildren` recurses **across** that window boundary — so both of the marking menu's input subsystems claimed those popup controls as part of its own gesture surface. Two enforcement points → two fixes: **(1) Combobox** [SUPERSEDED — combobox selection was actually the `blockMouseReleaseTimer`; see the `ComboBox` entry above. The filter below is real and kept, but it does NOT fix combobox selection; `MouseTracking` is dormant during those clicks.] — `MouseTracking.update_child_widgets` pulled the dropdown's `QListView` viewport into `_widgets` and `grabMouse()`'d it on hover (re-run on the window-activation the popup itself triggers: `_reinitialize_tracking` → `update_child_widgets` → `_filter_viewport_widgets`), stealing the very press/release the list needed to commit a selection. Fixed by the **same-window filter** in `update_child_widgets` — keep only widgets whose `window()` is the tracker's container window; explicitly-registered ExpandableList sublists still survive via `_extra_widgets`. **(2) Checkbox** — the gesture child-handler `child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent` swallowed the checkbox's release via the stuck `_action_dispatched` latch (the launching click left it `True`; a popup press never resets it). Fixed by the **`_is_popup_menu_child` gate** on `child_enterEvent`/`child_leaveEvent`/`child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent` — the gesture handlers ignore any widget whose top-level window is a `Menu`. **Method:** a gated (`UITK_INPUT_LOG`) live probe in `ComboBox.showPopup` logged each popup-view click's resolved row vs the view's current row + the `activated` signal; post-fix it showed `hitRow==curRow` and `activated` **committing**, with `winActive=True`. That data **refuted** two earlier theories that were tried and reverted: window-activation (`ComboBox._activate_host_window` was a *no-op* here — the host was already active) and a *grab leak to the marking menu* (the `changeEvent` / `_relinquish_input_control`-on-`Menu`-activation attempt — the probe showed `mouseGrabber()` was **None**, not the marking menu; reverted, along with an earlier `dismiss_gesture`/overlay-hide attempt that also didn't fix it). Tests: `test_events.py::TestMouseTrackingUpdateMethods::test_excludes_combobox_popup_viewport` (real combobox popup — its `QListView`+viewport must not enter `_widgets`; fail-before/pass-after proven by toggling the filter) and `test_marking_menu_chord_release.py::MarkingMenuIgnoresPopupMenuChildren` (gesture handlers ignore popup-`Menu` children so the latch can't swallow their release). events / combobox / marking-menu / menu / optionBox suites green offscreen (400). `_relinquish_input_control` is retained for the *standalone-window* leaf-launch path (its `hide()`/`hideEvent` call sites — the 2026-06-21 entry below), just no longer driven from the reverted `changeEvent`.
- **2026-06-24 `ExternalAppHandler` — external apps now fully self-describe; hosts no longer enumerate them.** `discover()` derives each app's `install_spec` straight from its distribution (`entry_point.dist.name`), so a host never repeats the install target. Entry-point extras are split into two namespaces: plain tokens stay semantic browser tags, while `hide_<host>` extras become a dedicated **visibility gate** (`hidden_in`) — `entries()` now hides an app whose gate intersects the switchboard's `context_tags` (mirrors widget `apply_visibility_policy`; exclusion semantics, empty context = no filtering), kept separate from semantic tags so a domain tag like `photogrammetry` can never accidentally hide an app from a host. Gated apps stay launchable by name — the gate governs *listing*, not reachability. New install-on-demand-**by-package** path: `add_provider(install_spec, …)` plus a declarative `uitk.external_app_providers` entry-point group; on a launch miss the handler installs untried providers and re-discovers before failing (`_bootstrap_providers`, once per provider per session), with a DCC-host guard so it never pip-installs into a live `maya.exe`/`blender.exe`. So a host points at the *provider package* once (or just depends on it) instead of carrying a per-app `(name, module, entry)` table. Tests: `test_external_app_handler.py` — install-spec-from-dist, hide-gate partitioning, context-visibility (hidden/shown/empty/still-launchable), provider discovery + bootstrap (install-then-launch, once-per-session, present-not-reinstalled); 54/54 offscreen.

- **2026-06-24 `OptionBox` — inline `ValueOption` now renders flush-left against the wrapped widget (the default order was defined twice; only one had `"value"`).** Follow-up to the `Slider`/`ValueOption` work below: the value field was meant to sit ahead of every icon button (`OptionBox._option_order` starts with `"value"`), but in practice it rendered to the **right** of the buttons. Cause: the default order is defined in two places — `OptionBox.__init__` (updated) and `OptionBoxManager.__init__` (missed) — and the manager passes its own list to `OptionBox(option_order=…)`, overriding the widget default. So a value+toggle option box laid out `[widget][toggle][value]`. Fix: prepend `"value"` to the manager's default too (the two lists now match). Also folded the four duplicated `replace=True` "remove existing options of this type" blocks (set_action/set_toggle/set_reset/add_value) onto one `_remove_options(predicate)` helper while here. Test: `test_value_option.py::test_value_field_sits_left_of_icon_buttons` (fail-before/pass-after — value's layout index < a toggle's). Option-box/value/slider suites green offscreen (129).

- **2026-06-24 New `Slider` widget + reusable `ValueOption` option-box plugin (the "interactive value").** Two reusable primitives the HDR Manager's viewport-preview control needed, built into uitk rather than the panel. (1) **`Slider`** (`widgets/slider.py`) — `QSlider` + `MenuMixin` / `OptionBoxMixin` / `AttributesMixin`, mirroring the other input widgets (`ComboBox`/`SpinBox`); there was no uitk slider before, so panels used a raw `QSlider` with no option box. Horizontal by default; registered in `DEFAULT_INCLUDE` (`widgets.slider`). (2) **`ValueOption`** (`widgets/optionBox/options/value.py`) — a *non-button* option: a compact, button-less `SpinBox` field that mirrors the wrapped widget's value two-way and live (drag the widget → field updates; type in the field → widget updates *and emits*, so downstream slots still fire). Reusable across any widget with `value()`/`setValue()` + `valueChanged` (slider, spin box, dial); inherits the wrapped widget's range/step/decimals (int for a slider). Fluent entry `option_box.add_value(width=…, decimals=…, suffix=…)`; public `refresh()` re-syncs after a signal-blocked programmatic set. Supporting change: `OptionBox._update_sizing` now honors an `option.square` flag (default `True`) — a `ValueOption` (`square=False`) keeps its own width instead of being forced to the icon-square `h×h`; `ValueOption` is slotted ahead of the icon buttons in `_option_order`/`_TYPE_TO_KEY`. Tests: `test_slider.py` (4), `test_value_option.py` (6 — initial mirror, both sync directions, no-echo-loop, int decimals, non-square sizing) against the real `Slider`+`OptionBox` wrap; full option-box suite green offscreen (362). Verified end-to-end by loading a real panel through the Switchboard compiled loader (customwidget resolves via the registry; value field syncs 750→300→123).

- **2026-06-24 `MouseTracking` — kill the per-`MouseMove` grab churn (drag perf + cleaner handoff); no gesture-semantics change.** During a grabbed drag, `track()` opened with `_release_mouse_for_widgets(self._mouse_over)`, which clears `_mouse_owner` for the widget it releases — so `_grab_widget`'s `if widget is self._mouse_owner: return` guard never held for the steady state, and the widget under the cursor was `releaseMouse()`/`grabMouse()`-churned on **every** move (each release posts a native capture-change — `ReleaseCapture` on Win32). Confirmed live via `UITK_INPUT_LOG`: `grab migrated to 'main'` ×12, `'i015'` ×11, … one record per move while stationary. Fix: release only the widgets the cursor actually LEFT (`self._mouse_over - new_mouse_over`), so staying on a widget is a no-op and the cross-widget handoff (the QSS `:hover` path) still fires on a real change. Also dropped the ungated per-grab `logger.info("Grabbing mouse for widget: …")` (+ its `objectName()`) that ran on every move even with logging off — the gated `_grab_widget` "grab migrated" debug already covers it. Regression: `test_events.py::TestMouseTrackingDragHoverHandoff::test_no_grab_churn_when_cursor_stays_on_widget` (fail-before/pass-after; asserts the spy + `_mouse_owner`, not the OS grab). events + marking-menu suites green offscreen (99). **Scope:** perf/robustness cleanup — does NOT fix the "combobox/checkbox won't change in a window launched from a leaf" symptom, which the silent input log shows happens after the menu hides with the grab already released (cause is in the launched-window phase, not the live handoff).
- **2026-06-21 `MarkingMenu` — clean mouse-grab handoff to standalone windows launched from a leaf (fixes "the launched panel is input-dead until I tap the activation key again").** Field symptom: launching a tool window from a marking-menu leaf left the *entire* window unable to receive clicks (not just comboboxes), and tapping the activation key (show→hide) restored it. Root cause: `_activation_key_held` was cleared only on the physical key release (`_on_activation_release`) and in `_show_window`, but the **leaf-click launch path** (`_handle_widget_action` → `hide()`, then the leaf's slot opens the window) goes through neither — so when the key-release was missed (focus jumps to the launched window), the flag stayed set and the hidden menu's re-grab guards (`mousePressEvent`, `_do_pending_hide`) kept/re-acquired the mouse grab, starving the new window. `hide()` also released a grab only when `mouseGrabber() is self`, missing a grab `MouseTracking` had migrated onto a leaf button. Fix: `hide()` now clears `_activation_key_held` (ending the gesture so the re-grab guards can't fire once hidden) and calls `_release_input_grab()`, which releases a grab held by the menu **or any child button** (`isAncestorOf`); `hideEvent` uses the same release as its safety net. This is exactly the cleanup the activation-key tap performed manually. Test: `test_marking_menu_chord_release.py::MarkingMenuHideRelinquishesControl` (`hide()` clears the held flag + releases a self/child grab; an unrelated grabber is left alone). **Live Maya confirmation warranted** — the missed-key-release race is live-only.
- **2026-06-21 `ComboBox` — first click in the dropdown no longer lost when the host window isn't active.** Field report: "sometimes I can't select a value in a combobox dropdown — I have to re-focus the window (or reopen the list) for it to take; happens across multiple panels." Root-caused (read-only audit) to **window activation**: these combos commonly live in windows shown *without* activation — option-box / dropdown menus use `Qt.Tool | WA_ShowWithoutActivating` ([menu.py](uitk/uitk/widgets/menu.py)), and a DCC-hosted panel may not be the foreground window — and on Windows the **first click into a popup of a non-active window is consumed activating that window** rather than selecting the row (the "re-focus fixes it" tell). `ComboBox.showPopup` now calls new `_activate_host_window()` before opening the popup: it activates `self.window()` *only when it isn't already active* (guarded on `isActiveWindow`, so no focus churn in the normal case), so the popup's click lands on the item. Tests: `test_comboBox.py::ActivateHostWindowBeforePopup` (activates when the host is inactive / no-op when active / safe when there's no window) — asserting the deterministic product behavior, **not** the OS focus outcome (unreliable under the offscreen QPA). **Live Maya/Blender confirmation still warranted** — the activation race is OS-level and can't be reproduced headless.

- **2026-06-21 `OptionBox` init perf — Phase 1: stop wasting per-widget work during `register_children` (no behavior change; measured halving of `Menu` construction in dense panels).** A dense tentacle panel wraps dozens of widgets via `widget.option_box.menu.add(...)`, each running `OptionBox.wrap` synchronously at register time. Four safe, headless-verifiable wins (the bigger `Menu`-chrome deferral is deliberately held for a later, live-DCC-verified phase): **(1) Non-creating menu probe** — `OptionBoxManager._find_existing_option_box` and the `container` fallback probed `widget.menu` directly, whose lazy `MenuMixin` descriptor *creates* a standalone context `Menu` as a side effect; the always-False inner check (`Menu` has no `option_box` attr) meant this was pure waste. Both sites now use the non-creating `getattr(widget, "has_menu", False)` check. **Measured: `Menu` objects built over a 40-widget dense build dropped 80→40** (every wasteful context menu eliminated), and the wrapped widgets stay menu-less. **(2) Skip dead QSettings** — a state-less `ActionOption`/`MenuOption` (the ubiquitous case) constructed a `SettingsManager`/`QSettings` and read `current_state` that is only ever used `if self._states`; `_init_settings` now early-returns when there are no states, and `set_states` lazily initializes persistence so runtime-added states still save (**0/40 MenuOptions now open QSettings**). The redundant trailing `_init_settings()`/`_load_state()` in `ActionOption.__init__` were removed as dead code. **(3) Hoist per-call allocations** — `ButtonOption.create_widget` re-`class`-defined `OptionButton` on every call (now module-scope in `_options.py`), and `OptionBox._sort_options` rebuilt 7 local imports + the `_type_to_key` map on every `wrap()`/`_rebuild_layout()` (now a module-level `_TYPE_TO_KEY` built once from top-level imports — the option modules never import `_optionBox`, so no cycle). **(4) Misc** — the `container` property's unconditional `time.perf_counter()` (ran on every access) dropped; `_apply_border_styling` now appends border-trim fragments idempotently via `_append_style_once`, fixing a latent bug where re-wrapping a widget accumulated duplicate `border-*-width:0px` fragments (and skipping the redundant `setStyleSheet` re-polish). Regression coverage: `test_optionBox.py::TestOptionBoxInitPerfRegressions` (no context-menu materialized on wrap — mechanism-proven fail-before/pass-after; state-less option skips QSettings while stateful initializes it incl. the runtime `set_states` path; idempotent border trim). uitk option-box / slot-init / menu / switchboard / persistence suites green offscreen (PySide6 6.10.1).

- **2026-06-20 `ExpandableList` — sublists reliably collapse when the list is no longer shown (top-level window hide AND containing-MainWindow hide), without touching the marking menu's own internals.** Reproduced + root-caused by driving a FRESH live Maya (`MayaConnection`, never an open session): open the main lower submenu's Workspace list → hover a directory with subfolders (e.g. `sourceimages`) → a sublist opens → on the next submenu show the sublist is still visible. **The decisive live finding:** Qt delivers a `hideEvent` to a widget's *direct* children when it hides, but NOT to a *deep descendant* — and `list000` sits several layout levels under the submenu UI. So when the marking menu hides the submenu UI (`_current_widget.hide()` on navigation — a non-window child added via `addWidget`→`setParent(self)`), the deep list never gets a `hideEvent`, its `_force_hide_all` never runs, and the sublists (reparented to `self.window()` = the still-visible menu window) linger; `showChildren` restores them on the next show. Everything funnels through one `_force_hide_all()`, triggered by every hide signal the list can actually observe: (1) `hideEvent` (the list itself hides); (2) `_watch_window_hide` — an event filter on the top-level window for `Hide`/`WindowBlocked` (full dismiss / spontaneous host reclaim / modal dialog; `WindowDeactivate` deliberately excluded — DCC overlays lose activation during normal chord nav); (3) `_watch_ui_hide` — connects `_force_hide_all` to the nearest containing uitk `MainWindow`'s `on_hide` signal (the submenu UI emits it from its `hideEvent`, covering navigation where the deep list gets no event); plus a `showEvent` `_force_hide_all()` reset so any missed hide can't leak forward. **An earlier interim attempt that installed event filters on the *whole ancestor chain* (incl. `TclMaya`/`staticWindow`) was reverted — it touched the marking menu's own event stream and broke the list.** The window watch installs exactly one filter (on the top-level, as before); `on_hide` is a targeted signal hookup that touches no menu internals. **Live-verified against the real `TclMaya` menu:** the list builds and opens normally, and `ui.on_hide`, a modal dialog, and `tcl.hide()` each collapse the sublist; reshow is clean. Regression coverage (mechanism-level, since offscreen Qt — unlike live — *does* deliver the deep-descendant hideEvent and would mask the hook): `test_submenu_ui_on_hide_collapses_reparented_sublists`, `test_toplevel_window_hide_collapses_through_nonwindow_ui`, `test_modal_dialog_blocking_window_collapses_sublists`, `test_show_resets_any_sublist_that_survived_a_missed_hide`, retarget test. Full uitk suite 1948 passed.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` cleanup — removed the gesture-diagnostics scaffolding (kept every real fix), and closed the resolver-fix test gap.** The `_diag` / `enable_diagnostics` / `_widget_id` / `_safe_int` trace subsystem (~340 lines: the framework + 53 inline `MM_*` trace points woven through every gesture handler + two orphaned `*_snapshot` helpers + the duplicate `_safe_int`/`_to_int` coercion) was scaffolding for the live-only marking-menu hunt.
