With the real fixes landed and pinned by behaviour tests, the trace is gone, and a vestigial deferred-show mechanism (`_delayed_show_ui` + its always-`None` `_pending_ui` flag, superseded by `_pending_show_timer`/`_perform_transition`) and the write-only `_setup_complete` flag were removed as dead code; the live transition state (`_pending_transition_ui`/`_widget`/`_transitioning_to_window`) is now declared at class level instead of read via defensive `getattr` (`_marking_menu.py` 2421→1974 lines). **Kept, unchanged:** the resolver fix (`ui_name_resolves` / `UiHandler.can_resolve`), the `_owned_item_at` `childAt` fallback, the `_action_dispatched` latch, and the chord-release tolerance timer. `test_marking_menu_diagnostics.py` deleted; tentacle's separate `_ClickDebugger` slot/mouse tracer decoupled from the removed API (its own tracing kept). New regression coverage the trace had been standing in for: `uitk/test/test_ui_handler.py` (base `can_resolve`: registered `.ui` stem + `#submenu` stripping + empty/None) and `mayatk/test/test_maya_ui_handler.py` (`MayaUiHandler.can_resolve` reports every `MENU_MAPPING` native menu — incl. the regression's `key` — while delegating real stems to the base). Full uitk suite green.

- **2026-06-20 `SwitchboardWidgetMixin` / `UiHandler` — nav-button click resolution recognises handler-built UIs (native Maya menus), so releasing over `key` opens the key main menu again (regression from 2cc9858).** THE actual root cause (the marking-menu `as_window`/latch work was the wrong layer and is reverted). A category nav button like `key` is wired so **hover → `key#submenu`** (the uitk overlay preview) and **release → `key`** (a native Maya menu built on demand by mayatk's `MayaUiHandler` from `MayaNativeMenus.MENU_MAPPING` — not a `.ui` file). The Phase-5 push (`2cc9858`) rewrote `menu_button_target_name` to prefer the base `target` only when `is_registered_ui(target)` — and that matches **file stems only**, so `is_registered_ui("key")` is always False → the resolver fell back to `key#submenu` and a release showed the overlay (which then re-centered/"shifted" and vanished with the menu) instead of opening the native menu. Fix (in the resolver, where it belongs): new `SwitchboardWidgetMixin.ui_name_resolves(name)` = registered file stem OR a name the active UI handler can build, queried via a new non-building `UiHandler.can_resolve(name)` hook (base = file stem; `MayaUiHandler.can_resolve` adds its `MENU_MAPPING` native-menu names). `menu_button_target_name` now uses `ui_name_resolves` for the base target, so `key` (and every category button) resolves to the native menu — which is untagged → opens standalone via the existing `show(menu, force=is_standalone)` dispatch. No marking-menu dispatch change needed. Verified live (`MayaConnection`): `ui_name_resolves("key")` True, `menu_button_target_name(key_btn)` → `"key"` (was `"key#submenu"`), `_resolve_button_menu` → the native `key` menu with `is_standalone=True`. Regression: `test_marking_menu.py::test_click_prefers_handler_resolvable_base_over_submenu` (+ `test_click_falls_back_to_submenu_when_base_unresolvable`). **Reverted** the same-day wrong-layer marking-menu changes (`MarkingMenu.show(as_window=…)`, the `_handle_menu_item_release(all_released=…)` latch reset, and the no-op guard add/remove) — none reintroduced; the dispatch is back to `show(menu, force=is_standalone)`.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` — THE live root cause: `QApplication.widgetAt` misses over the translucent overlay; release + press hit-tests now fall back to geometric `childAt`.** Reproduced live by driving a fresh Maya (mayatk `MayaConnection`) and tracing the real gesture: with the cursor squarely inside a menu button's rect, `QApplication.widgetAt(globalPos)` returns **None** — its OS `WindowFromPoint` falls through the marking menu's `WA_TranslucentBackground` layered window's transparent pixels — while `current_ui.childAt(localPos)` correctly returns the button. So BOTH the release hit-test (`_resolve_release_target`) and the press click-vs-chord classification (`_is_menu_item_press`) missed and the gesture fell through to `_sync_menu_to_state`, navigating away instead of clicking — "the menu item under the cursor never registers a click, the menu just shifts/switches", pixel/alpha-dependent (hence "needs several clicks"). Fix: new shared `_owned_item_at(pos, current_ui)` helper that tries `widgetAt` first (the only probe that resolves a *logical* descendant — an ExpandableList sublist) then a geometric `childAt` fallback; both hit-test sites route through it. This is why the offscreen tests never caught it — they *mock* `widgetAt`, so the real OS miss was invisible. Verified end-to-end in live Maya across all three release-routing paths (menu-grab `mouseReleaseEvent`, child-grab `child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent`, clean-vs-imperfect both-button release): chord → hover `key` → release both → `key#submenu` → pick `playback` → `playback#submenu`. (The childAt fallback is the real, kept fix; a no-op guard briefly added here was wrong-axis and has been reverted — see the resolver entry above for the actual `key`-opens-its-menu fix.) Regression tests (which *would* have caught it — they assert childAt resolves when widgetAt returns None): `test_release_resolves_via_childAt_when_widgetAt_misses`, `test_press_classified_as_item_via_childAt_when_widgetAt_misses`, `test_owned_item_at_prefers_widgetat_then_falls_back_to_childat`; `test_genuine_chord_still_navigates` updated to null BOTH probes for a true empty-space chord. Marking-menu suites 118 passed.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` — chord-release ORDER fix: an owned-item release dispatches immediately; the tolerance governs navigation only (supersedes the same-day tolerance entry below).** The earlier tolerance fix put the partial-release deferral *ahead* of the owned-item dispatch in both release handlers — so releasing **both** buttons over a menu item (e.g. the `key` MenuButton in `maya#startmenu`) deferred the click into the tolerance window, the timer then navigated the menu to the remaining-button menu (the "stays open and shifts"), and the click was never registered (single-button worked because it has no partial). Verified against the proven `git show 3b7213e~1` (v1.0.66) source: that code resolved and fired the owned item **first**, with NO wait for the other held button, and consulted the chord-release timer **only** for a release over empty overlay (the "switch menus by releasing a button" gesture). Fix: reorder `mouseReleaseEvent` / `child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent` to dispatch an owned-item release immediately (keeping the `_resolve_release_target` event-then-cursor hit-test and the `_action_dispatched` single-shot latch that swallows the trailing release of the pair); `_defer_partial_or_settle` is now reached only after ruling out an owned item, so the tolerance applies to navigation alone. New coverage: `test_both_button_partial_release_over_item_fires_immediately`, `test_menu_grab_partial_release_over_item_fires_immediately`, `test_chord_release_dispatches_once_on_nav_button`, the navigation deferral tests re-pointed to the empty-overlay case, and a faithful tentacle GUI-Maya repro (`test_both_button_release_over_menu_button_registers_click`). Marking-menu suites 106 passed.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` — restore chord-release tolerance: imperfect both-button release no longer "stays open and shifts" (regression).** A real both-buttons (L+R chord) release is imperfect — the two buttons lift a few ms apart — so the first release arrives with the other still held (a "partial"). The rewrite treated that partial as an immediate menu *switch* (`_sync_menu_to_state` → the remaining single-button menu), so the menu shifted and the item under the cursor never clicked; single-button has no partial, so it always worked. Fix: restore v1.0.66's tolerance timer — a partial release is **deferred** (`CHORD_RELEASE_TOLERANCE_MS`, 75ms) instead of navigating; the final all-up release within the window selects the item under the cursor, and only a button held *past* the tolerance navigates (an intentional switch). The hit-test on the final release still resolves at the event position then the live cursor (`_resolve_release_target`). Testing fidelity: the prior tests fired both releases instantly (no gap) and so never exercised the tolerance — new `test_real_timing_*` (uitk, real event loop) and `test_imperfect_both_button_release_*` (tentacle GUI-Maya) drive a real timing gap; mutation-verified.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` — Maya release hit-test falls back to the live cursor.** In Maya a chord release's `event.globalPos()` can resolve to the menu background rather than the item the pointer is over; the final-release dispatch now also probes `QCursor.pos()`. Folded into the tolerance fix above. A chord (multi-button) release in Maya reports an `event.globalPos()` that resolves to the menu *background* rather than the item the pointer is over, so the hit-test missed, the dispatch was lost, and the release fell through to `_sync_menu_to_state` (the shift). Commit 1dab9ae had moved the release hit-test from `QCursor.pos()` (v1.0.66) to `event.globalPos()`. Fix: new `_resolve_release_target` hit-tests at the event position first (Blender drift-immunity) then **falls back to the live cursor** (`QCursor.pos()` — what the user is pointing at), recovering the item; both release handlers route through it. Regression test `test_maya_chord_release_recovers_item_at_live_cursor` (mutation-verified by dropping the fallback). Builds on the same-day chord-dispatch hardening below.

- **2026-06-20 `MarkingMenu` — chord-release dispatch hardening (immediate-fire + single-shot latch).** A chord release (`F12|Left|Right`) arrives as **two** `MouseButtonRelease` events a few ms apart — one per button — whereas a single button has only one. Two independent bugs made the double-button case misbehave where single-button worked: (1) **dead click via the child grab** — during a drag the grab migrates to the leaf `QPushButton` (the `should_capture_mouse` opt-out is commented out), so the release lands on `child_mouseButtonReleaseEvent`, which the `_sync_menu_to_state` rewrite (3b7213e) had left a no-op pass-through; (2) **double dispatch on the trailing release** — the first release dispatches the item, but if the action doesn't hide the menu (a nav `MenuButton` opens a submenu and stays visible), the *trailing* release lands on the freshly-shown submenu and fires a *second*, unwanted action. v1.0.66's `_chord_release_timer` had coalesced the pair into one decision; the rewrite dropped it. Fix: (a) both release sites route an owned-item release through one shared `_handle_menu_item_release` that fires `_handle_widget_action` **immediately** (the proven pre-rewrite dispatch — fixes the dead child-grab click); (b) a per-gesture **single-shot latch** (`_action_dispatched`, re-armed on press/activation, never on `show()`) makes a chord release dispatch **exactly once**, like a single-button release. Chord *navigation* (release over empty overlay) is untouched. Covered by `test_marking_menu_chord_release.py` (10, mutation-verified — the double-dispatch and immediate-fire tests each fail when their fix is reverted); marking-menu suites 32 passed.

- **2026-06-20 Test — plain-`QLineEdit` persistence coverage (`test_persistence_hardening.py::TestLineEditPersistence`).** Text widgets had no cross-session persistence test; this adds the line-edit analogue of the combobox round-trip coverage (a registered plain `QLineEdit` saves on `textChanged` and restores its value, including an intentionally-cleared empty value). No behavior change — confirms the existing restore path works for plain text widgets.

- **2026-06-19 `BridgeSlotsBase` — fix Output Dir field right-shifted / not filling the row.** The option-box-wrapped path field rendered far right with a gap after its label (reported live on the Unity bridge's "Unity Project" field). Root cause: `_build_output_dir_row` created the `QLineEdit` **parentless** and wrapped it before adding it to the row, so the option-box container briefly showed as a top-level widget — `OptionBoxContainer.showEvent` then scheduled a `_refit_to_content` that collapsed it to its `sizeHint` and absolutely-positioned it *after* it had been reparented into the row, freezing the stale geometry. Fix: parent the edit into the row layout (with stretch) **before** calling `_configure_output_dir_options`, so the wrap reparents it in place via `replaceWidget` (preserving the stretch factor) while it is layout-managed from the start. No core option-box change needed; verified by an offscreen width probe (field now fills from label to row edge for both the recent+browse and recent+menu variants) + the uitk option/bridge suite (157).
- **2026-06-19 `BridgeSlotsBase` — Output Dir row uses option-box buttons instead of a "..." button.** The shared output-dir/path row (every bridge + workflow panel: unity / marmoset / substance / blender / metashape / photogrammetry) now carries uitk **option-box** icon buttons on the field: a persisted **recent-values** history (`settings_key=<LOG_TAG>_output_dir_recent`, path-aware `display_format="auto"`, auto-recorded) + a **directory browse** action (records its pick). The bare `...` push-button and the module-level `_pick_dir` helper are gone. New override seam `_configure_output_dir_options(edit)` (default = recent + browse) lets a subclass customise the field's buttons; shared helpers `_add_recent_output_dir_option`, `_pick_output_dir`, `_record_output_dir` (so any programmatic `setText` — browse, a subclass 'New Project' — keeps the history in sync), `_output_dir_browse_title`. Verified end-to-end via the extapps panel suite (400 passed) which constructs these panels for real.

- **2026-06-19 Feature** — **`MainWindow.run_when_ready(callback)` — run a callback once the window's child widgets are registered (first show), or immediately if already shown.** A slot class's `__init__` can run before its child widgets exist on `self.ui` (the switchboard may build the slots instance eagerly during construction via `slot_source=`), so cross-widget setup (presets, footer wiring, label colours) must wait. This encapsulates the `is_initialized ? now : on_first_show` idiom that extapps' texture-map panels now share (replacing two hand-rolled copies; mayatk's `lightmap_baker` uses an equivalent `QTimer.singleShot` and could migrate). Per-widget setup still belongs in the `*_init` hooks. Tests: `test_mainwindow.py::TestRunWhenReady` (defers until first show; runs immediately when already initialized).
- **2026-06-19 Fix** — **An explicitly-passed `slot_source` is now honored even when the class name doesn't follow the `<ui-basename>` convention (`Slots._find_slots_class(..., allow_sole_fallback=True)`).** Slot resolution matches a UI's basename against derived class/file names (`packer` → `PackerSlots`/`Packer`/`packer.py`/…). That's the right SSoT mechanism for multi-UI apps, but it silently ignored a single explicit `slot_source=SomeSlots` whose name didn't match — e.g. extapps' de-stuttered `packer.ui` paired with the (then) `MapPackerSlots` class resolved to **nothing**, so `get_slots_instance` returned `None` and the panel loaded slot-less (`ui.slots is None`). `_find_slots_class` now falls back, **after** name/file matching, to the **sole** registered slot class when exactly one is registered — the unambiguous single-panel case. **Gated** behind `allow_sole_fallback`: only the slot-*creation* callers (`get_slots_instance`, `_add_to_placeholder`) — which already hold a real, registered UI — opt in; the UI-*name* resolver (`_resolve_ui_using_slots`) leaves it off, so an unknown `loaded_ui.<name>` still raises `AttributeError` instead of fabricating a phantom UI from the sole class. Restricted to the single-class case: multi-UI apps (tentacle) register many slot classes, so the fallback never fires and name-matching still disambiguates as before. Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestExplicitSlotBinding` (sole class binds despite name mismatch; strict lookup never fabricates a UI; name-match still wins with >1 class; ambiguous multi-class no-match returns `None`). Switchboard/dynamic-slot/loader/mainwindow suites green.
- **2026-06-19 Fix** — **Select comboboxes now persist their value across sessions — populating a `ComboBox` no longer clobbers the stored selection (`ComboBox.clear/addItem/addItems/insertItem/insertItems` are signal-safe).** Root cause of "the combobox doesn't restore across sessions": Qt-native population moves the current index off `-1` and fires `currentIndexChanged`, and a combo registered for state persistence **saves** on that signal. When a panel populates a combo *outside* the signal-blocked `init_slot` wrap — e.g. the map-packer's channel combos, filled via `addItems` in the slot-class `__init__` — reopening the panel re-ran `addItems`, which saved the transient index `0` **before** restore read the store, wiping the user's selection (the named preset survived, but the per-channel value combos reset → "restored preset but no actual settings restored"). `restore_state = True` was necessary but not sufficient: the value was already gone by restore time. uitk's own `ComboBox.add()` already avoided this via `@Signals.blockSignals`; this extends the same protection to the Qt-native population API by wrapping each structural mutator in a `_silenced()` context that blocks the combo's signals for the span of the mutation (saving/restoring the prior blocked state, so nesting inside `add()` / `init_slot` never unblocks early). Population is now inert with respect to state and slots — the single emit a caller wants (the restored/default value) still arrives via the normal restore flow, matching `add()`'s long-standing behavior. Fixes the map-packer and every other `addItems`-populated select combo across the ecosystem in one place. Complements the 2026-06-16 deferred-batch `suppress_save` fix (which covered `*_init` population) with a widget-level guarantee that holds regardless of *where* the combo is populated. Regression: `test/test_persistence_hardening.py::TestComboPopulateClobber` (populate writes no state; cross-session round-trip survives repopulation — both fail without the fix). Combo/persistence/loader/menu/option-box suites 714 green offscreen.
- **2026-06-19 DRY** — **`BridgeSlotsBase` now ships a default `header_init`, so bridge / workflow slots declare their header menu as *data, not code*.** Every DCC-bridge and workflow slot used to hand-roll the same `header_init` (a "Utilities" separator + `menu.add(...)` buttons + `set_help_text(fmt(...))`). That boilerplate is now a single default on `BridgeSlotsBase`, driven by two class-attr hooks: `HEADER_MENU_ITEMS` — a tuple of `(label, objectName, tooltip, handler_method_name)`, defaulting to Open Templates / Refresh / Clear Log — and `HELP_SPEC` — the `fmt()` kwargs dict (or `None`). A bridge with a different menu sets the tuple (unity → Open Unity Project; rizom → UV-editor + scripts); a panel that needs runtime-computed items overrides the `header_menu_items()` hook (the photogrammetry panels, whose tooltips carry the engine label). Help is the `help_spec()` hook (default returns `HELP_SPEC`). ~9 subclasses across mayatk / blendertk / extapps dropped their `header_init` for a data declaration. New `test_bridge_slots_header.py` (6) pins the mechanism: default items + wiring, custom override, dynamic method override, no-help-when-absent, and a missing-handler error.
- **2026-06-19 Feature/Fix** — **Preset combos now remember the active preset across sessions, flag unsaved edits, and Refresh actually reverts (`PresetManager`, `wire_combo`, `ComboBox.current_text_suffix`, `bridge/slots.py`).** Three related preset gaps, all rooted in the combo having *no notion of an "active preset"* — it drove everything off the transient `currentIndex` and persisted nothing:
  - **Active preset restored between sessions.** `PresetManager.active_preset` (backed by `pythontk.PresetStore.active`'s `.active` sidecar) records the selected preset. On `wire_combo`, the selection is restored **with signals blocked — no values are re-applied** (the widgets restore themselves from QSettings; only the *selection* needs restoring, which is the whole point). The preset combo was never registered with `StateManager`, so it previously persisted nothing; and persisting the **name** (not the combo *index*) is immune to the list reordering that rename/add/delete cause.
  - **Modified ("dirty") marker.** `is_modified()` compares the live values (`_capture_values`, the shared SSoT `save` also uses) against the active preset's stored snapshot over the preset's keys (overlay semantics). When they diverge the combo paints a `" *"` suffix on the *displayed* current text via the new reusable `ComboBox.current_text_suffix` (item data / `itemText` stay the raw name, so load/rename/delete are unaffected). `refresh_modified_state()` + `on_modified_changed()` observers fire only on a transition; `connect_value_widgets()` auto-wires the marker for menu/standalone widgets, and the bridge wires it for semantic-mode params via `connect_changed`. Save (overwrite) and Refresh clear it.
  - **Refresh now works.** The Refresh action re-applies `mgr.active_preset` instead of `combo.itemText(currentIndex)`. The index-based version silently no-oped whenever the index was `-1` (after a session restore, or any state reset) — which read as "Refresh is broken" in the live app.
  - The combo shows a `"Presets…"` placeholder when nothing is active; `_reset_to_defaults` clears the active pointer + marker. `WidgetComboBox` already inherits header support from `ComboBox` (`add_header`/`header=`), but a header force-resets the index to -1 per pick — incompatible with the dirty marker — so a placeholder is used instead. Tests: `test_preset_manager.py` (+10: active persists across managers, restore-without-apply, marker set/clear on edit/save/refresh, Refresh-at-index-`-1` regression, placeholder, delete clears active; widget-state + semantic). pythontk `PresetStore.active` change ships alongside.

- **2026-06-18 Fix** — **`ExpandableList` child sublists no longer survive a hide/show with the list expanded.** Two distinct causes:
  - **Show side (synthetic Enter reopen):** `hideEvent`→`_force_hide_all` already collapsed sublists on hide, but Qt then delivers a synthetic `Enter` to the item under a stationary cursor when the list reappears, and that Enter ran the normal hover-to-expand path — silently restoring the previously-open sublist. Fix: a show-time latch (`_suppress_open_pos`, armed in the root list's `showEvent`) gates the Enter-driven open in `eventFilter` and clears the first time the cursor is seen at a *different* position, so genuine hover still expands but the show-time synthetic Enter is ignored. Direct/programmatic `_handle_widget_enter_event` calls bypass the gate (unchanged).
  - **Hide side (explicit dismiss did nothing):** `hide()` used to *early-return* while any sublist was visible (`_has_any_visible_sublist` guard). Because sublists are reparented to the window (not Qt children of the list), an explicit `list.hide()` then closed **nothing** — neither the list nor the sublist. `hide()` now force-collapses the hierarchy (`_force_hide_all`) and then hides; the now-unused `_has_any_visible_sublist` guard helper was removed.
  - Internal cleanup: the duplicated "resolve the root list" expression in `leaveEvent` now goes through a shared `_get_root_list()` helper.
  - Regression tests: `test_sublist_stays_collapsed_after_window_reshow`, `test_auto_open_resumes_after_cursor_moves`, `test_explicit_hide_collapses_open_sublists`.

- **2026-06-17 Fix** — **Marking-menu leaf clicks over Blender no longer go "dead" when the menu holds the mouse grab (`MarkingMenu` click-vs-chord classification + release-at-event-position).** Closes the leaf-click item left open by the grab-policy fix: a leaf — *Average* / *Set To Face* / … — needing up to four clicks, Blender only. **Reproduced + diagnosed live** (`tentacle/test/blender/normals_multiclick_check.py`, real Blender + the real buttons): with the grab held by the menu the named leaves fired **0/3** and the menu jumped to `cameras#startmenu`; with the fix, **3/3**. Mechanism: reaching `normals` through a *chord* (hold key + mouse button → main/edit → Normals) grabs the mouse via `_transfer_mouse_control`, so the menu — not the button — holds the grab. A leaf's left **press** is then delivered to `MarkingMenu`, where `_sync_menu_to_state` re-resolves `buttons=LeftButton` (key held) as the `F12|LeftButton` **chord** and navigates away before the leaf can fire. (In Maya the button consumes the press so the menu never sees it. Live, the activation poller's 0.02s `MouseTracking.track()` periodically migrates the grab to the button under the cursor, which lets a click through — so each click is a *race*, hence "up to four".) Two-part source fix: **(1)** `mousePressEvent` now treats a **lone-button press over an interactive descendant of the current start/submenu** as a click (early-return; dispatched on release via `_handle_widget_action`), never a chord — the discriminator is position + button count (`_is_menu_item_press` / `count_buttons == 1`), which already excludes a real chord (second concurrent button, or a press on empty overlay), so it correctly applies **even mid-chord** — that was the missing half (an earlier `_chord_gesture` gate wrongly skipped exactly the chord-reached case and is removed). **(2)** `mouseReleaseEvent` resolves the click target at the **release event's** position (`event.globalPos()`) instead of the live `QCursor.pos()`, which drifts off the leaf between the physical release and the pumped handler under Blender's timer-driven loop (equals the cursor under Maya's native loop → no behavior change there). Deterministic guard: `test/test_marking_menu_leaf_click.py` (leaf fires while the menu holds the grab; release dispatches at the event position despite a drifted cursor; genuine chord still navigates). Full marking-menu/overlay/events surface green; entire uitk suite 1882 passed.

- **2026-06-17 Fix** — **Marking-menu submenus no longer collapse to an ~18px sliver that renders detached from the gesture ("submenu shows in the wrong location") — `MainWindow.fit_height_to_content`.** A submenu's content (an `ExpandableList`, nested `Region`s) is **absolutely positioned** in a layout-less central, so the window exposes *no* layout height: both `minimumSizeHint().height()` and `sizeHint().height()` are `0`. The original `fit_height_to_content` hit `if target <= 0: return` and left such a window at its natural `_init_ui` size — correct. The recent `_content_min_height()` change (added to floor `adjust_height_by` against an under-reporting central) was also wired into `fit_height_to_content` *as the resize target*: it returns the tiny **laid-out** part only (`~18px` for a lone nav button), which is `> 0`, so the early return was skipped and the submenu was resized to 18px — its real content then overflowed/rendered outside the collapsed window. `_content_min_height` is now applied **only as a floor** once a positive target exists (preserving the overlap protection); when both hints are `0` the window keeps its natural size. Maya/standalone *and* Blender share this path, so both were hit. Reproduced live (fresh Maya, `cameras#lower#submenu`: 18px→600px, content renders in place) and locked headless: `test/test_main_window_resize.py::TestFitHeightToContent::test_fit_does_not_collapse_when_layout_min_is_zero`. Resize/footer/collapsable/marking-menu/menu/visibility suites 259 green.

- **2026-06-17 Fix** — **Clicking a marking-menu nav launcher now opens its submenu instead of raising (`MarkingMenu._resolve_button_menu` / `_cached_ui`).** The click path resolved a `MenuButton`'s **bare** `target` (`"cameras"`), but a bare-target nav launcher (`target="cameras"`, `filterTags="lower"`) isn't itself a registered UI — only its composed submenu `"cameras#lower#submenu"` is. So `_cached_ui("cameras")` → `get_ui("cameras")` raised `AttributeError("Slot class 'cameras' not found")`, which propagated out of `mouseReleaseEvent` (so the grab was never released either): clicking an upper/lower nav region threw instead of launching the submenu, and the failed click read as "needs several clicks". Now `_resolve_button_menu` resolves via the shared `Switchboard.menu_button_target_name` SSoT (also used by the `menu_button_target_resolves` auto-hide check, so the click and hide paths can't drift): the registered **base `target`** is preferred — preserving the original click→base-panel behavior (e.g. the polygons component buttons open the tag-filtered `polygons` panel) — falling back to the composed `submenu_name()` (`"cameras#lower#submenu"`) when the bare target isn't itself a registered UI (the cameras/editors nav launchers). `_cached_ui` now returns `None` for an unregistered name (honouring its `Optional` contract) rather than letting the resolver raise — every caller guards on a falsy result. Reproduced + locked headless against the real Blender menu (`cameras`/`editors#startmenu`): `test/test_marking_menu.py::TestNavButtonMenuResolution` (submenu vs standalone resolution, no-raise on unregistered, caching). Marking-menu suites 220 green.

- **2026-06-17 Fix** — **`RecentValuesPopup` width regression test is no longer font-dependent (`test_optionBox.py::TestRecentValuesPopupWidthSizing`).** `test_adjustsize_widens_to_content_before_show` asserted the popup widened past a hardcoded `600px` — but the rendered width of the sample paths is font-dependent (574px at 9pt Segoe UI under pytest vs >1000px at the default font), so it failed deterministically wherever the test font was small. The popup itself sizes correctly (`adjustSize()` → `sizeHint`, which exceeds the grid content width). Reassert the actual intent font-independently: the popup width reached its content (grid) width and is well past the 150px minimum — still catches a genuine collapse-to-minimum regression without the magic pixel threshold.

- **2026-06-17 Fix** — **Marking-menu drag-time hover tracking is now host-aware so chord submenus reveal over Blender (`MouseTracking(buttons_provider=…)` + `MarkingMenu._host_mouse_buttons`).** A chord menu (`F12+LMB` → cameras, `F12+MMB` → editors) opens with the mouse grabbed (`_transfer_mouse_control`), and a Qt grab suppresses native `enterEvent`. The menu's `visible_on_mouse_over` `Region`s (the cameras/editors upper+lower nav clusters) depend on `MouseTracking.track()` to *synthesize* enter events for non-grabbable widgets during a grab — but `track()` is gated behind "a button is held", tested with `QApplication.mouseButtons()`, which is **blind to GHOST's mouse under Blender**. So during a Blender chord `track()` never ran, the Regions never revealed their nav buttons, and the upper/lower submenus "didn't launch" (and stale hover/grab state read as "click buttons more than once"). `MouseTracking` now takes an injectable `buttons_provider` (default `None` → queries `QApplication.mouseButtons()` **live at call time** — never cached, so patches/monkeypatches still apply); `MarkingMenu._host_mouse_buttons()` is the overridable hook wired into it (default = Qt, so Maya/standalone are byte-identical). The earlier speculative `mouseReleaseEvent` drop-grab (a wrong fix for the same symptom) is reverted — the grab is correctly *held* through the chord so `track()` can drive the reveal; it releases on the handled action / key-up as before. Live-verified on a fresh Blender (`tentacle/test/blender/cameras_track_check.py`: region reveals + hover opens `cameras#lower#submenu`); the Blender side that drives `track()` off its timer (GHOST never delivers `MouseMove` to the grabbed overlay) lives in `tentacle/tcl_blender.py`. Tests: `test_events.py::TestMouseTrackingDragHoverHandoff::{test_buttons_provider_overrides_qt_query, test_default_buttons_provider_reads_qt_live}`. Events/marking-menu/menu/resolver/visibility/option-box suites 262 green offscreen.

- **2026-06-16 Fix** — **Persistent widget settings no longer silently reset to defaults a few sessions later (`MainWindow.sync_widget_values`, `StateManager.save_value`, `Slots._process_deferred_widgets`).** Three independent ways a *default* could get written over a good value — each intermittent, so values "restored fine, then reset themselves" — are closed:
  1. **Cross-surface divergence (the main one).** A panel and its marking-menu surfaces (`<panel>`, `<panel>#submenu`, `<panel>#startmenu`) present the *same* controls but keep **separate per-surface QSettings namespaces** (`switchboard/<tagged_name>/…`). `sync_widget_values` only mirrored a change to a sibling surface that was **loaded *and* shown** at the time (`get_widget` reads `ui.widgets`, empty until a surface's first `showEvent`) — and it mirror-saved through the *current* UI's `StateManager`, i.e. into the wrong namespace. So a value set from the docked panel never reached an unopened marking-menu's store; reopening that surface a later session restored its stale/default copy. It now persists the value into **every** related surface's store directly (loaded or not) via the new `StateManager.save_value(key, value)` on a per-sibling branch (`_relative_state`, cached), and still mirrors onto any *live* sibling widget — but under that sibling's `suppress_save()` so the visual mirror can't ping-pong back into a save. (`sync_widget_values` now drives off relative *names*, so it no longer force-loads every sibling window on each change.)
  2. **Deferred-init default clobber.** The immediate `init_slot` path blocks a widget's signals around slot-init + restore; the **deferred batch** (`_process_deferred_widgets`) ran *unblocked*, so a widget whose `*_init` mutates its value (`addItems` flips a combo to index 0, `setChecked` fires `toggled`) persisted that post-init default **before** Phase-2 restore ran. Both phases now run inside `ui.state.suppress_save()`, matching the immediate path (restore-time slot firing is unchanged — still per `block_signals_on_restore`).
  3. **Combobox index transients.** `StateManager.save_value` skips a `-1` (no-selection) write for `currentIndexChanged` keys (a combo briefly reports `-1` while its model repopulates), and `apply` skips a stored index that outruns the current model (`value >= count()`) instead of letting it clamp/no-op and later persist the wrong index. Serialization is now a single chokepoint (`_coerce_for_store` + `save_value`, reused by `save`/`save_custom`).
  Regression tests in `test/test_persistence_hardening.py` (cross-surface store written for an unloaded sibling + restored on first open; deferred batch runs save-suppressed; `-1`/out-of-range combo guards). Persistence/state/switchboard/optionBox/marking-menu suites green (312 + 5 new).
- **2026-06-16 Fix** — **`MessageBox` action buttons (Ok / Cancel / …) are no longer cramped.** The popup's button-box buttons inherited the base `QAbstractButton` rule's `padding: 0px 1px`, so the modal's **Ok** button rendered with almost no breathing room. Added a `.MessageBox QPushButton` rule to the dark-theme QSS (`padding: 10px 28px; min-width: 72px; margin: 6px`) — generous padding on all sides plus margin off the dialog edge; hover/pressed states still inherit from the `QAbstractButton` rules. Label/host styling unchanged.
- **2026-06-16 Refactor** — **Severity colours now come from one SSoT (`pythontk.LoggingMixin.LOG_COLORS`).** `Footer.LEVEL_COLORS` (status-text severity) and `_html_style.PREFIX_STYLES` (the `Error:`/`Warning:`/`Note:`/`Result:` tokens that `MessageBox`/`TextViewBox` auto-colour) both previously hardcoded their own hex; they now derive from pythontk's logging palette (`_html_style.LOG_COLORS`, re-exported), so footers, message boxes, text views, and console logs share one colour scheme — change the palette in pythontk and it propagates everywhere. Literal fallbacks keep both usable if pythontk's logging module is unavailable in a minimal env. No public API change (the constants keep their names/shapes). Tests: `test_footer.py::test_level_colors_come_from_pythontk_log_colors`; footer + message/text suites 61 green offscreen.
- **2026-06-16 Feature** — **`Footer` status text is now colour-codeable by severity (`Footer.setStatusText/setText(text, level=...)`).** A new optional `level` argument — one of `LEVEL_COLORS` (`info`/`success`/`warning`/`error`) — tints the status label's foreground (soft green / amber / red shades tuned for the dark chrome) while preserving its transparent/no-border styling; `info`/`None` restores the theme default colour, so every existing caller is unaffected (the param defaults to `None`). The colour is re-applied on each `setStatusText`, so switching from an error back to a plain message cleanly drops the override (`_apply_status_level`). Lets slots surface errors/warnings/successes at a glance in the footer instead of a single undifferentiated grey. Tests: `test_footer.py::TestFooterStatusText` (level tints the label / `info` leaves no override / resets when unset); footer suite 47 green offscreen.

- **2026-06-16 Fix** — **Window auto-fit no longer shrinks into overlapping children when a central widget under-reports its minimum (`MainWindow._content_min_height`).** The first-show dead-space trim (`fit_height_to_content`) and the dynamic `adjust_height_by` both floored their resize on `self.minimumSizeHint().height()`. That hint is an unreliable floor: Qt's `qSmartMinSize` **replaces** a child's layout-computed minimum with any explicit `setMinimumSize` value — *even when the explicit value is smaller than the content needs*. So a central widget carrying a stale/too-small `minimumSize` baked into its `.ui` dragged the window's `minimumSizeHint` below the real content size, and the subsequent `resize()` packed the fixed-height children into too little space — they overlapped. Reported on the Scene Exporter panel under Blender's `windows11` style: `central_widget` advertised `minimumSize.height=240` while its content needed ~268, so the window snapped to 240 on show and the output group + footer overlapped the File box; the *expanded* output group was squeezed out of view, so it read as "always collapsing" even though its persisted state restored correctly. New `_content_min_height()` returns `max(self.minimumSizeHint().height(), centralWidget().minimumSizeHint().height())` — the central widget's own `minimumSizeHint()` reflects its layout's real minimum (it is not subject to the explicit-min override), so the floor always covers content while still trimming dead space above a footer/spacer. Both resize paths now floor on it. (The companion `mayatk` `scene_exporter.ui` also had its bogus `central_widget` min height zeroed.) Regression tests in `test/test_main_window_resize.py::TestFitRespectsTrueContentMin` (recover the true layout min past a too-small explicit central min; fit/adjust pin the window minimum at content height — deterministic, asserting `minimumHeight` not the live-WM resize outcome); window/widget suites 249 green offscreen.
- **2026-06-15 Fix** — **Menu-hosted dynamic widgets keep persisting after the menu reparents to a popup (`Menu._resolve_registration_window` / `_register_with_main_window`).** Widgets added via `Menu.add` (header-menu checkboxes/combos, option-box menu items) are registered with their owning `MainWindow` on a *deferred* event-loop tick (`_schedule_registration` → `QTimer.singleShot(0, _drain_pending_registrations)`). Registration found the window by walking `self.parent()` up to the first object exposing `register_widget`/`widgets`. But a menu **reparents itself to a top-level Tool/Popup window on show** (`setParent(active_window, Qt.Window)`), severing that chain — and in a live DCC session the show/reparent can win the race to run before the drain. The walk then hit no `MainWindow`, returned silently, and the widget never received `restore_state`, so its value was **neither saved nor restored** — the long-standing "menu-hosted options reset every session, but only in interactive Maya" symptom (headless/standalone/`mayapy.standalone` all passed because the reparent doesn't race the drain there). Fix: capture the owning `MainWindow` *weakly* while the chain is still intact — `_schedule_registration` now calls `_resolve_registration_window()`, which prefers a live parent-chain walk (cheap, correct in the common un-reparented case, refreshes the cache) and falls back to the cached window (liveness-probed; dead C++ wrapper drops the ref). `_register_with_main_window` routes through the resolver and now debug-logs the genuinely-unresolvable case instead of failing silently. `_restore_menu_defaults` gets the same cached-window fallback. Note: only widgets added through the menu path were affected — plain `.ui`-tree widgets register at panel-build time and were never at risk. Regression tests in `test/test_menu.py::TestMenuRegistrationSurvivesReparent` (live-chain resolve, cache fallback after reparent, and end-to-end add→reparent→drain still registers + sets `restore_state`); menu suite 150 green, state/persistence/option-box/mainwindow/switchboard suites green (1 pre-existing real-OS popup-width flake unrelated).
- **2026-06-15 Fix** — **`ExpandableList` now reopens collapsed — sublists no longer survive a hide/show in their previously-expanded state (`ExpandableList._force_hide_all`).** Sublists are reparented to the window (so they aren't clipped by intermediate native widgets), which puts them outside the root list's child tree. When an ancestor is hidden, such a sublist receives a *spontaneous* hide — `isVisible()` goes False — but keeps its **explicit-visible flag** (it was opened via `show()`, never explicitly hidden). `_force_hide_all` (run from `hideEvent`, and the hover-collapse paths) guarded its `QWidget.hide()` behind `if w.sublist.isVisible():`, so a sublist already reading as not-visible mid-hide was skipped, its flag survived, and Qt's `showChildren` re-showed it on the next show — the list reappeared expanded ("reshown in the previously open state sometimes"; which sublist had already gone non-visible by the time the root's `hideEvent` fired is what made it intermittent). The hide is now **unconditional** — the flag is cleared whether or not the sublist currently reads as visible — so the list always reopens collapsed; hiding an already-hidden widget is a no-op, so the extra calls are harmless across the shared callers (`hideEvent`, `_maybe_hide_sublist`, `_close_sibling_sublists`). Regression test in `test/test_expandable_list.py::TestExpandableList::test_force_hide_collapses_sublist_shown_under_hidden_ancestor` (shows a sublist under a not-visible window — `isVisible()` False, `isHidden()` False — then asserts `_force_hide_all` leaves it `isHidden()`; fails against the old guarded code); expandable/marking-menu/mouse-tracking suites 125 green.
- **2026-06-13 Fix** — **Option-box rows in the marking-menu overlay re-fit to content on show (`OptionBoxContainer.showEvent` / `_refit_to_content`).** A `tbXXX` option-box button in a `#submenu` overlay rendered far wider than its label — the option-box square pushed ~2–4× too far from the text — but **only on some hosts** (e.g. Blender's `windows11` Qt style; not Maya's `adskdarkflatui`). Root cause is a measure-before-polish + frozen-geometry interaction: the marking menu sizes overlay widgets via `center_widget(w, padding_x=25)` → `minimumSizeHint().width()+25` during `_init_ui`, **before** the theme QSS has polished the button, so on a style whose un-polished button minimum is large (Windows' native ~80px `CT_PushButton` floor) the row was resized to ~80px and that inflated geometry then froze in the absolute-positioned overlay (no parent layout re-runs to correct it once the QSS collapses the hint to ~32px). Styles whose un-polished minimum is already tight (Maya's) never inflated, so the bug was invisible there — and the docked panels masked it everywhere (their buttons stretch to the column regardless). Diagnosed by measuring the real overlays in fresh Maya 2025 vs Blender 5.1 (Blender "Clean" gap 28px / Maya 7px → both ~3px after). Fix: `OptionBoxContainer.showEvent` defers one tick (so the QSS has settled) then re-fits to its content size hint and re-centers — but **only when no parent layout owns it** (the absolute/overlay case); a layout-managed container, e.g. a docked panel where the button intentionally stretches, is left untouched. Verified end-to-end in fresh Maya + Blender GUIs (overlay gaps converge to ~3px; panels unchanged). Regression tests in `test/test_optionBox.py::TestOptionBoxOverlayRefit` (no-parent-layout container collapses an inflated size on show and preserves its center; a layout-managed one stays stretched); optionBox/switchboard 245, marking-menu/mainwindow 129 green.

- **2026-06-13 Fix** — **Persisted marking-menu bindings are now namespaced per host context (`MarkingMenu._binding_store_key` / `_bindings_store` / `on_bindings_changed`).** `SettingsManager` keys QSettings by a fixed `(org, app)`, so a Maya and a Blender session (same OS user) shared ONE `marking_menu_bindings` value — but the `F12+L+R` chord means `maya#startmenu` in one host and `blender#startmenu` in the other. Whichever wrote last hijacked the shared key, so once the forward-merge fix made Maya persist `maya#startmenu`, Blender's identical chord resolved to a UI it doesn't have (the reported "fix works in Maya, not Blender"). The store key is now suffixed with the host's `context_tags` (`marking_menu_bindings_maya` / `_blender`; standalone keeps the legacy un-suffixed key), so each DCC keeps an independent set — the pre-namespace key is intentionally orphaned (re-seeding each host from its own current defaults is the correct recovery). All five store accesses route through `_bindings_store`, and a new public `on_bindings_changed(callback)` lets the binding editor subscribe to the SAME namespaced store (tentacle's settings slots were poking the bare key directly — now they go through `bindings` / `on_bindings_changed`, verified live: the editor reads the identical namespaced dict the menu does). Verified end-to-end in a fresh Maya GUI (`store_key=marking_menu_bindings_maya`, L+R→`maya#startmenu`). Regression tests in `test/test_marking_menu_resolver.py::TestBindingStoreKey` (maya/blender keys differ, standalone unsuffixed, multi-tag deterministic).

- **2026-06-13 Fix** — **Marking-menu bindings now forward-merge new defaults into a user's persisted set (`MarkingMenu._reconcile_bindings`).** `__init__` seeded `configurable.marking_menu_bindings` only when storage was *empty*, so a user who had ever run an older build kept a frozen binding set and **never received newly-shipped default chords**. Concretely: the `F12+L+R → maya#startmenu` default was added after these users' bindings were persisted, so it was absent from the resolver's lookup and the chord fell through resolution step 2 (collapse-to-priority-button) to the RightButton-only sibling `main#startmenu` — "L+R no longer launches the maya windows." Now a new pure static `_reconcile_bindings(defaults, stored)` returns the dict to persist: `defaults` on first run, else `{**defaults, **stored}` (stored/user values win on key overlap, so rebinds survive while missing default keys are added), or `None` when the stored set already covers the defaults (no redundant write/`changed` signal). Verified end-to-end in a live Maya GUI: the L+R chord now resolves to and shows `maya#startmenu`. Regression tests in `test/test_marking_menu_resolver.py::TestReconcileBindings` (first-run seed, stale-set gets new key, user customization preserved on overlap, no-write when current, empty-defaults no-op).

- **2026-06-13 Fix** — **Nav auto-hide no longer blanks marking-menu start menus (`apply_visibility_policy` / new `Switchboard.menu_button_target_resolves`).** The Phase-5 visibility policy hid a nav `MenuButton` when `is_registered_ui(target)` failed, but it tested the **bare** `target` (`"render"`) against the registry's **tagged** filenames (`"render#submenu"`) — an exact-match that can never hit. Marking menus navigate on hover to `"#".join([target, *filterTags, "submenu"])` (see `child_enterEvent`), so every submenu launcher in tentacle's Maya menus carries a bare base-name target; the policy hid all of them and the L+R chord (and every other chord) popped an **empty** menu — "tentacle no longer launches the maya windows when both buttons are held." Resolution now mirrors the live nav paths via `menu_button_target_resolves(widget)`: a target resolves if the direct name (click path) or `widget.submenu_name()` (hover path) is registered. The submenu-name format `"#".join([target, *filterTags, "submenu"])` is now a single source of truth on **`MenuButton.submenu_name()`**, read by both `child_enterEvent` (which opens it) and the policy (which must not hide a button that reaches it) — so the nav target and the hide check can no longer drift (the precise failure mode of this bug). Genuinely-unresolved targets (unported submenus) still hide. The fire happens at polish-time (`MainWindow.register_widget` on the menu's first show), so it only surfaced live, not in the offscreen load tests. Regression tests in `test/test_visibility_policy.py` (bare-target-via-submenu stays visible, filter-tagged resolves, no-match still hides); suite 15/15, marking-menu suites 283/283.

- **2026-06-12 Feature** — **`MarkingMenu._on_activation_press(buttons=None)`** accepts an injected Qt mouse-button mask. Hosts whose native event loop owns the mouse (e.g. Blender's GHOST) pass the physically held buttons in — `QApplication.mouseButtons()` only reflects events Qt itself has seen, so `F12|LeftButton`-style chord bindings could never resolve from such hosts. `None` (the Qt `GlobalShortcut` path — Maya/standalone) falls back to the Qt query, byte-for-byte the prior behavior; the downstream consumer is tentacle's Blender held-button key poller. Marking-menu + events suites 120/120.

- **2026-06-12 Feature** — Context-driven widget visibility + missing-slot policy (the tentacle Blender-port "Phase 5" mechanisms, generic to any host). (1) **`Switchboard.context_tags`** (new ctor kwarg, also on `MarkingMenu`): a set of feature tags the host satisfies (e.g. `{"maya"}`). (2) **`apply_visibility_policy(widget)`** — applied centrally in `MainWindow.register_widget` (before slot init; getattr-guarded for duck-typed sb stubs): hides a widget whose `requires` Designer property (string; `|`/comma/space-separated alternatives) shares no tag with `context_tags` (empty tags = no filtering, standalone/dev shows all), and auto-hides a nav `MenuButton` whose `target` doesn't resolve in the UI registry (`is_registered_ui` — exact-stem lookup, no UI load). Hide reason recorded on `widget.hidden_by_policy`. (3) **Missing-slot policy hook** — `connect_slot`'s no-slot branch now calls `notify_missing_slot` → the switchboard's `on_missing_slot` hook (callable|None; default None = prior silent behavior, zero production cost). Only fires for signal-bearing widget types and never for nav `MenuButton`s. `UITK_MARK_MISSING_SLOTS` env installs the built-in `mark_missing_slot` (grey + explanatory tooltip — a live "not-yet-built" map for development). Covered by `test/test_visibility_policy.py` (12 tests, offscreen-deterministic: isHidden/isEnabled/recorder state only); regression-clean: switchboard 133/133, mainwindow 91/91, dynamic_slot_init 19/19, marking-menu multiscreen/position suites pass.
- **Second-pass audit fixes (2026-06-11)** (`_audit/second_pass_audit_2026-06-11.md`): `ValueManager.set_value` no longer resets a numeric widget to `minimum()` on an unparseable value — the direct path now delegates to `_set_numeric_value`, which leaves the current value untouched (and accepts string numbers); `StateManager.save`/`save_custom` coerce `enum.Enum` values (PySide6's `Qt.CheckState` is not an int subclass, so the primitive-type gate silently dropped tri-state checkbox state — `stateChanged`-wired widgets now persist); `StateManager._defaults` switched to a `WeakKeyDictionary` (a plain dict pinned every registered widget forever) and `reset_all` skips + prunes wrappers whose C++ object is gone instead of crashing; duplicate `Menu.get_padding` removed (unused verbatim copy of the static `ExpandableList.get_padding`). Regression tests in `test/test_value_manager.py`.
- **Audit fix pass (2026-06-11)** (`_audit/uitk_audit_2026-06-11.md`): **`Switchboard.app` is now a lazy `ClassProperty`** — the old class-body `QApplication(sys.argv)` constructed an app as a side effect of merely referencing `uitk.Switchboard`, violating the package's no-side-effects-on-import rule (an app is still guaranteed once a Switchboard is instantiated); removed the duplicate `widgets.optionBox.options.clear` key in `DEFAULT_INCLUDE` (first entry was silently discarded); `Menu.add` no longer lets an item's objectName clobber Menu's own methods (an item named `clear`/`show` replaced the bound method silently — now guarded + warned); `AttributesMixin._set_custom_attribute` warns when a setter-looking kwarg (`set_*`/`setX…`) falls through to the plain-setattr fallback (typos used to be absorbed silently) and its error path logs instead of printing; `ui_history()` is now a pure read (it used to truncate + dedupe the stored history on every call — trimming moved to the `current_ui` setter); dead `Switchboard.__new__` removed; CLAUDE.md/`__init__` docs no longer point to the nonexistent `uitk/signals.py`.

- **Slot busy-cursor now auto-yields to *native* modal dialogs (`slots._ModalBusyCursorFilter`).** The earlier fix (below) only covered uitk's own modal helpers, which suspend the override around their `exec_()`. A slot that opens a **native** DCC dialog the switchboard doesn't wrap — Maya's `cmds.fileDialog2` / `promptDialog`, an OS file picker — still showed the busy hourglass over the dialog's own buttons and fields while waiting for the user (the reported symptom). Rather than wrap every native call site by hand, `SlotWrapper._invoke` now installs a `_ModalBusyCursorFilter` on the `QApplication` for the slot's duration (only while it holds the `WaitCursor`). Qt posts `QEvent.WindowBlocked` when a modal blocks the app and `QEvent.WindowUnblocked` when it's released — for native Qt-backed dialogs too — so the filter pops the whole override stack (preserving order) on the first block and restores it on the matching unblock; nesting is depth-counted so only the outermost pair toggles, and the hourglass resumes automatically for the slot's post-dialog work. The filter is observational (never consumes events) and defensively re-balances on cleanup if an unblock never arrives. uitk's own modal helpers keep their internal suspension (harmless belt-and-suspenders; their mocked-`exec_` test never fires a real block event). Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestModalBusyCursorFilter` (block suspends / unblock restores, nested pairs, full-stack order, never-consumes, dangling-suspend cleanup).
- **Non-modal `text_view_dialog` now cancels the slot busy-cursor when it opens (`utils._drain_override_cursor`).** The earlier busy-cursor fix (below) suspended the override only around *modal* dialogs' `exec_()`, deliberately leaving `text_view_dialog` alone on the assumption it "self-corrects when the spawning slot returns." It doesn't reliably: the viewer is non-modal, so `show()` returns while the dispatcher still holds the `Qt.WaitCursor` override, and a slot that opens the viewer *then keeps working* (or streams content via `append_text`) leaves the hourglass sitting over the report. A suspend/restore context can't apply here — there's no bounded event loop to restore after, and re-pushing the WaitCursor on the window's close would strand a busy cursor with no matching pop (the reported "cursor stays active"). The correct behaviour for a non-modal viewer is to *cancel* the busy cursor outright: the slot's work product is on screen and the user is meant to interact with it. New `_drain_override_cursor()` pops the entire override stack after `show()`; this also makes the dispatcher's own `restoreOverrideCursor` `finally` a harmless no-op, keeping the stack balanced. No-op when no override is active (viewer opened outside a slot). Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestSuspendOverrideCursor::{test_drain_clears_whole_stack, test_text_view_dialog_cancels_busy_cursor}`.
- **`Menu.sizeHint()` now reflects content width even while the menu is invisible — fixes the cropped option-box history popup (`Menu._activate_inner_layouts`).** A history/recent-values popup (e.g. tentacle's "Set Workspace" gear) is *sized then shown*: `RecentValuesPopup._show_popup` populates the menu, calls `adjustSize()`, positions it, then `show()`. But `add()` deliberately skips `self._layout.activate()` while the menu is off-screen (Qt re-activates before paint — see the bulk-add note), and only invalidates the *outer* layout. The inner `centralWidgetLayout` / frame `QBoxLayout`s kept the cached sizeHint from when they were empty — collapsed to just their margins `(4,2)` — while `gridLayout.sizeHint()` was correctly ~1100px. Since `Menu.sizeHint()` reads `self._frame.sizeHint()` directly (bypassing the grid's own recompute) and `invalidate()` only posts a *deferred* `LayoutRequest` that never runs while invisible, `adjustSize()` saw the collapsed width and clamped the popup to its 150px minimum — center-clipping every path into uselessness. `sizeHint()` now forces a synchronous `activate()` on the inner layout chain (`centralWidgetLayout` + frame layout; the outer `self._layout` is left to Qt, which drives its activation) **while the menu is invisible** — once shown, Qt drains the pending `LayoutRequest` and the hints stay current, so the hot visible path is byte-for-byte unchanged (verified: a shown menu reports the correct width with no activation). The refresh runs behind an `_activating_chain` re-entrancy guard, so every pre-show consumer (`adjustSize`, `resize(sizeHint())`, width-matching, screen-clamp) gets the true content width. The existing screen-width cap + `_clamp_to_screen` then keep a very wide popup on-screen as intended. Empty popups stay compact. Tests: `test_optionBox.py::TestRecentValuesPopupWidthSizing` (invisible-popup sizeHint ≥ grid content, `adjustSize` widens past 600px, empty stays < 400px) — all fail (sizeHint width 10) before the fix; full menu/optionBox suites (385) still green.
- **Modal switchboard-utils dialogs suspend the slot busy-cursor so they show natural cursors (`utils._suspend_override_cursor`).** `SlotInvoker._invoke` pushes an application-wide `Qt.WaitCursor` override for every slot's duration (the one busy affordance that survives a frozen Maya `cmds.*` call). A `QApplication` override cursor beats *every* widget cursor, so a modal dialog a slot spawns — `message_box(*buttons)`, `file_dialog` / `dir_dialog` / `save_file_dialog`, `input_dialog` — showed the hourglass over its own buttons, file list, and text field while *waiting for the user to interact*. A per-widget `setCursor` cannot win against an active override, so the fix suspends the whole override-cursor stack (pop-all, preserving order) for the dialog's `exec_()` and restores it exactly afterward via a `contextlib.contextmanager`; it's a no-op when no override is active (dialog opened outside a slot). Non-modal popups (`text_view_dialog`, passive `message_box`) are left alone — they don't block on interaction and self-correct when the spawning slot returns. Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestSuspendOverrideCursor` (no-op without override, suspends+restores a single WaitCursor, restores a stacked override in order, restores on exception, and an end-to-end `input_dialog` check that `exec_` runs with the override cleared) — the `input_dialog` case fails before the fix.
- **Marking-menu navigation windows opt out of the on-screen clamp (`MarkingMenu.setCurrentWidget`) — fixes "the shift breaks the overlay starting position".** The clamp that pins a positioned menu fully within the anchor screen's available geometry now runs only when the widget opts in via `ensure_on_screen` (default `True`); it was previously unconditional. Stacked navigation menus (startmenu/submenu) already set `ensure_on_screen=False` in `_init_ui` (the same flag `MainWindow._ensure_on_screen` honors for standalone windows), so the clamp is now skipped for them and their center stays pinned to the **gesture origin**. That matters because a marking menu's directional flick is measured relative to that point — nudging the menu on-screen desynced the gesture and shifted the overlay's starting position; the user never expects or needs that shift mid-navigation. Standalone windows (shown via `_show_window` → `ui_handler.show`, never through `setCurrentWidget`) are unaffected and keep their `_ensure_on_screen` clamp. For navigation menus this restores the exact pre-clamp behavior (`widget.move(mapFromGlobal(anchor) - rect().center())`). Tests: `test_marking_menu_position_stability.py::TestSetCurrentWidgetOnScreenOptOut` (ensure_on_screen=False → unclamped center-on-anchor; True → clamped to the screen's available top-left; corner-anchored so it's screen-size-independent on CI 'offscreen'); the False case fails against the old unconditional clamp.
- **Marking-menu overlay now follows the active monitor — fixes "shows once, then subsequent shows silently fail" on multi-monitor (`MarkingMenu._ensure_fullscreen_on_active_screen`).** The overlay is a single frameless full-screen window and every menu is positioned inside it via `self.mapFromGlobal(...)`. Since `showFullScreen()` binds the window to whichever screen it currently occupies — set once at construction to the parent (Maya) window's screen — dragging the host DCC to a second monitor left the overlay pinned to the original screen. A menu anchored on the new monitor then mapped to local coordinates outside the overlay's bounds and never appeared (no error). `_show_marking_menu` now relocates the overlay to the screen containing the menu's **anchor** — the same point `setCurrentWidget` positions/clamps against (the gesture origin mid-chord, else the cursor), so the two always agree — (drop full-screen state → `windowHandle().setScreen` + `setGeometry(target.geometry())` → re-`showFullScreen`) **before** `setCurrentWidget` positions the menu, so the coordinate mapping resolves against the correct window origin. The relocation fires only on a *confirmed* screen mismatch (active screen ≠ overlay's `windowHandle().screen()`); single-monitor and indeterminate cases (no window handle / no screens) fall through to the original `if self.isHidden(): self.showFullScreen()`, so it's a strict no-op there. Regression: this is the `super().show()` → `self.showFullScreen()` change that introduced single-screen pinning. Tests: `test_marking_menu_multiscreen.py` (relocates on mismatch, no-op when already on the active screen, indeterminate falls back to show-if-hidden); existing `test_marking_menu*.py` (64 total) still green.
- **`Switchboard.add_reset_buttons(ui, widgets=None, *, types=(QAbstractSpinBox,), skip=(), **set_reset_kwargs)` — batch wrapper that gives a panel's value widgets per-field reset buttons in one call (`SwitchboardUtilsMixin`).** A thin loop over the option-box `ResetOption` (`widget.option_box.set_reset`): for every resolved widget it adds the small reset-to-default icon button (plain click resets to the registry default; Alt/Ctrl+click bypasses to default, greyed/restorable). Widget resolution **mirrors `connect_multi`** — `widgets=None` auto-discovers every child of `types` via `findChildren` (spin boxes by default; pass e.g. `(QComboBox,)` for a combo-driven panel), a shorthand string (`"s000-4"`) resolves through the naming convention, and an explicit list wires exactly those. `skip` accepts objectName(s) and/or widget instance(s) (e.g. a field sharing a tight row with a button); extra kwargs forward to `set_reset` (`reset=`, `icon=`, `tooltip=`, `on_toggled=`). Per-widget failures are caught + debug-logged (so one un-resettable widget can't abort the batch); returns the list of widgets that got a button. This is the shared SSoT for the pattern that several mayatk preview panels were about to hand-roll (it replaces curtain's private `_add_param_reset_buttons` loop). Tests: `test_switchboard.py::TestSwitchboardAddResetButtons` (findChildren discovery, string-pattern + explicit-list resolution, skip-by-name / skip-by-instance, `types=` combo override, kwargs forwarding, empty-container no-op) — uses uitk spin/combo widgets so it mirrors real panels.
- **Preset selector actions → a single row of compact icon buttons, plus a new Refresh (`WidgetComboBox` + `PresetManager.wire_combo`).** The two-row text-button grid (Rename | Delete / Open | Save) under a separator is now one toolbar-style row of icon-only buttons: **Rename · Refresh · Delete · Open · Save**. *Refresh* reloads (re-applies) the currently selected preset; the separator is removed. Backed by two general `WidgetComboBox` knobs: `action_icon_only` (compact, textless square buttons — text becomes the tooltip; default `False`) and `show_action_separator` (default `True`); every action button now also carries an `accessibleName` (its text) so icon-only buttons stay identifiable to screen readers (and tests). `wire_combo` sets `action_icon_only=True` / `show_action_separator=False` / `action_columns=len(actions)` and adds the Refresh action (icons edit/refresh/trash/folder/save at 16px). Tests: `test_widget_combobox.py::{test_icon_only_no_separator_single_row, test_separator_drawn_by_default}`, `test_preset_manager.py::{test_wire_combo_actions_are_icon_only_single_row_with_refresh, test_wire_combo_refresh_reloads_current_preset}`.
- **Centralized reset-to-default now follows an option-box reset toggle's bypass snapshot (`StateManager` + `ResetOption`).** When a field was *bypassed* (held at default via the reset toggle's Alt/Ctrl mode, which stashes a snapshot of the user's value) and the panel's global reset ran, the snapshot survived — so restoring the field resurrected the pre-reset value and the global reset effectively "didn't take." `StateManager.reset`/`reset_all` now call a duck-typed `widget.sync_stored_default(default)` hook right after applying the default; `ResetOption` registers it on the widget while bypassed (and clears it on restore), refreshing its snapshot to the new default. Decoupled by design — StateManager doesn't import the option. Tests: `test_persistence_full_chain.py::TestSyncStoredDefaultHook` (reset/reset_all invoke the hook; no-hook is harmless) and `test_optionBox.py::TestResetOption::test_centralized_reset_clears_bypassed_snapshot` (end-to-end: bypass → global reset → restore yields the default, not the stale value).
- **`SpinBox` / `DoubleSpinBox` gain `set_text_color()` (shared `SpinBoxTextColorMixin`).** Tints a spin box's displayed value text, enabling compact red/green/blue **X/Y/Z value coding** as an alternative to per-axis prefixes. The tint is applied as a `color` directive **on the spin box itself** — the uitk theme draws the value via the `QAbstractSpinBox` color rule, which overrides a color set on the embedded `lineEdit()` (verified by pixmap render under a competing theme rule), so the spin box is the only level that reliably wins. The directive is tagged with a `/*tc*/` marker and merged into (never allowed to clobber) any other inline style on the widget; `None`/`""` clears just our directive. The new mixin (`widgets/mixins/spin_box_text_color.py`) mirrors `wheel_step.py`'s shared-by-both pattern and is applied to both spin classes. Public API: `set_text_color(color)` + `text_color()`. Tests: `test_double_spin_box.py::TestDoubleSpinBoxTextColor` (default unset, applies to the spin box, merge-preserves other inline style, `None`/empty clears) and `test_spinbox.py::TestSpinBoxTextColor`.
- **New OptionBox plugin — `ResetOption` (per-widget reset-to-default button with a modifier-gated *bypass* toggle).** A small option-box icon button beside any value widget. A **plain click resets the field to its registry default** (a normal, *persisted* reset — the user chose it). Hold **Alt or Ctrl** while clicking to **bypass** instead: snapshot the current value, reset to default *transiently*, and grey the widget out; clicking the bypassed button restores the snapshot and re-enables. The icon goes the project "error" red while bypassed so held-at-default fields read at a glance. Bypass is **non-persistent** (each session starts un-bypassed — a panel never reopens with parameters mysteriously held at default); the snapshot is in-memory. The default is resolved **automatically** from the wrapped widget's window `StateManager` (`window.state.reset(widget)`) — the *bypass* reset runs inside the StateManager's `suppress_save()` (transient hold, doesn't bury the value at its default on close), while a *plain* reset persists. `widget.option_box.set_reset()` needs no per-field wiring — pass an explicit `reset` callable to override. Built as a first-class plugin: `options/reset.py::ResetOption(ButtonOption)` (plain `reset()` + `set_bypassed()` state, icon-swap visuals, `_current_modifiers()` seam for the Alt/Ctrl gate, emits `toggled(bool)` on bypass changes only), a fluent `OptionBoxManager.set_reset(...)`, and a `"reset"` slot in the option ordering (`_option_order` + `_sort_options` type map, between `pin` and `toggle`).
  - **Bypass no longer traps itself (`_optionBox.py` enabled-sync).** Bypass greys out the wrapped widget; the container's `_sync_option_buttons_enabled` (fired by the wrapped widget's `EnabledChange`) cascade-disabled *every* option button — including the reset button itself — so once bypassed it could never be clicked again to restore. Added a general per-button opt-out: `_sync_option_buttons_enabled` skips any option widget whose `keepEnabledWhenWrappedDisabled` dynamic property is set, and `ResetOption.setup_widget` sets it. Surgical — sibling option buttons (pin, clear, …) still cascade-disable with the wrapped widget; only the reset button is exempt (and Qt parent-propagation still effectively disables it when the whole container is disabled).
  - **Bypass snapshot/restore are now type-signal-correct (so a connected slot / live preview re-runs).** The restore set the value via the generic `ValueManager.set_value`, which for non-spin widgets could change the value without firing the signal the Switchboard wired for that type — a combo box restored by text needn't fire `currentIndexChanged`, and a check box's `get_value` even snapshotted its *label* (`text()` precedes `isChecked()`). Snapshot/restore now route through `ValueManager.get_value_by_signal`/`set_value_by_signal` keyed on the widget's `default_signals()` (falling back to the generic accessors for unregistered widgets). The reset-to-default path was already type-correct (it delegates to `StateManager.apply`, which uses the widget's default signal). Tests: `TestResetOption::{test_bypass_restore_emits_widget_type_signal_combobox, test_snapshot_uses_type_signal_checkbox, test_bypass_restore_emits_valuechanged_spinbox}`.
  - Tests: `test_optionBox.py` (`TestResetOption` — plain click resets without greying, `reset()`, Alt/Ctrl click enters bypass, click-while-bypassed restores, bypass button stays clickable while widget disabled + siblings still disable, snapshot/restore, `toggled`/silent-set signals, plain-reset-doesn't-emit, auto-reset via window `StateManager`, and the bypass-suppresses-save / plain-reset-does-not-suppress split; `TestOptionBoxManagerReset` — fluent returns-self/adds/replaces + the order key). All optionBox tests green (108).
  - Replaces the earlier `DisableOption`/`set_disable` (unreleased): the primary action is now a plain reset, with the bypass toggle behind a modifier, since the bare "undo" icon read as a simple reset. Downstream: `mayatk` curtain panel updated (`set_reset`).
- **Saved presets no longer vanish next session — legacy-wrap migration stops reburying placed packages (`PresetManager` migration block).** A user preset saved into a package dir (e.g. `mayatk/curtain`) disappeared on the next launch. The save/load core was fine; the deprecated folder-consolidation migration — which runs on the first preset op of every session via `preset_dir` → `_maybe_migrate_legacy` → `_maybe_clear_legacy_qt_roots` — was relocating the whole package tree into the inner `<root>/uitk/` wrapper, where the live load path never looks. Two bugs, two fixes: (1) **`_looks_like_ecosystem_wrapper` misfired on husks.** A prior wrap leaves behind data-less *husk* dirs at the root (`style_presets/`, `hotkey_presets/`, `switchboard_browser/` holding only a `.migrated` sentinel — `_merge_move` keeps the destination on a sentinel collision, so the source survives). Those non-known names made the detector return False *every* launch, re-firing the wrap forever. The detector now treats a husk (no `*.json` at any depth — new `_dir_has_preset_data` helper) as "already wrapped", same as an empty dir. (2) **`_wrap_pre_wrap_uitk_state` relocated known packages.** Even when it did run, it moved *all* root children — including correctly-placed `mayatk/` / `extapps/` siblings — down into the wrapper. It now skips any `known_pkgs` child (only uitk's own non-known pre-wrap dirs move down), so a freshly re-created package dir can never be buried. The two fixes are independent (either prevents the burial; together they also stop the needless churn) and each has its own regression test in `test_preset_manager.py::TestLegacyMigration`: `test_husk_dirs_do_not_rebury_known_packages` reproduces the field bug exactly (husks present → wrap must not fire), and `test_wrap_leaves_known_package_sibling_at_root` forces a genuine wrap (real pre-wrap state present) and pins that the known-package sibling is left at the root. Both fail before their respective fix and pass after; all existing pre-wrap / candidate-drain tests still green.
- **Disabled-while-checked buttons now read as disabled, not active (`style.qss` + `StyleSheet`).** A checked toggle that gets disabled (e.g. an option that doesn't apply to the current mode but is still checked) showed the full `BUTTON_CHECKED` accent — `:checked` and `:disabled` are equal-specificity, so the later `:checked` rule won and the control looked active. Added `QAbstractButton:checked:disabled` and `.default:checked:disabled` rules (two pseudo-classes → higher specificity) backed by a new **derived** token `DISABLED_CHECKED_BACKGROUND`: the resolved `DISABLED_BACKGROUND` blended ~22% toward `BUTTON_CHECKED` (new `StyleSheet._blend` 2-color lerp; `_disabled_checked_mix`), so the button reads as *disabled with a faint checked tint*. It's internal-only (injected by `_derive_internal_vars` alongside the `*_TINT` companions, tracks source/override changes, rejected by `set_variable` via `_is_derived_token`) — no new exposed theme var. Tests: `test_style_sheet.py` (`test_disabled_checked_background_derived_and_protected`; `test_qss_has_no_unresolved_tokens` now derives its known-token set the same way assembly does, covering any internal token).
- **Widget-state restore hardening: checkable-button value path + no double-JSON-decode.** Two latent bugs in the state-restore value path (surfaced while auditing a "checkbox state not restored between sessions" report):
  - **`ValueManager.set_value` set a checkable button's *label* instead of its *checked state*.** Every `QAbstractButton` (incl. plain `QCheckBox`) inherits `setText`, and the `setText` branch preceded the `setChecked` branch — so a checkbox routed through the fallback `set_value` path had its text set to the value. The uitk `CheckBox` made it worse (it overrides `setText` with a rich-text setter), so `set_value(chk, True)` wrote `"True"` into the label and left the box unchecked. Added an `isinstance(widget, QAbstractButton) and widget.isCheckable()` branch (delegating to `_set_boolean_value`) *before* `setText`; non-checkable `QPushButton`s still take text. The signal path (`set_value_by_signal`'s `toggled`) was already correct — this only affects the fallback used by presets / pin-values / signal-less restore. Tests: `test_value_manager.py::TestSetValueCheckableButtons`.
  - **`StateManager.load` double-decoded values.** `MainWindow` passes a `SettingsManager` (not the raw `QSettings` the signature declares); `SettingsManager.value` already JSON-decodes, so `load`'s second `json.loads` was redundant and lossy (decoding an already-decoded `True` raised `TypeError` and silently fell back). `load` now only `json.loads` raw `str` values, passing already-typed values through — preserving the raw-`QSettings` path without the double-decode. Tests: `test_persistence_full_chain.py::TestStateManagerNoDoubleDecode`.
- **`MainWindow` snaps its height to content on first show (`fit_to_content_on_show`, default `True`) — removes trailing vertical deadspace.** Covers both the gap above a `Footer` (when present — a trailing Expanding spacer absorbing the slack between the last widget and the footer) and the empty band at the bottom of a footerless window; most visible after a persisted session resize is restored larger than the content. `MainWindow.showEvent` now calls the existing `fit_height_to_content()` once on first show. The fit lives on `MainWindow`, not `Footer` — the footer is a fixed-height leaf with no authority over the top-level geometry, and `MainWindow` already owns the first-show lifecycle and the resize toolkit (`fit_height_to_content` / `adjust_height_by` / `_activate_descendant_layouts`). It runs **regardless of whether a saved geometry was restored**: a restored geometry's width and position are kept (the fit preserves width), and only the vertical dead space is trimmed. Opt out per-window with `fit_to_content_on_show=False` for windows whose extra height is meaningful (a growable list / scroll area). Tests: `test_main_window_resize.py::TestFitToContentOnShow` (runs on first show by default, skipped when disabled, runs even when a saved size was restored, first-show-only, and an end-to-end "deadspace collapsed" check on the tentacle-style group+spacer+footer layout); `test_mainwindow.py::test_restore_disabled_ignores_saved_geometry_on_show` opts out so it keeps isolating the orthogonal saved-geometry path.
- **Preset selector: 2-column action grid, separator dead-space fix, and read-only built-in handling (`WidgetComboBox` + `PresetManager.wire_combo`).** Three related fixes to the persistent actions section under a preset combo, affecting every panel that uses preset templates:
  - **`WidgetComboBox.action_columns`** (default `1`) lays the action buttons out in a row-major grid. `PresetManager.wire_combo` sets it to `2` and reorders the actions to **Rename | Delete** on the first row and **Open | Save** on the second, replacing the four-line vertical stack.
  - **Separator dead-space fix.** The actions separator is a NoFrame/HLine that advertises an *invalid* sizeHint height, so `_apply_uniform_height` couldn't size its row and the view fell back to the delegate's font-based default — taller than the 7px line, rendering as visible dead space between the separator and the buttons (pronounced under Maya's larger UI font). `_rebuild_actions_section` now pins the separator row's `Qt.SizeHintRole` to the separator widget's own height.
