  - **Read-only built-ins are marked and protected.** `wire_combo` italicises built-in (shipped) presets in the dropdown + adds a read-only tooltip (via the model item's `Qt.FontRole`/tooltip, so `itemText` stays the raw name for load/rename/delete, and the collapsed display keeps the widget font so the dropdown arrow is unaffected), and **disables Rename/Delete while a built-in is selected** — they can only no-op on a read-only preset, so greying them out is clearer than a silent click (the prior "deleting a built-in does nothing" confusion). Save stays enabled (writes a user preset that shadows the built-in — "duplicate to edit"), as does Open. Buttons follow their `QAction.setEnabled` state via the new `WidgetComboBox._bind_button_to_action` (bindings tracked + disconnected on rebuild so they don't accumulate). Tests: `test_widget_combobox.py::TestWidgetComboBoxActionsSection` (grid row-major, separator row pinned, button mirrors action-enabled, no connection accumulation) and `test_preset_manager.py::TestBuiltinTier::{test_wire_combo_italicises_builtins, test_wire_combo_disables_rename_delete_for_builtin}`.
- **`Header` menu button auto-hides when its menu has no real content, and auto-shows when content is added.** The header's `menu` (`☰`) button was always shown once configured, so tools that never populated their header menu (or only ever surfaced the transient "No options" placeholder) presented a button that opened an empty popup. The button now mirrors `Menu.contains_items` — which already excludes the empty-state placeholder — so an empty (or placeholder-only) menu keeps the button hidden, and populating the menu later reveals it. Implementation: `Header._sync_menu_button_visibility()` is the single source of truth (called from `showEvent`, from `config_buttons` after a layout rebuild that recreates the button visible, and wired to the menu's `on_item_added` signal for live auto-show); it reads `_menu` directly so it never force-creates a menu just to hide a button. This also surfaced and fixed a latent `Menu` bug: **`on_item_added` was never delivered to listeners** because `add()` blocks the menu's signals for the duration of the (recursive, bulk) insert, swallowing the synchronous `emit`. Added items are now queued and flushed once the *outermost* `add()` unwinds and the menu is settled (updates re-enabled, layout activated) — recursion tracked by a `_add_depth` counter so a single item, a bulk collection add (one ordered emit per item), and an externally pre-blocked `add()` (notifications dropped, never leaked into a later call) all behave correctly. Tests: `test_header.py::TestHeaderMenuButtonAutoVisibility` (hidden-when-empty, shows-on-add, placeholder-doesn't-count, never-accessed-stays-hidden) and `test_menu.py::TestMenuSignals` (delivery for single + bulk add, external-block suppression).
- **`WidgetComboBox` dropdown rows now sit tight with an exposed `item_spacing` (default 1px).** Rows showed an unexplained ~3px gap between embedded widgets. Cause: `_apply_uniform_height` captured each widget's `sizeHint` at *add-time*, but a widget's height can change afterward — a `CheckBox` measures 17px before the theme is applied and 14px after — so `_uniform_item_height` stayed at the stale 17 while the widget rendered at 14, and `AlignVCenter` rendered the 3px surplus as dead space between rows. Fixes: (1) `showPopup` now calls the new `_recompute_uniform_heights()` to re-derive the uniform height from the widgets' *current* sizeHints (rows fit tightly); (2) the deliberate inter-row gap is the new **`item_spacing`** property (default `1`, settable; row height = tight widget height + `item_spacing`), so the spacing is a single exposed knob instead of an accidental by-product of stale sizing. Set `combo.item_spacing = 0` for flush rows. Tests: `test_widget_combobox.py::TestWidgetComboBoxItemSpacing` (default, adds-to-row-height, stale-height correction); the existing uniform-height test pins `item_spacing = 0` to isolate that behavior.
- **`BridgeSlotsBase` log-panel `action://open` links now work standalone (no Maya).** `_on_log_link_clicked` delegated *every* `action://` anchor to mayatk's `UiUtils.dispatch_log_link`, so when a bridge panel runs as a standalone external app (the photogrammetry Metashape/RealityCapture/Brush case, and the common one) the import failed and a clicked output-dir link silently did nothing — even though the `open` action (reveal a file/folder) is DCC-agnostic. The base now handles `open` itself via the cross-platform `_open_in_file_manager` (and as a bonus this is cross-platform, where mayatk's handler used Windows-only `os.startfile`), and only the node-based actions (`select`/`reveal` in the Maya Outliner) defer to the lazily-imported Maya dispatcher. Additive + backward-compatible: the marmoset/substance/rizom `open?path=` links keep working and now also work outside Maya; node actions are unchanged. Covered by `test_bridge_slots.py::TestBridgeLogLinkOpen`.
- **`AttributeSpec` gains a `section` field; `BridgeSlotsBase` renders titled category dividers from it, plus a reusable `reveal_folder()` helper.** Parameter panels with many knobs were a flat list. A spec can now carry `section="…"`; `_build_param_widgets` inserts a titled `uitk.widgets.Separator` before the first spec of each new section (one per section; sections expected contiguous), and `_refresh_param_visibility` hides a section's divider when all its params are hidden for the current template/mode (so a fully-hidden category leaves no stray rule). Backward-compatible — specs without `section` render exactly as before (the DCC bridges set none). The field lives on the shared `AttributeSpec`, so `AttributeWindow` can adopt the same grouping when a consumer needs it. Also extracted **`BridgeSlotsBase.reveal_folder(path)`** (existence check + cross-platform open + error log) out of `open_templates_folder`, so subclass header actions ("Open Output Folder", …) reuse it instead of re-implementing. Covered by the extapps Metashape panel test `test_param_sections_have_dividers_that_track_mode`; the marmoset mock-bridge suite confirms the no-section path is unchanged.
- **Themeable layout metrics + uniform text inset across form widgets.** Two cosmetics that were hardcoded literals in `style.qss` are now exposed as theme tokens (resolved via the existing `{TOKEN}` substitution, editable live in the Style Editor):
  - **`COMBOBOX_ITEM_HEIGHT`** (default `19px`, was a hardcoded `min-height: 14px`) — the row height of combobox popup items. The token is the QSS `min-height` floor (also for plain `QComboBox` popups) *and* the value `_CurrentItemIndicatorDelegate.sizeHint` reads to **force** uitk `ComboBox` rows to exactly that height. The delegate enforcement is the key fix: `min-height` alone is only a floor, so a larger UI font or the combobox's `AdjustToMinimumContentsLengthWithIcon` icon-height reservation inflated rows past the token (the "rows look taller than 19px / uitk tallest" report). Rows carrying an explicit `Qt.SizeHintRole` are respected, so `WidgetComboBox` rows hosting a taller embedded widget still grow. The popup item's top/bottom padding is also zeroed so the plain-`QComboBox` floor isn't `token + 2px`. Tests in `test_combobox.py::ComboBoxPopupRowHeight` (default, custom value, clamp-down under a 20pt font, and explicit-size-hint respect).
  - **`StyleSheet.get_variable_px(name, theme, widget, default)`** — new SSoT accessor that parses a length token to an `int` (`"19px"` → `19`, `default` when unset/non-numeric). The delegate above and the Style Editor's px spin boxes now route through it instead of each re-implementing the parse (removed `style_editor._parse_px`). Covered by `test_style_sheet.py::test_get_variable_px`.
  - **`TEXT_INSET`** (default `2px`) — one horizontal text inset shared by `QLabel`, `QComboBox`, `QLineEdit`, and `QAbstractSpinBox` (symmetric left+right). Previously each set its own value (label 2px, combobox 1px, line edit 8px, spin box Qt-default), so text started at a different x in every widget; they now align in a layout. The combobox shifts ~1px right to match labels as requested; line edits tighten from 8px to the shared inset (tune the one token for roomier inputs).

  The Style Editor's `LENGTH_TOKENS` became a `{token: (min, max)}` map (SSoT for "which tokens are lengths *and* their spinbox range") so both new metrics render as px spin boxes rather than being misclassified as colors; `RADIUS`/`BORDER_W` keep their justified ≤8 cap. Tests: `test_style_editor.py::test_combobox_item_height_renders_as_spinbox` and `test_style_sheet.py::test_text_inset_is_uniform_across_form_widgets` (distinctive-override proof that each base rule reads the token).
- **`BridgeSlotsBase` gains a `_relevant_param_keys()` hook so panels can drive dynamic parameter visibility from something other than a template file.** `_refresh_param_visibility` hard-coded "the keys are whatever `__TOKEN__` placeholders the active template file references" — fine for the script-substitution bridges (marmoset / substance / rizom), but a single-runner panel selected by a *run mode* (e.g. the photogrammetry Metashape panel's Full / Align-only / Refine-only) had no template file and was forced to override the whole method to show every row statically. The "which keys are relevant?" decision is now a `_relevant_param_keys()` hook (default = the previous template-file behavior, returns `None` to skip), while `_refresh_param_visibility` keeps the shared row-toggle + height-fit bookkeeping. Run-mode panels override the hook to feed *their* current input (e.g. a run mode) to *their* `params_module.referenced_keys(...)` — so relevance stays declared in the params module (the SSoT) exactly as the script-substitution bridges declare it via `__TOKEN__` placeholders, with no relevance map leaking into the slots. Behavior-preserving for the existing bridges (verified by the marmoset mock-bridge suite + `test_bridge_slots.py`).
- **`ExternalAppHandler.launch()` self-heals a stale cached registration instead of failing with a confusing install-then-import error.** `discover()` caches each app's entry-point module path in `self._apps` once (at host startup). If that path later changes on disk — a package move (`extapps.metashape_workflow` → `extapps.photogrammetry.metashape_workflow`) or a version bump that rewrites an editable install's entry-point metadata — a long-running host (e.g. an open Maya session) kept importing the **old** path, hit `_is_importable() == False`, ran a surprise `pip install`, and then raised *"Install completed but `<old.module>` is still not importable"* — leaving the user stuck until a full host restart. `launch()` now, on import failure and only when the module came from the registry (no explicit `module=` kwarg), **re-discovers once and retries with the refreshed path** before the install fallback. Because `discover()` rebuilds a registration from entry-point metadata alone, the re-discovery **preserves the launch-augmentation fields a manual `register()` layered on** (`install_spec` / `python` / `show_kwargs`) — snapshotting them before and restoring any the rebuild blanked — so correcting the module path never silently drops the `install_spec` a host (e.g. tentacle's `install_spec="extapps"`) relies on for the install fallback. Importability is evaluated once and re-checked only after a successful self-heal, so the happy path and the explicit-`module=` install path are unchanged (existing `_is_importable`-call-count assertions still hold). Tests: `test/test_external_app_handler.py::TestExternalAppHandlerLaunch::{test_launch_self_heals_stale_registration, test_self_heal_falls_through_to_install_when_unchanged, test_self_heal_preserves_install_augmentation_fields}`. Verified end-to-end in a fresh Maya (via `mayatk.MayaConnection`): a stale `extapps.metashape_workflow` registration auto-corrected to `extapps.photogrammetry.metashape_workflow`, `install_spec` survived the heal, and the panel constructed (and found the local Metashape exe — no silent mock) without a host restart.
- **`PresetManager` + `BridgeSlotsBase` gain an opt-in *semantic-preset* mode — presets keyed by meaning, shareable with a headless CLI.** Bridge presets were raw widget-state keyed by `objectName` (GUI-only); a panel that wanted to persist the *same* run-template its CLI reads (e.g. photogrammetry's `specular_metal`) couldn't. Two additive, backward-compatible hooks:
  - **`PresetManager(value_provider, value_applier)`** (also on `setup()`): when both are set, `save` serializes `value_provider()`'s `{key: value}` dict (instead of widget snapshots) and `load` hands the payload (with `_meta` stripped) to `value_applier(data)` — so presets (de)serialize by semantic key. The two-tier `_store` (built-in + user via `pythontk.PresetStore`) and `wire_combo` are unchanged, so built-ins still layer under user saves and the combo's Save/Rename/Delete still work. Default (no callbacks) = exactly today's widget-state behavior.
  - **`BridgeSlotsBase.make_preset_store()`** (default `None` = widget-state, per-template subdirs under `PRESETS_ROOT`): returning a `pythontk.PresetStore` flips the panel to semantic mode — `_build_preset_controls` builds a `PresetManager` wired to `collect_param_values` / the new **`_apply_param_dict`** (maps `{param_key: value}` onto the panel's param widgets, ignoring keys it doesn't surface — overlay semantics matching a CLI `--preset`), and `_on_template_changed` no longer re-points the preset dir (the store is template-agnostic — one shared set). The DCC bridges (marmoset / substance / rizom) don't override the hook, so they're untouched. Tests: `test/test_preset_manager.py::TestSemanticPresetMode` (provider/applier round-trip, `_meta` stripped, user shadows built-in, combo lists both tiers) and the new `test/test_bridge_slots.py::TestBridgeSemanticPresets` (built-in run-template loads into param widgets, a Save is read back by the headless store, unknown keys ignored). This is the machinery the `extapps` Metashape panel now uses to share `specular_metal` + user presets with `run_combined --preset`.
- **`PresetManager` gains a built-in (shipped, read-only) preset tier and delegates storage to `pythontk.PresetStore`.** Presets were single-tier (user-writable only), so a panel couldn't ship default presets layered under a user's saves. `PresetManager` now takes an optional **`builtin_dir`** (constructor / `from_widgets` / `setup`) — a panel's `presets/` dir by convention, ignored when `None`/absent — whose presets appear in `list()` **under** the user tier (a user save of the same name shadows the built-in; saving a built-in's name is the natural "duplicate to edit" flow). New `source(name) → "user"|"builtin"|None` lets a UI lock/relabel built-ins; `delete`/`rename` act on the user tier only (built-ins are read-only). The file-facing internals (`list`/`save`/`load`/`delete`/`rename`/`exists`/`_preset_path` + name sanitization) now delegate to a `pythontk.PresetStore` built off the (still legacy-migrated) user `preset_dir` plus `builtin_dir`, so the GUI and any headless path share one implementation, directory layout, and naming — a user-saved preset is reachable both ways. **Backward-compatible**: callers that don't pass `builtin_dir` behave exactly as before (user-only); widget-state capture/apply and combo wiring are unchanged. Tests: `test/test_preset_manager.py::TestBuiltinTier` (built-in listed/sourced, loads into widgets, user save alongside + shadowing, read-only built-in).
- **`BridgeSlotsBase._selected_template_mode` accepts list-or-tuple `itemData`** — some PySide bindings round-trip the `(template, mode)` tuple stored via `addItem` back through `QVariant` as a *list*, so the `isinstance(data, tuple)` gate returned `None` and the send button reported "no template chosen." It now accepts either and normalizes to a tuple. Surfaced by the new standalone `extapps.marmoset_workflow` panel (the Maya-hosted bridges run under a binding that preserves tuples, so they never hit it). Strictly more permissive — can't break the tuple case.
- **`UiHandler.apply_styles` no longer treats the auto-installed help button as a configured layout** — its "did the slot already configure header buttons?" gate read `current = header.buttons.keys()`, and a slot's `header_init` calling `set_help_text(...)` populated `{"help"}` before `apply_styles` got a chance to apply defaults. The non-empty `current` made apply_styles skip its `config_buttons(...)` call entirely, so the UI was left with only the help button — the rest of the chrome (menu / collapse / hide / refresh) silently disappeared. Now the gate filters help out: `non_help_current = tuple(b for b in current if b != "help")`. If the only thing the slot installed is help, defaults still apply (and `config_buttons` preserves help across its rebuild because `_help_text` is set). Regression test `TestApplyStylesWithHelpButton` pins the three cases: help-only must NOT block defaults, non-help buttons MUST still block them, and empty headers get defaults as before.

- **`fmt()` rich-text tooltip helper gains `kbd()` / `hl()` and a `notes` parameter; colored title / section / note styling** — the helper used to render plain bold titles and white-text bullets, so multi-section help tooltips (Shot Manifest, Shot Sequencer, Channels, Mat Updater, etc.) ran together as a wall of text. Improvements:
  - **New `kbd(*keys)`** — render keyboard keys as `<kbd>`-style chips with monospace font, rounded border, and consistent spacing. Multi-key combos join with `+` so `kbd("Ctrl", "Z")` renders as two chips. Now used in Shot Sequencer (keyboard shortcuts section), Channels (wheel-scrub ladder), Wheel Rig (Shift-select), Color Manager (Ctrl-click).
  - **New `hl(text, color=_C_ACCENT)`** — wrap text in an inline color span for state callouts (e.g. <i>On</i> in green) without rebuilding the surrounding HTML.
  - **New `notes=[...]` parameter for `fmt()`** — italic muted "note:"-prefixed callouts rendered after main content. Use for caveats, plugin prerequisites, and "see also" hints.
  - **Color palette** tuned for Qt's dark tooltip background: titles in cool off-white, section headings in soft cyan, row keys / "note:" prefix in muted gray, note body in warm muted gold.
  - **Tighter spacing** — title `margin:0 0 3px 0`, sections `margin:6px 0 1px 0`, notes `margin:3px 0 0 0` — gives each segment visual breathing room without inflating the tooltip height.
  - 16 tests in `test/test_tooltip_mixin.py` covering chip rendering, color spans, each `fmt` section type, ordering invariants, embedded-HTML pass-through, and `kbd`-inside-`fmt` composition.

- **Header `set_help_text(...)` API replaces per-tool "Instructions" menu entries** — every Switchboard tool was duplicating the same 8-line pattern (`widget.menu.add("Separator", setTitle="About")` + `QPushButton` with `setText="Instructions"` and `setObjectName="btn_instructions"`) just to surface a tooltip nobody could find without opening the header menu first. `Header` now ships a `help` entry in `button_definitions` (icon: `uitk/icons/help.svg`) and a one-liner API:
  - `widget.set_help_text(text)` lazily inserts a `?` button at the leftmost slot (immediately right of the layout stretch) and stores `text` as its tooltip. Hover shows the tooltip (Qt default); clicking forces it open via `QToolTip.showText` anchored just below the button.
  - `widget.help_text()` reads the persisted text back; `widget.show_help()` is the click callback (also callable directly).
  - The text persists across `config_buttons(...)` rebuilds — config_buttons now re-adds the help button if `_help_text` was set but `'help'` wasn't in the list, so the help text never silently disappears when a later layout rebuild fires.
  - `'help'` is also accepted as an explicit `config_buttons` entry for callers who want fixed ordering.
  - 10 tests in `TestHeaderHelpButton` (auto-add on set, tooltip wiring, leftmost-slot insertion, idempotence, click-invokes-QToolTip, config_buttons persistence regression).
  - Migrated 39 ecosystem files away from the old menu pattern in parallel — see [`m3trik/docs/HEADER_HELP_INVENTORY.md`](../m3trik/docs/HEADER_HELP_INVENTORY.md) for the full list and the standalone-tool candidates that still lack help text.

- **Separator title no longer crops in narrow hosts** — `Separator` inherited `QFrame.sizeHint()`, which for the default `HLine` shape reports near-zero width. Once switched to `NoFrame` for the titled variant, the hint still didn't account for the child title label, so host containers (notably `QMenu`) auto-sized the separator off sibling widgets only — and any time the host was narrower than the title text, the label (a child positioned at `x=4` with no width clamp) was clipped on the right.
  - **Width fix**: `sizeHint()` and `minimumSizeHint()` now return `title_label.sizeHint().width() + 2 * margin` when the title is visible; `updateGeometry()` on title change makes parent layouts re-query. The 4-pixel positioning margin is extracted as `_TITLE_MARGIN_X` so the position math and the advertised width agree.
  - **Positioning fix** (follow-up): the width fix wasn't enough on its own — the label was still rendering cropped because `resizeEvent`'s gate was `isVisible()`, which is False whenever any ancestor is hidden. When a `Separator` lives in a menu that's hidden at construction (every `option_box.menu` is hidden until first show), no resize during the title-setter chain reached the positioning code, and the label stayed at its default 0×0 geometry. Even a correctly-sized host then rendered a 0-width label. Two changes: extracted `_position_title_label()` and called it directly from the title setter so the label gets its real size immediately; switched the guard from `isVisible()` to `not isHidden()` so subsequent resize events position correctly regardless of ancestor visibility. Regression test `test_title_label_has_non_zero_size_before_show` pins the contract.
- **MarkingMenu position stability — chord transitions no longer drift with cursor jitter** — every show of a startmenu used to call `overlay.start_gesture(QtGui.QCursor.pos())` and `setCurrentWidget` cursor-anchored. Repeated chord transitions (e.g. holding F12 and tapping LMB/MMB/RMB) rebound `start_pos` to whatever pixel the cursor was on at press time; natural hand jitter migrated the menu pixel-by-pixel in a consistent direction. User report: "the ui steadily shifts to the left or right a small amount each time."
  - Gesture origin is now established **once** per activation cycle. `_show_marking_menu`, `mousePressEvent`, and `keyPressEvent` only call `start_gesture` when `overlay.path.is_empty` (genuinely a fresh activation). Subsequent startmenu shows during the same cycle anchor at the preserved `start_pos` instead of the current cursor.
  - `setCurrentWidget` and `_prepare_ui` now accept an optional `anchor: QPoint` kwarg (defaults to current cursor for back-compat). `_return_to_startmenu` collapsed from prepare-then-override-with-move to a single `_prepare_ui(startmenu, anchor=start_pos)` call.
  - `_position_submenu_smooth` no longer side-effects the destination widget's size — uses the source's center for both `mapToGlobal` reads (mathematically identical to the resize-then-align approach).
  - 4 new tests in `test_marking_menu_position_stability.py` (initial cursor anchor, chord anchored at start_pos, zero drift across 20 jittered iterations, fresh gesture after path clear). Existing integration tests unchanged (one-line stub field added).

- **MarkingMenu breadcrumb clones now match the original launcher's size** — `Overlay._clone_widget` was silently dropping the size copy: `CLONE_ATTRS` listed `"size"` and the loop auto-generated the setter name as `setSize`, but `QWidget` has no `setSize` (the setter is `resize`). The `hasattr` check filtered it out and every clone fell back to Qt's default widget size (~100×30 for `QPushButton`). Breadcrumb clones placed along the gesture path looked oversized and didn't match the buttons they represented.
  - Fix: removed `"size"` from `CLONE_ATTRS` and added an explicit `new_widget.resize(prev_widget.size())` call *after* the attribute loop (so `minimumSize`/`maximumSize` don't clamp the final size).

- **MarkingMenu submenu positioning — resize no longer pulls neighbors off layout** — the real root cause of the "drift across most submenus" bug. `_position_submenu_smooth` resizes the destination's same-name widget (`w2`) to match the launcher's size; `w2.resize` keeps the top-left fixed, so its local *center* shifts by half the size delta. That shift propagated into `diff = p1 - p2` and `ui.move(ui.pos() + diff)` then slid every neighboring widget by the same amount — the visible symptom was clone-to-breadcrumb spacing tightening as you descended the hierarchy, even though the captured anchor positions were mathematically consistent. Fix: after `w2.resize`, also `w2.move` it back so its local center stays at the original layout position — the resize then affects only `w2`'s extent, not its position, and neighbors keep their layout offsets. New `test_smooth_positioning_resize_does_not_shift_neighboring_widgets` regression catches the shift directly.

- **MarkingMenu submenu positioning now anchors to path-saved center** — `_position_submenu_smooth` previously re-read the trigger widget's global center via `w.mapToGlobal(w.rect().center())` at smooth time, *after* `_prepare_ui` had already hidden the source UI. Any intermediate state change (layout-on-hide, deferred geometry, style reapply) could shift the live re-read away from what `Path.add` captured a few function calls earlier. `_perform_transition` now threads the path-captured anchor through to `_position_submenu_smooth` via a new `anchor_global` kwarg — single source of truth for "where the cursor crossed the button," eliminating one whole class of timing-dependent drift. `Path.add` returns the captured position (or `None` if skipped) so callers don't have to peek at the private `_path` list. Live re-read is preserved as fallback when callers don't pass an anchor.

- **MarkingMenu clone widget size now applied first** — `_clone_widget` previously copied `minimumSize` / `maximumSize` first and resized to `prev_widget.size()` afterward, with a comment claiming the order kept attrs from clamping the size. In reality the opposite is more dangerous: if `prev_widget`'s stated bounds happen to disagree with its actual size (rare but possible after style/layout interactions), the explicit resize is silently clamped and `rect().center()` no longer corresponds to the saved global anchor — clone lands off-pixel. Fix: resize *first* (uncontested, before any attr can interfere), copy attrs, then re-apply resize if anything perturbed the geometry, then position. The position math now uses a verified-correct `rect().center()`.

- **MarkingMenu breadcrumb clone positioning hardened against deferred geometry** — `Overlay._clone_widget` previously computed its placement via `new_widget.mapFromGlobal(position - new_widget.rect().center())`. That relies on the newly-created clone's geometry being trustworthy *before* its first showEvent — a fragile assumption that synthetic tests couldn't reproduce but users reported as descend-then-ascend drift ("the polygons button and the mesh button" appearing closer together in the deeper submenu).
  - Fix: position is now computed via `ui.mapFromGlobal(position)` (the clone's parent — the QMainWindow — whose geometry is fully initialized) then offset by `-new_widget.rect().center()`. Functionally equivalent for fully-initialized widgets; immune to Qt's deferred geometry state for fresh widgets.
  - The clone *stays* parented to the QMainWindow (NOT to its central widget). Hovering the clone re-triggers `MarkingMenu.child_enterEvent` for the return-to-previous-submenu gesture; that dispatch depends on the marking-menu event filter installed at the QMainWindow level catching enter events from its direct children. Burying the clone inside `ui.centralWidget()` breaks the gesture (cursor-over-clone does nothing — only the gesture-origin Region remains as a navigation-back affordance).
  - New regression tests in `test_overlay_clone_positioning.py`: clone-to-breadcrumb distance must equal polygons-to-mesh in polysub (zero drift descending), AND the clone must be a direct child of the QMainWindow (interactivity).

- **TableWidget cell-wheel-scrub — axis-swap fix + modifiers via signal** — same Alt-axis-transpose bug that hit `SpinBox` also broke `TableWidget._emit_wheel_scrub`: it read only `event.angleDelta().y()`, so Alt-held wheels (which transpose to `.x()` on some Qt builds) produced `steps == 0` and never emitted the signal. Reads `delta.y() or delta.x()` now.
  - **Signal signature widened**: `cellWheelScrolled = Signal(int, int, int, object)` — appended the event's modifier mask. Receivers used to poll `QApplication.keyboardModifiers()`, which can race against the wheel event itself; passing modifiers along the signal kills that whole class of bug. **Breaking** for direct connectors (the only one in the monorepo is `mayatk.ChannelsSlots._on_wheel_scrolled`, updated in parallel).
  - 5 new tests in `test_table_widget_wheel.py` covering y-axis emit, x-axis (Alt-transposed) emit, negative direction, zero-delta no-emit, modifiers payload.

- **SpinBox / DoubleSpinBox — symmetric modifier ladder + themed FeedbackMixin** — overhaul of the modifier-wheel handling and the transient HUD popup.
  - **Symmetric ladder** (Ctrl scales up, Alt scales down, stacking amplifies)::

        plain         singleStep                    (default Qt step)
        Ctrl          singleStep × 10               (coarse)
        Ctrl+Shift    singleStep × 100              (very coarse)
        Alt           singleStep / 10               (fine)
        Ctrl+Alt      10 ** -decimals               (smallest)

    The previous "Alt re-calibrates `singleStep`" gesture was asymmetric (a meta-operation rather than a value step) and inconsistent with how Houdini, Blender, 3ds Max all pair Ctrl/Alt with coarse/fine. The new ladder is fully symmetric: `Ctrl` scales the step **up** ×10, `Alt` scales the step **down** ×10, and stacking (`Ctrl+Shift` / `Ctrl+Alt`) amplifies to the extremes (×100 / smallest representable). An earlier iteration used `Ctrl+Alt` for *snap-to-next-integer* (Blender's `Ctrl`-drag) but it visually collapsed to the same result as `Ctrl` for any integer-aligned starting value, so the smallest-step gesture is the cleaner default. The "re-calibrate `singleStep`" feature is removed -- it was undiscoverable and a different conceptual category from the rest of the ladder.
  - **Axis-swap fallback**: direction reads `delta.y() or delta.x()` so Alt-held wheels still work on platforms / Qt6 builds that transpose `angleDelta` onto the X axis.
  - **FeedbackMixin** (`uitk/widgets/mixins/feedback.py`): the transient HUD that flashes the step amount is now a reusable mixin instead of `self.msgBox = MessageBox(...)` duplicated in each widget. Hosts get `show_feedback(html)`; the underlying `MessageBox` is lazy-instantiated on first call so widgets that never show feedback pay zero cost. `WheelStepMixin` calls `show_feedback` via duck-typing, so hosts that don't include `FeedbackMixin` silently no-op the feedback path.
  - **`MessageBox` now picks up uitk theme tokens** (`PANEL_BACKGROUND`, `TEXT_COLOR`, `BORDER_COLOR`, `BORDER_W`, `RADIUS`). New QSS rules in `style.qss` for `.MessageBox` + the inner `qt_msgbox_label`. Per-call `background=` overrides are applied on the inner label directly (not via `self.setStyleSheet`) so they layer on top of the themed QSS without replacing it. `setText(...)` default for `background` changed from `0.75` → `None` (use theme) — passing an explicit value still works the same way.
  - **AttributeWindow `_build_int` now uses uitk `SpinBox`** instead of plain `QtWidgets.QSpinBox`, so integer attribute rows pick up the same modifier-driven wheel behaviour as float rows (they previously silently dropped it). `SpinBox` returns `int` from `value()` when `decimals == 0`, so the contract for `_read_int` is unchanged.
  - **Refactor**: dispatch + helper methods consolidated in `mixins/wheel_step.py` `WheelStepMixin`. Both spin-box widgets are slim subclasses; the `msgBox` attribute is gone (use `show_feedback` from the new `FeedbackMixin`).
  - **Breaking**: public methods `increaseValueWithLargeStep` / `decreaseValueWithSmallStep` / `adjustStepSize` and the `msgBox` attribute removed from `SpinBox` and `DoubleSpinBox` — no consumers anywhere in the monorepo. External callers that drove the helpers explicitly should switch to synthesizing a `QWheelEvent` with the appropriate modifier mask and dispatching to `wheelEvent`; callers that touched `msgBox` directly should switch to `show_feedback(html)`.
  - Tests rewritten for the new ladder in `test_spinbox.py` + `test_double_spin_box.py` (Ctrl coarse, Ctrl+Shift very-coarse, Alt fine, Ctrl+Alt snap, axis-swap fallback covering both Alt-alone and Ctrl+Alt paths).

- **Current-item strip widened 1px → 2px + colour from theme `BUTTON_CHECKED`** — the 1px white strip read too subtle. Now 2px wide and sourced from the theme's `BUTTON_CHECKED` token (the orange "active selection" accent used by checked buttons elsewhere). Theme is resolved by walking up the combobox's parent chain to the nearest widget registered with `StyleSheet`, then `get_variable("BUTTON_CHECKED", theme=…)` is parsed via regex into a `QColor`. Hardcoded `rgb(165,135,110)` fallback if no theme can be inferred.

- **Row hover suppression scoped per-row in delegate, not blanket QSS** — the prior fix used a blanket `background-color: transparent` for `WidgetComboBox`'s view, which also killed the standard blue (`BUTTON_HOVER`) hover for **text-only** rows mixed into widget popups. Hover suppression now lives in `_CurrentItemIndicatorDelegate.paint`: it checks `view.indexWidget(index)` and strips `State_MouseOver`/`State_Selected` from the style option **only** when the row hosts an embedded widget. Text rows render with full hover styling; widget rows render with no row-level hover bg (avoiding the blue frame above/below shorter centred widgets).

- **`WidgetComboBox` row hover/selection bg suppressed** — after enforcing uniform-height rows + vertical-centering widgets, the parent QSS rule `QComboBox QAbstractItemView::item:hover { background-color: {BUTTON_HOVER}; }` showed as a **blue frame above and below** shorter embedded widgets (e.g. a 20px embedded combobox in a 24px uniform row). Embedded widgets already provide their own hover feedback and the current-item indicator strip still marks the active row, so the row-level shift was redundant. View's own stylesheet now sets `background-color: transparent` for `:hover`/`:selected`/`:selected:hover` at higher specificity than the parent rules. Text-only comboboxes are unaffected (different view, different stylesheet).

- **`WidgetComboBox` rows now uniform-height + zero item padding** — mixed-widget popups previously rendered ragged (slider ~22px / checkbox ~18px / spinbox ~20px) because each row's sizeHint came from the embedded widget's natural sizeHint. Added `_uniform_item_height` tracking that grows as taller widgets are added and re-syncs all existing rows so every selectable row reports the same height. The actions section (separator + multi-button container) is excluded via `track_height=False` so its legitimately taller container doesn't inflate normal rows. Embedded widgets are now added with `alignment=Qt.AlignVCenter` so shorter widgets stay at natural size centred in the uniform row instead of stretching. Item padding is overridden to `0` via the view's own stylesheet (parent `QComboBox QAbstractItemView::item { padding: 1px; }` was framing every embedded widget with a 1px gap unlike a standard combobox).

- **Current-item strip width 2px → 1px + colour from `palette.windowText()`** — after the popup item padding was tightened to `1px` uniform, the 2px strip overlapped the first 1px of every glyph in the current row (super().paint() drew text first, strip painted on top). Now `_STRIP_WIDTH = 1` so the strip fits inside the padding column and never touches text. Colour now sources from `palette.windowText()` (which Qt's QSS engine sets directly from the view's `color:` rule) with a fallback to `palette.text()` — both track the theme's text colour, so the strip is always visible against the surrounding background.

- **List/tree item-hover bg bumped from ~10% to ~20% alpha** — `QTreeWidget::item:hover:!selected` used `rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1)` (float-alpha form Qt QSS parses inconsistently — often clamps to 0) and `QAbstractItemView::item:hover` used 30/255 ≈ 12% alpha. With dark theme defaulting to `BORDER_W: 0px`, the border-hover provided no fallback feedback, and the bg-hover at ~10% was imperceptible. Both rules now use integer `rgba(255, 255, 255, 50)` ≈ 20% — visible on dark, still subtle on light. Combobox popup items override with `BUTTON_HOVER` so they're unaffected.

- **Custom `_CurrentItemIndicatorDelegate` replaces the menu-style checkmark** — `SH_ComboBox_Popup == 0` killed the menu-item delegate, which also killed the checkmark next to the current item. New `QStyledItemDelegate` paints a 2px white-tinted accent strip on the left edge of the current row. The strip is drawn *on top of* the standard item paint, so item geometry is unchanged across all states — no text shift.

- **ComboBox popup forced to list-view rendering via `SH_ComboBox_Popup` override** — the previous indicator-zeroing in QSS didn't fix the hover text-shift because the shift wasn't from `QAbstractItemView::indicator`. With Fusion's default `SH_ComboBox_Popup == 1`, Qt installs a menu-item delegate (`QComboMenuDelegate`) that reserves a checkmark column on every popup item; that column is what offsets text right on hover/selected. `CustomStyle.styleHint` now returns `0` for `SH_ComboBox_Popup`, which keeps the plain `QStyledItemDelegate` and renders items edge-to-edge. The QSS indicator-zero rule stays as belt-and-suspenders.

- **ComboBox popup indicator column zeroed** — the residual ~12px text-shift on hover came from `QAbstractItemView::indicator { width: 12px; height: 12px; }` (the checkmark column for tree/table views). Fusion reserves that column on hover/selected items in combobox popups too, shifting text right. New rule `QComboBox QAbstractItemView::indicator { width: 0px; height: 0px; border: none; }` removes it inside combobox popups only — tree/table indicator behavior is unchanged.

- **ComboBox popup items get explicit padding + no-border** — after the Fusion swap, popup item text shifted noticeably right on hover (Fusion's `PE_PanelItemViewItem` paints selection chrome with internal padding the base state lacks) and the generic `QAbstractItemView::item:selected` rule added a 1px border that further offset text. New explicit rules: `QComboBox QAbstractItemView::item { padding: 2px 6px; border: none; min-height: 16px; }` and the same padding/border on `:selected`/`:hover`/`:selected:hover`, so item geometry is constant across all states. `min-height: 16px` also tightens vertical rhythm vs Fusion's roomier default.

- **ComboBox base style swapped from app-default to Fusion** — Win11's native style paints a blue accent border on focus that survives `outline: none` in QSS and `State_HasFocus` stripping at `CC_ComboBox` (Win11 paints the focus indicator through multiple primitive paths, not only the complex control). Win11 also delivers `:hover` events unreliably to popup items. Both behaviours go away when the `CustomStyle` proxy wraps `QStyleFactory.create("Fusion")` instead of `self.style()`. Visible chrome (drop-down arrow, frame, padding) is already QSS-painted, so swapping the base is cosmetically transparent. The popup view also gets `setStyle(self.custom_style)` + `setMouseTracking(True)` in `showPopup` so the same Fusion base + event delivery applies to the dropdown.

- **Bg-hover removed from `QFrame:hover` and `QAbstractScrollArea:hover`** — these are way too broad an attachment point: `QTextEdit`/`QPlainTextEdit` extend `QAbstractScrollArea` → `QFrame`, and the combobox popup is a `QListView` (same chain). The earlier `QTextEdit:hover { border: ... }` rule had no `background-color` declaration so the cascading bg from the broader rules leaked through unopposed, producing the textedit + combobox-view bg-hover the user reported. Both rules now keep only the border-hover; bg-hover survives only on widgets that are themselves a hover target (closed `QComboBox`, `QAbstractSlider`, `QProgressBar`).

- **Native focus-border suppressed on `ComboBox`** — Windows' platform style paints a blue focus border on `CC_ComboBox` whenever `State_HasFocus` is set, and `outline: none` in QSS does **not** cover this (QSS `outline` only affects QSS-drawn dotted rects). After clicking and moving the cursor away, the combobox retained focus and the native blue border lingered. Fix: `CustomStyle.drawComplexControl` (already wrapping every uitk `ComboBox`) now copies the option and strips `State_HasFocus` for `CC_ComboBox` before delegating, so the underlying platform style paints it as un-focused.

- **Combobox `:on` drops out of hover style** — when the popup opens, the cursor is still over the combobox, so `:hover` kept firing and the combobox's hover-bg (`WIDGET_BACKGROUND_HOVER`) sat directly above the popup's `WIDGET_BACKGROUND` — close-toned and adjacent, the two read as one continuous panel. `QComboBox:on` now explicitly resets background and border to the non-hover values; the popup itself is the open-state feedback.

- **Hover-bg dropped on text-entry widgets** — `QAbstractSpinBox`, `QLineEdit`, `QTextEdit`, `QPlainTextEdit` no longer change background-color on hover. The cursor lives in these widgets and a bg shift while moving the mouse competes with the text content. Border-hover (`BORDER_HOVER`) is unchanged. The five non-text widgets (`QComboBox`, `QFrame`, `QAbstractScrollArea`, `QAbstractSlider`, `QProgressBar`) keep the bg-hover as before.

- **Token rename `HOVER_BORDER_COLOR` → `BORDER_HOVER`** — aligns with the rest of the theme dict's `<FEATURE>_<STATE>` suffix convention (`WIDGET_BACKGROUND_HOVER`, `TEXT_HOVER`, `BUTTON_HOVER`, `TEXT_CHECKED`). The old state-prefix form was the lone outlier. 10 QSS sites updated.

- **Hover-bg + focus-rect fixes** — two artifacts surfaced after the prior bg-tint addition:
  - **Hover bg is now opaque**: the previous `rgba(255,255,255,30)` made inputs 88% transparent on hover, which revealed whatever rendered underneath (placeholder layers, sibling widgets, parent paint state) and surfaced as e.g. the widget's objectName overlaying its actual text. Replaced with a new `WIDGET_BACKGROUND_HOVER` token — opaque slightly-lighter per theme (`rgb(140,140,140)` light, `rgb(78,78,78)` dark) — so the bg change still reads as feedback but the widget stays fully opaque.
  - **Qt focus rect suppressed on inputs**: added `outline: none` for `QLineEdit`, `QComboBox`, `QTextEdit`, `QPlainTextEdit`, `QAbstractSpinBox`, `QFrame`, `QAbstractScrollArea`, `QAbstractSlider`, `QProgressBar`, `QAbstractButton`. Without this, Qt drew its native blue focus rectangle on widgets that had been clicked into and out of (e.g., the hierarchy manager's diff-options combobox), and the rect lingered after the cursor left.

- **StyleEditor + theme — six follow-ups** —
  - **Controls row gap removed**: dropped the `addSpacing(8)` between the theme combo and the show-tier label — the layout-default spacing now handles it consistently.
  - **`{RADIUS}` reach extended**: added `border-radius: {RADIUS}` to `Header`, `Header:hover`, `Footer`, `Footer:hover`, `QLabel`, and `QLabel:hover` (previously square-cornered with literal `0px`). The radius now affects these widgets uniformly with the rest of the UI.
  - **Radius cap tightened from 10 → 8**: empirical degradation point moved down after fixing the slider-handle and adding more `{RADIUS}` consumers; 8 is safe for every current `{RADIUS}` site.
  - **Dark theme defaults to `BORDER_W: 0px`**: the dark theme reads softer without internal widget borders by default. Light theme stays at `1px`. Users can still dial it up via the editor.
  - **`ColorSwatch` gets a fixed black border**: previously `border: 8px solid transparent` (faded into the panel for light fills); now `border: 1px solid black`. `border-radius` and the checked-state overlay (`border-color: <fill>`) are unchanged from the original.

- **StyleEditor — layout + radius-cap polish** —
  - **Controls row spans the window**: the Theme/Show comboboxes now stretch (factor 1 each) so they fill the row width instead of clumping on the left.
  - **Length spinboxes capped at 10**: above 10 Qt's border-radius rendering degrades on small widgets. Cap applies to both `RADIUS` and `BORDER_W` for simplicity.
  - **Spinbox container loses horizontal padding**: cell QSS padding (`2px 5px`) already provides visual breathing room; the extra container `4px` was contributing to the cramped feel.
  - **Slider handle decoupled from `{RADIUS}`**: `QAbstractSlider::handle` is `width: 10px` by design, so scaling its corner with the global radius turned it into a pill at 6px and a degraded oval at 10px+. Now uses a literal `1px` like the scrollbar handle. Locked in by a new `test_slider_handle_radius_is_literal_not_token` test.
  - **Spinbox widened to 76px**: Qt's QSpinBox reserves internal layout space for the up/down arrow column even when QSS hides those buttons; 60px cropped the visible " px" text.

- **StyleEditor — live self-styling, length-token inputs, tier filter** —
  - **Live self-styling**: the editor now registers itself with the theme system on `__init__`, so color/size edits show up in its own chrome in real time. The theme combobox both filters the table and re-themes the editor — switching to "dark" makes the editor go dark and the rows reflect dark theme values. Registered with `recursive=False` because Qt stylesheets cascade to children naturally; recursing would wipe `ColorSwatch`'s inline self-styling.
  - **Length-token inputs**: tokens listed in `LENGTH_TOKENS` (currently `RADIUS`, `BORDER_W`) render with a `QSpinBox` + `" px"` suffix instead of a `ColorSwatch`. Length and color rows are separated by a bold `— Sizes —` divider row that spans all columns.
  - **Tier filter**: new "Show:" combo with `Basic` (12 most-edited tokens — main surfaces, text, accents, border color, radius) / `All` (every token, including the `ACTION_*` status palette and Python-consumed `ICON_COLOR` / `LINK_*`). Defaults to Basic.

- **StyleSheet — token cleanup + parsed-template engine** — finalized the dynamic-stylesheet token set and replaced the per-token `str.replace` loop with a parsed-template engine.
  - **Engine**: `style.qss` is now split once on first load into `[literal, TOKEN, literal, TOKEN, ...]` (cached as `_template_cache`), and `_apply_template` assembles each QSS string with one `''.join` of dict lookups instead of N full-string scans. `reload()` groups registered widgets by `(theme, resource, package, kwargs)` and assembles each group's QSS once — large registries no longer pay the template-apply cost per widget. Dropped the stale `setStyleSheet("")` clear in `_set_style` (Qt diffs internally). New `StyleSheet.clear_caches()` helper for dev hot-reload.
  - **Token additions**: `RADIUS` (default `1px`, replaces ~20 literal `border-radius: 1px` defaults), `BORDER_W` (default `1px`, replaces every `1px solid …`), `HOVER_BORDER_COLOR` (replaces the 10 literal `rgba(255,255,255,110)` :hover borders). Semantic-exception literals (footer `3px`, scrollbar `2-4px`, optionBox `0px`, 2px focus emphasis) intentionally stay inline.
  - **Renames**: `TEXT_BACKGROUND` → `SELECTION_BG`, `HIGHLIGHT_COLOR` → `SELECTION_FG` (text-selection bg/fg in inputs; the originals were misnamed), `WINDOW_FOREGROUND` → `TREE_ALTERNATE_BG` (tree alternate-row tint; the original was misleading since FG usually means text).
  - **Drops**: `TABLE_ITEM_HOVER`, `TABLE_ITEM_SELECTED`, `BUTTON_PRESSED` — zero meaningful QSS uses; `BUTTON_PRESSED`'s one site was a scrollbar arrow that takes the literal `rgb(120,120,120)` inline.
  - **Typo fix**: `{PANEL_BACKGROUND_BACKGROUND}` (doubled suffix on Footer) → `{PANEL_BACKGROUND}`.
  - **Breaking**: persisted user overrides bumped from `overrides_v2` → `overrides_v3` namespace; no migration — old `v2` data remains on disk but unread. Any external Python calls to `get_variable("TEXT_BACKGROUND" / "HIGHLIGHT_COLOR" / "WINDOW_FOREGROUND" / TABLE_ITEM_* / BUTTON_PRESSED)` will return `""` and need to be updated. `LINK_COLOR` / `LINK_VISITED_COLOR` kept (consumed by `textEditLogHandler.py`).
  - Net token count: 31 → 31 (drop 3, rename 3, add 3) — cleaner semantics, same surface size.
  - New tests: template engine cache behavior, alternation parsing, unknown-token fallback, QSS-tokens-resolve-against-themes sanity check, and a grouping-optimization assertion that 5 widgets sharing a config trigger 1 template-apply call (not 5).

- **OptionBox dead-code purge** — removed unused surface from `OptionBoxContainer` and `OptionBoxMixin`. Deleted: `OptionBoxContainer.setPassThrough` / `_pass_through` / `_update_mask` / `resizeEvent` (no callers anywhere in the monorepo); `OptionBoxMixin.has_pin_values` and `get_pin_values_service` (both methods had zero call sites and both depended on `_pin_values_controller`, which has zero writers — they unconditionally returned `False`/`None`). Also dropped the no-op parent-walk branch in `OptionBoxManager._find_existing_option_box` (returned `None` on hit). No behavior change.

- **Renamed ExternalToolHandler → ExternalAppHandler** — The handler that installs/launches uitk-compatible Python packages is now uniformly named after the things it launches (apps, matching the `extapps` package). Affected surface: module file `external_tool_handler.py` → `external_app_handler.py`, class `ExternalToolHandler` → `ExternalAppHandler`, handler key `external_tool` → `external_app`, entry-point discovery groups `uitk.external_tools[.in_process]` → `uitk.external_apps[.in_process]`, `CONFIG_BRANCH` (QSettings branch for persisted user_tags) `"external_tool"` → `"external_app"`, internal cache `_tools` → `_apps`. The `kind` strings reported in `HandlerEntry` (`external_in_process` / `external_subprocess`) and the browser's `_KIND_CHIP_LABELS` were left as-is — those describe the launch-mode taxonomy, not the handler. **Breaking change**: callers must update handler-key references (`sb.handlers.external_tool` → `sb.handlers.external_app`) and imports. Persisted user_tags under the old QSettings branch are dropped on first run.

- **ExternalAppHandler — `launch(show=False)` + install-failure wrapping** — `launch()` previously always called `widget.show() / raise_() / activateWindow()` after import, leaving no hook for hosts that want to inject context (e.g. `ui.slots.texture_provider`) and route the widget through a custom show path (such as `marking_menu.show()` for cursor-relative positioning). Added a `show: bool = True` kwarg: when False, the widget is install-checked, imported, cached, reparented under the host, and visibility-wired — but not shown. Refactored `_show_in_process` into `_prepare_in_process` (parent + visibility filter) + `_show_in_process` (prepare then show/raise/activate). Also wrapped `PackageManager(...).install(...)` so any underlying pip / OS failure surfaces as a single `RuntimeError` (was previously letting raw OSError/subprocess errors propagate), giving hosts a single exception type to catch. New tests in `test_external_app_handler.py`: `TestInProcessShowOptOut` (3 cases) and `TestInstallFailureSurfaces`.

- **SpinBox / DoubleSpinBox Ctrl+Alt wheel fix** — Ctrl+Alt+scroll on either widget now steps the value by the lowest decimal place (10⁻ᵈᵉᶜⁱᵐᵃˡˢ), as intended; previously it did nothing on PySide6.
  - **Root cause**: `wheelEvent` polled `QGuiApplication.keyboardModifiers()` and dispatched with strict `==`. In PySide6, `Qt.ControlModifier | Qt.AltModifier` evaluates to a `KeyboardModifier` value while the live modifier state is a `KeyboardModifiers` flag set — `==` between them is false even when bits match, so the Ctrl+Alt branch never fired. `SpinBox` also had unreachable dead code inside the Ctrl-only branch claiming to handle Ctrl+Alt. `DoubleSpinBox` additionally had Ctrl-alone and Ctrl+Alt bindings swapped relative to `SpinBox`.
  - **Fix**: read modifiers from `event.modifiers()` (event-time, also unit-testable) and detect with bitwise `&`. `decreaseValueWithSmallStep` now always uses `10 ** -decimals` instead of `max(step/10, 10**-decimals)`, so Ctrl+Alt truly targets the lowest decimal place regardless of `singleStep`. `DoubleSpinBox` bindings aligned to `SpinBox`.
  - 5 new wheelEvent dispatcher tests in `test_spinbox.py` plus a new `test_double_spin_box.py`.

- **CollapsableGroup ↔ MainWindow resize fix** — collapsing a `CollapsableGroup` inside a uitk `MainWindow` no longer leaves the window oversized.
  - **Root cause**: QMainWindow's auto-cached `minimumSize` follows `minimumSizeHint` UP when content grows but does NOT follow it back DOWN when content shrinks. After a collapse, `minimumSizeHint` correctly dropped to e.g. 156 but the explicit `minimumSize` cache stayed at the pre-collapse 279 — so the subsequent `resize()` got clamped above the requested shrink. Observed in tentacle: window shrunk by ~10px when the group lost ~120px of content.
  - **Fix**: `MainWindow._sync_min_height_to_hint()` aligns `minimumHeight` with the freshly-computed hint before each `resize()` in `adjust_height_by` and `fit_height_to_content`. `CollapsableGroup._fallback_window_resize` does the same for non-MainWindow hosts. Tracks in both directions: once we take over the explicit min, Qt stops auto-raising it on grow, so subsequent expands need us to raise it back too.
  - Added 5 end-to-end regression tests in `test_main_window_resize.py` exercising a tentacle-style layout (nested QVBoxLayouts, multiple `CollapsableGroup`s, trailing `Expanding` spacer, footer).

- **ToggleOption** — new OptionBox plugin (`uitk/widgets/optionBox/options/toggle.py`) for persisted binary on/off buttons. Icon dims to the project's "error" red (`pythontk.Palette.status()["error"]`) when off, so the user can see which control caused a dependent filter / widget to stop.
  - Emits `toggled(bool)` on user clicks and on `set_on(v)` (suppress with `emit=False`).
  - Optional `gated_widgets=[…]` disables listed widgets in sync with the toggle. Does not auto-restore on destruction — caller owns widget lifecycle.
  - `OptionBoxManager.set_toggle()` / `add_toggle()` for fluent setup, including `on_toggled=` to wire the signal in one line.
  - Persistence: pass `settings_key=str` for explicit namespacing, omit to auto-derive from the wrapped widget's `objectName`, or `False` to opt out (consumer owns storage).
  - Default `_option_order` now includes a `"toggle"` slot between `"pin"` and `"action"`.
- **Persistence mixin** — extracted shared `settings_key` resolution + lazy `SettingsManager` construction into `optionBox/options/_persistence.py` (`PersistedOption`). Currently consumed by `ToggleOption`; `ActionOption`, `PinValuesOption`, and `RecentValuesOption` keep their existing ad-hoc copies and will be migrated in a follow-up.
- **switchboard_browser filter button migration** — `_build_filter_lineedit` now uses `ToggleOption` instead of a hand-rolled two-state `ActionOption`. The fragile `find_option(ActionOption)` lookup at the end of the factory ("the first action that isn't the scope action") is gone — the toggle reference is held directly from construction. Preset restore now syncs the toggle's visual state via `set_on(..., emit=False)` so the icon reflects the restored `filter_enabled` flag.

- **Menu popup fixes** — fixed option menus not opening and flashing during init.
  - **Root cause**: `_register_with_main_window()` called synchronously inside `Menu.add()` triggered `mainWindow.register_widget()` → `widget.init_slot()` → `tb###_init()` recursively during menu population. Fixed by deferring via `QTimer.singleShot(0)`.
  - `showEvent`: skip `_apply_position()` when `show_as_popup()` already handled positioning (check `_current_anchor_widget`).
  - `_setup_as_popup`: consolidated double `setWindowFlags()` + `setParent()` into single `setParent(parent, flags)` — avoids double native window recreation.
  - `Header.show_menu`: changed `menu.setVisible(True)` → `menu.show_as_popup(anchor_widget=self, position="bottom")`.
  - `MenuOption` / `OptionMenuOption.set_wrapped_widget`: preserve popup flags via `setParent(widget, self._menu.windowFlags())`.
  - Added 13 regression tests in `test_menu.py` covering init visibility, deferred registration, header menu popup, option box menu flags.

- **Marking menu reshow fix** — fixed marking menu reopening on top of standalone windows while activation key is still held.
  - `_show_window`: always hides the MarkingMenu and clears `_activation_key_held`; reparents child widgets so they aren't hidden alongside the overlay.
  - `_transition_to_state`: guards against transitioning when MarkingMenu is already hidden, preventing `Key_F12` → startmenu reshow.
  - `_standalone_suppress` flag: set in `_show_window`, cleared in `_on_activation_release`. Blocks `_on_activation_press` from processing spurious key re-fires caused by focus changes in Maya.
  - Added 9 regression tests in `test_marking_menu.py`.
